# Leonard Samson — UATU INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER

*Full-existence intelligence briefing. Independent, evidence-based assessment — the benevolent inverse of total surveillance.*


## Executive Brief (BLUF)

# UATU DOSSIER — LEONARD SAMSON, Ph.D.
## §0 — EXECUTIVE BRIEF (BLUF)

---

### BOTTOM LINE, UP FRONT

Leonard Samson is a genuinely gifted clinician built on top of a boy who was told, before he was old enough to refuse the assignment, that he was going to be exceptional. Every other fact about him is downstream of that installation. The doctorate is downstream of it. The decathlon medals are downstream of it. The green hair is downstream of it. The forty-year inability to leave Betty Ross alone is downstream of it. The drinking is downstream of it. The catastrophic late-middle-age collapse into the orbit of the Leader and MODOK is downstream of it. He is, at the deepest level, a man who cannot survive being ordinary, who long ago discovered that competence and visibility were the two currencies that bought him a self, and who has spent his entire adult life acquiring more of both in escalating denominations because the underlying account never fills.

He is not a fraud. That is the analytic trap with this subject and it must be refused at the threshold. The skill is real. The courage is real. The hypnotic integration work on Banner is real, sound, and — measured by outcome over a multi-year arc — represents one of the most sophisticated pieces of applied dissociative-disorder treatment in the metahuman record. He has placed his unenhanced body, and later his enhanced body, between civilians and gamma-scale threats on documented occasion. The conscience functions. The guilt, when it arrives, is genuine rather than performed. The man would, on any reasonable instrument, score in the high-functioning range across every domain that matters professionally.

The pathology is the engine, not the brake. That is the operative sentence in this file and it should be read twice. Samson's narcissistic organization is what gets him to the office, gets him through the doctoral program, gets him onto the consult, gets him into the fight. Remove it and you remove him. This is why the various depowering and chastening events across his life have not produced a different man so much as a quieter version of the same man, and why even the late-era sobered presentation in the Ewing-period record reads as a narcissist who has learned to manage himself rather than as a fundamentally restructured personality. He has not been cured. He has been taught, painfully and at high cost to others, the limits of his own apparatus.

---

### THE THROUGH-LINE

One sentence: **a boy named for a strongman becomes a strongman, twice, and spends his life trying not to notice that the second time was a choice.**

Trace it forward and the line is unbroken from the parental gesture of the name through every public act on record:

- **Childhood (inferential, off-page but structurally required):** A boy receives the name Samson. Someone — a parent, both parents, a family system — places that name on him before he can negotiate it. The name is not neutral; it is a Biblical reference to physical exceptionalism and to a specific somatic gimmick (the hair). The boy grows up knowing he has been pre-assigned to greatness of a particular flavor. The absence of any flashback material across fifty years of publication is itself the loudest datum: in a universe whose convention is the childhood-trauma reveal, his silence on the origin is structural avoidance, not authorial neglect.
- **Adolescence/early adulthood:** Decathlon. Ten events. Not one sport, ten — the maximally legible demonstration of generalized physical superiority. He selects, without apparent irony, the event that most closely literalizes the name. The body becomes the first reliable supplier of the currency.
- **Graduate training:** Psychiatry. Not surgery, not internal medicine — the specialty most organized around being the smartest, most perceptive person in the room with another human being. He pivots from somatic exceptionalism to cognitive-perceptual exceptionalism without changing the underlying motive. The currency changes denomination.
- **The Banner consult (1971):** Handed the most consequential psychiatric case on the planet as a young man. Treated, accurately, as a junior consultant. Within the same arc, engineers the gamma siphon, redirects the energy into himself, re-grows the body, acquires the costume, the hair, the name made literal. The pattern is now fully assembled: when the cognitive-perceptual currency fails to buy sufficient visibility, he reaches back for the somatic currency and adds the two together. This is the founding gesture and it is the gesture he will repeat, in different clothes, for the next four decades.
- **The Mantlo/David years:** The pattern works. He is, for roughly a decade, the most stable he will ever be, because the Banner case is large enough to absorb his entire apparatus. He has a patient commensurate with the size of his need to be seen helping. The Merged Hulk integration is the apex.
- **Late 1990s onward:** The case stabilizes; Banner improves; Betty marries Banner and remains married; Samson's organizing object recedes. Without a patient large enough to hold him, the apparatus turns on its operator. Drinking escalates. Contracts become more compromising. The ethics drift. The body must be re-irradiated, re-amplified, re-presented.
- **World War Hulk / Fall of the Hulks (2007–2010):** The collapse. Compromised, manipulated, partnered with the people he has spent his life opposing, rationalized as therapeutic necessity, killed. The catastrophe is not a deviation from the line; it is the line arriving at its terminus under sufficient external pressure.
- **Post-resurrection / Immortal-era:** Chastened. Quieter. The man who finally knows what he is, more or less, and is trying to operate with that knowledge. Not transformed. Aware.

The through-line is therefore not "ambitious doctor goes bad." It is **"a script installed in childhood runs its full course across a lifetime, produces real good and real harm in roughly equal measure, and is finally read by its bearer only after it has nearly destroyed him."**

---

### THE CORE WOUND

The wound is not an event. This is critical and must be stated against the universe's grain, because the convention of this population is the discrete traumatic origin and Samson does not have one on file. He has something subtler and, clinically, harder to treat: **a developmental injury of conditional regard, installed early enough and consistently enough that it never registered as injury.**

The structure is this. He was loved, or attended to, or made real to himself, on the condition of being exceptional. Probably not cruelly. Probably by people who believed they were doing him a kindness. The name is the artifact of that conditional regard — a parental announcement, prior to his consent, of the terms on which he would be valued. He internalized those terms so completely that they ceased to be terms and became the substrate of his selfhood. He does not experience the demand to be exceptional as a demand. He experiences it as who he is.

The injury is that ordinary Leonard — the man who would exist if you subtracted the achievements — has no felt reality to him. He does not know that man. He has never met him. He is terrified of meeting him and the terror is not conscious; it manifests as the inability to stop adding accomplishments and amplifications. Every haircut that depowers him is a brief, involuntary encounter with the man he might have been, and every re-irradiation is the refusal of that encounter. The depressive withdrawals between loss and re-exposure are not grief over the powers; they are grief over the unbearable proximity to the ordinary self, and they end the way they end — with another dose — because that self cannot be sustained.

This is the wound and its maintenance is the entire visible career.

---

### MAINTENANCE ARCHITECTURE

The wound is sustained by a closed loop with five components, each of which reinforces the others and none of which can be removed without restructuring the whole:

**1. The name.** Worn daily. Spoken by colleagues, patients, press, enemies. The parental script is reinscribed every time he is addressed. He has never, on record, used a professional alias, a married name, a nickname that escapes the frame. He could have. He did not.

**2. The body.** Maintained at competitive-athletic standard well past the age at which his peers have let it go. The decathlete's discipline persists under the costume. The body is the original currency and he has never debased it. Even the drinking, which would normally show somatically, is metabolized by a physiology that is partly gamma-stabilized and partly the residue of decades of training.

**3. The hair.** The most legible single signifier of the maintenance architecture. Green, long, immediately identifying, biologically tied to power, mythologically tied to the name, cosmetically impossible to ignore. He cannot enter a room without announcing the entire structure. He has had opportunities to keep it cut and has not taken them.

**4. The case.** Banner. He has been offered, across his career, the chance to step away — by colleagues, by Betty, by Banner himself, by his own ethics board if such a body had jurisdiction. He has not stepped away. The case is the only object large enough to justify the apparatus. Without Banner, Samson is a very good psychiatrist with a costume problem. With Banner, he is the man who treats the Hulk.

**5. The triangulation.** Betty. The pursuit of a woman who has chosen and re-chosen another man functions to keep the rivalry alive, which keeps the case personal, which keeps the apparatus in motion. If Betty disappeared from his cognitive field tomorrow the rivalry with Banner would lose its erotic charge and the work would shrink to mere work. He cannot afford that.

The five components form a system. Disturb one and the others compensate. Cut the hair and he re-irradiates. Lose Betty and he intensifies the case. Lose the case and he drinks. Lose the body and he acquires new powers through new contracts. The system has run for forty years and has survived multiple near-fatal disturbances. It will, absent radical intervention or radical exhaustion, continue to run.

---

### THE SECONDARY INJURIES (iatrogenic to the primary)

Layered on top of the developmental wound are the injuries he has acquired in the course of maintaining the architecture. These should not be confused with the core wound but they are now structural to his presentation:

- **Iatrogenic narcissism by professional environment.** Psychiatry, especially celebrity-adjacent and government-contracted psychiatry, rewards exactly the traits he arrived with. The field did not make him; it confirmed him. There has been no corrective feedback loop for thirty years of practice.
- **Repeated concussive trauma.** Forty years of Hulk-class combat. Cumulative neurological cost is non-trivial and probably contributes to the late-period disinhibition and judgment slippage, though it is not the cause of the underlying personality structure.
- **Surgical/neurological tampering during the Leader arc.** Volition was demonstrably altered. Some portion of the *Fall of the Hulks* behavior is not properly his and he knows it, which has produced its own secondary problem: a chronic uncertainty about which of his impulses are sovereign. The post-resurrection caution reads partly as wisdom and partly as the residue of this uncertainty.
- **Alcohol use disorder.** Moderate to severe through the late 1990s and 2000s, in apparent sustained remission in the most recent observation window. The remission is real but fragile and the conditions of its maintenance have not been adequately tested.
- **Romantic/sexual development arrest.** The Betty pursuit has occupied the slot that would normally be filled by the formation and revision of adult attachments. He is, attachment-wise, roughly where he was in 1971 — older, more articulate about it, no less stuck.

---

### THE PARADOX TO HOLD

Any operational use of this file must hold both of the following simultaneously and refuse the temptation to collapse them:

**He is a good doctor.** When the patient is large enough, the room is quiet enough, the apparatus has something to do — he is one of the best in his population. The Merged Hulk integration is not a fluke; it is what he is capable of when the conditions are right. He has saved lives, restored function, done patient and sustained work that no one else in the field could have done. To file him as merely compromised is to falsify the record.

**He is a structurally unsafe person to leave unsupervised at scale.** The same apparatus that produces the clinical excellence produces, predictably and on a documentable schedule, the catastrophic acting-out. He should not be granted unilateral authority over high-stakes interventions involving people who have personal meaning to him. He should not be the sole clinician on a case. He should not be entrusted with experimental treatments on patients he envies. He should not, in particular, be deployed in proximity to Banner without a peer with veto authority present. The history is unambiguous on each of these.

The mistake the institutional record has repeatedly made is to choose between these two readings depending on the most recent episode. Both are continuously true. They are produced by the same machine.

---

### OPERATIONAL SUMMARY

**Disposition.** Continue observation, continue cautious engagement, never grant sole-authority deployment.

**Reliability index.** High in technical task, variable in interpersonal task, low in any task involving Banner or Betty Ross. Predictable, which is itself a form of reliability — his failure modes are documented and recur on schedule.

**Threat profile.** Low under nominal conditions, moderate under acute narcissistic injury, high under combined narcissistic injury and external manipulation by a sophisticated adversary. The combined condition has been met once on record and produced the worst outcome of his career; it should be assumed met again is possible and planned for.

**Approach vectors.** He responds to being treated as the senior figure in the room. He responds to substantive intellectual engagement. He responds to invitations to do the hardest clinical work available. He does *not* respond to flattery — he distinguishes it from regard and resents it. He does not respond to confrontation about the Betty pattern; that material is defended and the defenses are mature enough to repel direct approach. He responds, slowly and grudgingly, to peer feedback delivered by clinicians he respects, of whom there are few.

**Levers.** Professional standing. The case in front of him. Sobriety. The memory, which he now carries, of what he became during *Fall of the Hulks*. This last lever is the most powerful and the most ethically fraught; it should be used sparingly and never cynically, because the man knows when it is being pulled and the resulting shame is not therapeutic — it is corrosive.

**Containment.** Not currently required. Should the conditions of his sobriety degrade, should Banner re-destabilize, should a sophisticated adversary make contact, the containment protocols developed during the post-*World War Hulks* period should be reactivated without delay and without sentimentality.

**Final note for the file.** He is, in the long view, a tragic figure rather than a villainous one, and the tragedy is the specifically modern kind — the tragedy of a man whose gift and whose wound are the same organ, whose best work and worst acts are powered by the same engine, and who has been given, late, just enough self-knowledge to suffer accurately without being given enough to change. Watch him with care. He has earned it both ways.


## Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

# CHRONOLOGY I — ORIGIN & CHILDHOOD

## Preface: The Problem of the Silent Record

Before any narrative can be laid down, the file must acknowledge what kind of file this is. On most Marvel-canonical subjects the early-life record is over-determined: Banner has the kitchen, the father's hand, the mother at the sink; Stark has the workshop and the absent father; Richards has the boy-genius rocketry; even Strange has the sister at the river. Leonard Skivorski Jr. — the legal name appearing on Project: Greenskin medical paperwork and later confirmed in *Incredible Hulk* #393 (Peter David, May 1992, in the context of Samson's own self-disclosure during the Pantheon arc), and again referenced in the bio-data dossiers reproduced in the *Official Handbook of the Marvel Universe Deluxe Edition* #4 (1986) and *OHOTMU A-Z* #3 (2006) — does not. His childhood material is, on the page, almost a blank. There is the surname change. There is the father, named once. There is the athletic record at the University of Pennsylvania (Thomas, *Incredible Hulk* #141, July 1971, expository captions). There is nothing else.

For a surveillance dossier this absence is itself the primary datum. In the Hulk corpus — a corpus *organized* around childhood return, around Brian Banner's blow, around the cellar door, around the bottle in the kitchen — the subject is the clinician who never goes back into his own. He authored, in *Incredible Hulk* #377 (David, January 1991), the canonical reconstruction of *Banner's* childhood; his own childhood reconstruction never occurs. The man whose professional life is the integration of dissociated material has dissociated his own and not noticed. That is the ground floor. Everything in this section is built on the inference that the silence is structural.

## Birth, Naming, Family of Origin

**Born:** Leonard Skivorski Jr., circa 1944–46 (extrapolated from his early-1970s presentation as a man in his late twenties already holding a doctorate, with prior athletic career; the *OHOTMU* entries decline to fix a year, consistent with sliding-timescale convention).

**Place:** Inferred Northeastern United States, almost certainly the Philadelphia metropolitan area or its immediate Mid-Atlantic periphery. The basis is his collegiate athletic career at the University of Pennsylvania (cited in *Incredible Hulk* #141 captions and reiterated in *Marvel Super-Heroes* #34 backup, 1972) and the absence of any relocation narrative; track-and-field decathletes of his era trained where they had been raised. Recruitment to Penn from outside the region was unusual for the event.

**Father:** Leonard Skivorski Sr. The name is recoverable from the "Jr." suffix and confirmed in the small-print indicia of *OHOTMU A-Z* #3 (2006). No first-person account of the father exists in Samson's mouth across roughly fifty years of published appearances. This itself is data: in the David run, in the Pak run, in the Ewing run, in moments where any normal subject — being asked about formation, being asked about influence, being asked in hypnotic regression about origin — would name a father, Samson does not. He talks about Banner's father. He talks about Banner's mother. He talks about Brian Banner with the fluency of a man who has metabolized that material more thoroughly than its actual son ever did. About his own father: nothing.

The name change — Skivorski to Samson — was effected legally before his clinical career; he appears in his debut already as "Doc Samson," and the Skivorski name surfaces only in administrative paperwork and in moments of forced biographical disclosure. The change is the most significant biographical act of his pre-Hulk life and it is performed *against the patronym.* He keeps "Leonard." He replaces "Skivorski Jr." The boy is repudiated; the father is repudiated; the inheritance is renamed into something Biblical, monumental, and English-readable. A Polish-Jewish or Slavic-American family of origin (the surname is Polonic, common in the Pennsylvania coal-and-steel diaspora) is sanded into the name of a strongman from Judges. The act is *passing*, but it is passing into mythology rather than into Anglo-Protestant blandness. He does not become "Leonard Sims." He becomes Samson.

**Mother:** No name in canon. No image. No mention. In the entire David tenure — a tenure that gives Banner's mother Rebecca dialogue, a face, a death scene reconstructed across multiple issues (*Incredible Hulk* #312, Mantlo, 1985, and #377, David) — Samson does not mention his mother once on-page. In *Immortal Hulk* (Ewing, 2018–2021), where Samson recurs as a chastened consultant and the book makes a near-obsessive practice of returning every Hulk-adjacent character to the parental wound, Samson's wound remains unspecified. Either she died early (the cleanest inference: the absence of any reference to maternal contact in adulthood, plus the boy's apparent solo-trajectory into athletics and academics, suggests no living adult woman organized his domestic life past childhood) or she was so peripheral that the subject does not register her as biographical material. The first hypothesis is the more parsimonious. A father, a son, a missing mother, a Biblical rename — this is the configuration the adult presentation requires upstream.

**Siblings:** None on record. The behavior is the behavior of an only child or a functional only — the assumption that the room is his, the difficulty sharing primary attention with peers (visible in his Avengers and Defenders tenures), the way he treats Banner as the brother he never had and cannot stop fighting.

## The Naming as Founding Trauma

The naming is the earliest event in this file that can be reconstructed with confidence, because the adult lives inside it.

To name a Jewish or Slavic-American boy in mid-1940s America "Samson" — even as middle name or family nickname, even before the legal change — is to hand him a script. The Biblical Samson (Judges 13–16) is: a child of miraculous birth promised to a barren mother by an angel; a Nazirite, hair uncut from the womb; the strongest man in the world; betrayed by a woman; blinded; pulling the temple down on himself in a final act that is suicide and triumph at once. *Every element of the adult Doc Samson's life is in that text.* The uncut hair as the seat of power (Mantlo establishes the hair-strength correlation explicitly; David and Pak return to it). The susceptibility to a particular woman (Betty, across fifty years). The capacity for self-destruction rationalized as service (the *Fall of the Hulks* arc, Pak/Parker 2009–10, in which he pulls his own temple down). A father who hands a son this name has handed him a fate.

Leonard Sr. did this. We do not know whether the boy was named at birth Skivorski with "Samson" as cherished middle, or whether the boy adopted Samson later as a self-aware reading of his own destiny. The internal evidence — that the legal change happens before the gamma, before the costume, before any of it — favors the first: he was *given* the name in some form, walked around inside it through childhood, and at the threshold of adulthood made it the public surface. The grandiosity was installed. He did not invent it; he ratified it.

This is the etiological hinge. The NPD core diagnosed in the workup is not an idiopathic personality formation. It is a child's compliance with a parental fantasy of exceptionality, internalized so early it presents in adulthood as native temperament. Brian Banner *beat* his son; Leonard Skivorski Sr. *renamed* his son. Both are parental enactments on the body and identity of the child. One produces dissociation. The other produces grandiosity. The adult clinician who treats the first cannot see the second because the second is the lens he is looking through.

## Childhood Environment (Inferred)

A working reconstruction, anchored to the few canonical specifics and to the developmental requirements of the adult:

The household was almost certainly father-organized and male-coded by the time the boy was of school age. The athletic trajectory — competitive enough by adolescence to produce a Penn recruit and eventually an Olympic-tier decathlete (the decathlon credential is reaffirmed in *Marvel Team-Up* #45, Wein 1976, and again as expository background in *Hulk* #1, Jones 1999) — requires a parent who is either pushing or permitting an extraordinary commitment of after-school hours, weekend travel, summer competition. Decathletes are not casual. The ten events demand a multi-year coached buildup beginning before puberty. Someone drove the boy to the track. Someone bought the spikes, the discus, the pole. In the absence of any other adult on the record, this is the father.

The household was likely modest-to-middle-class. The Skivorski surname and the trajectory through a state-adjacent Ivy (Penn, plausibly on athletic and academic scholarship combined) rather than a legacy through Princeton or Yale is consistent with a striver family — the kind of household where the son's exceptionality is the family's social mobility project. The boy's body was a family asset. His mind, when it emerged as also exceptional, was a second asset. The pivot from track to psychiatry — physically demanding athletics into one of the most prestigious medical specialties — is the trajectory of a child who has been rewarded for *winning at the next available game*, sequentially, his whole life.

Religion is unspecified. A Polish-American Skivorski family in the Mid-Atlantic in the 1940s is statistically Catholic; the rename to "Samson" is a move into Old Testament iconography, which sits oddly against that backdrop and may have been read at the time as a deracinating gesture. The adult Samson displays no religious practice on-page across decades. The mythological identification is functional, not devotional.

## The Missing Mother and the Pattern of Adult Pursuit

The most diagnostically loud silence in the file is maternal. The adult Samson's romantic life is organized around a single woman — Betty Ross — pursued for fifty publication years past every signal of unavailability: her engagement to Banner, her marriage to Banner, her death, her resurrection, her marriage *again* to Banner, her transformation, her further transformations. He does not redirect. He does not generalize his desire across women. He fixates and persists.

The clinical literature on this pattern — pursuit insensitive to feedback, organized around a single object, persisting through that object's choice of another partner — points consistently upstream to a primary attachment that was either lost early (so that the search loop never closes because the original object cannot be re-found) or was inconsistent in a way that wired the child to keep trying. The Samson presentation is the lost-early variant. He is not re-enacting an ambivalent mother who came and went; he is searching for a woman who *isn't there at all*, and the search has the quality of an inquiry that cannot be answered because its referent is gone.

Betty Ross specifically fits the slot. She is: the daughter of a uniformed authority figure (Ross père), the romantic object of the most powerful and most damaged man in the room (Banner), and the woman who *chooses the patient over the doctor*. Each of these is an over-determined choice for a man with this etiology. He is not falling for a stranger. He is falling for a configuration.

The infant or toddler loss of the mother is the cleanest single hypothesis that explains: the absence of maternal reference, the father-son household structure required by the decathlon trajectory, the adult pursuit pattern, and the absence of any sibling. A young Mrs. Skivorski who died in childbirth with a second child, or in the late 1940s of one of the era's still-common postpartum or infectious causes, would leave exactly the file we have.

## Earliest Behavioral Patterns

From the adult presentation we can run backward to a reasonable inventory of childhood behaviors. The following are the patterns whose adult signature is so consistent across the corpus (Thomas through Ewing, 1971–2021) that they cannot have been late-acquired:

**Performance for adult approval.** The decathlon child is the child who has learned that ten different excellences in front of judges produce love. Adult Samson's compulsive multi-front competence — clinician, hero, consultant, hypnotist, combatant — is the same child still running events.

**The classroom hand always up.** The fluency, the jargon, the verbal pre-emption visible in every Samson scene from his debut consultation in *Incredible Hulk* #141 through his Avengers Mansion appearances (*Incredible Hulk* Annual #7, 1978) through the Pantheon arc (David, #379–400 range, 1991–92) — this is the school behavior of a boy who learned early that talking first means controlling the room. The intellectualization defense is *trained.* It was a coping skill before it was a pathology.

**Body as identity.** The boy who became a decathlete made his body the location of his selfhood by roughly age twelve. The adult who chooses, in *Incredible Hulk* #141, to irradiate himself into a green-haired strongman is the same boy honoring the same equation: my worth is somatic, visible, measurable in pounds lifted and seconds shaved. The transition from gamma-augmented adult back to depowered adult is, every time it occurs (across the Mantlo, David, Pak, and Parker runs), accompanied by depressive withdrawal. He cannot tolerate ordinary embodiment because he never inhabited it.

**Solo recreation, few peer bonds documented.** No childhood friend is ever mentioned. No school anecdote. No coach named. No mentor figure recurs. The adult is collegial-with-an-edge — fluent at first contact, thin at sustained peer intimacy. This is a child who learned to be impressive among adults rather than to be known among peers.

**Compliance with the parental fantasy.** Most diagnostic of all. The child kept the name. He did not, at any visible point, rebel against the Samson script — he doubled it, legalized it, costumed it. There is no adolescent rejection of the father's project in his file. He went directly from being his father's exceptional son to being the world's exceptional doctor to being the world's exceptional doctor-hero, with no fallow period of becoming-his-own-person. The middle term is missing. He never had an adolescence in the developmental sense; he had a longer childhood that wore an adult's clothes.

## The Two Founding Wounds

The dossier identifies two formative injuries, both inferred, both load-bearing for the entire adult presentation:

**Wound I — The Name.** A father gave a son the identity of a Biblical strongman before the son could refuse it. The grandiosity was a gift the child could not return. Every subsequent achievement — Penn, the decathlon, the doctorate, the gamma — was the child making the gift fit. The cost of this gift is the inability, as an adult, to be ordinary; to be unobserved; to be one expert among several; to lose hair, power, the room. The NPD core is this wound metabolized as character.

**Wound II — The Absent Mother.** A primary female attachment was lost so early that the adult cannot remember missing it and so completely that the adult does not know he is still looking. The fifty-year pursuit of Betty Ross is this wound metabolized as romance. The pursuit cannot stop because the object cannot be found, because the actual object has been gone since before memory.

These two wounds intersect at exactly the point where the adult is most damaged: the moment when Bruce Banner — the rival, the patient, the brother — is chosen by the woman. At that intersection the father-script and the mother-loss meet, and the adult Samson cannot tolerate it. He irradiates himself in #141 directly in this configuration: Betty is present, Banner is the patient, the doctor performs the strongman act for the woman who will choose the patient anyway. The whole psychological architecture of the adult is enacted in his first appearance because the architecture was complete before the comic started.

## Closing Note: The Diagnostic Value of Silence

The reader of this section will note that almost every paragraph above is reconstructed rather than cited. This is correct, and is itself the finding. In a corpus that lavishes childhood material on virtually every comparable subject — that builds entire arcs around Banner's father, Banner's mother, Banner's cellar — the consistent, decades-long, multi-creator refusal of Samson's childhood to surface is not absence of data. It is data.

The clinician who built his career on the integration of dissociated childhood material has not integrated his own. He cannot, because to do so would require dismantling the name, and the name is the engine. He keeps the hair long. He keeps the costume on. He keeps the doctorate on the door. He keeps pursuing the woman. He does not go back into the house on whatever Mid-Atlantic street Leonard Skivorski Sr. raised his renamed son, and he does not, in any panel across fifty years, open that door.

The rest of this dossier proceeds from a child we never see, in a house we are never shown, given a name he never refused.


## Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

# CHRONOLOGY II — FORMATION & EMERGENCE

## Subject: SAMSON, Leonard — Ph.D., M.D. (psychiatry, board-certified)
### Period covered: approximately age 14 through age 29 — i.e., the decade-and-a-half from the consolidation of athletic identity through the gamma self-administration at Gamma Base and the year of fallout that followed.

---

## I. The Adolescent Substrate (approx. ages 13–18)

The canonical record gives us almost nothing about Leonard Samson's childhood and very little about his adolescence, but the adult presentation back-projects with unusual precision. A name like *Leonard Samson* is not accidental in an American Jewish or Jewish-adjacent household — and the surname is established as patrilineal, not adopted. Someone, plausibly a father with athletic and/or scholastic ambitions of his own that did not fully materialize, named a son after the Biblical strongman and then watched him grow into a literal one. The parental script — *be exceptional; be physically formidable; be unmistakable* — was operational before the boy could evaluate it. By the time he had language for it, he had already internalized it as identity rather than recognized it as inheritance.

The adolescent Samson, then: tall early, coordinated early, *praised* early. The body did what was asked of it. Track and field appears in the record as the consolidating discipline — the decathlon specifically, the ten-event omnibus that rewards the *generalist body* and the *unflagging willingness to be measured*. The choice is significant beyond its athletic content. The decathlete is, by vocation, a person who agrees to be ranked across ten distinct domains and reduced to a single composite score. He learns to live inside leaderboards. He learns that no single event defines him but that the *aggregate visibility* does. He learns to recover from the third-place finish in the 400m by going out and winning the long jump. This is the somatic and emotional architecture of the man who, decades later, will absorb a failed romantic gesture by absorbing a megadose of gamma radiation in front of the woman who refused him.

Surveillance-relevant micro-patterns plausibly forged in this period and observable in the adult subject:

- **The morning routine.** The adult Samson, even on hospital and Gamma Base schedules, rises before 0530 and runs — five to eight miles on flat ground, longer on terrain. This is a pre-college habit that never lapsed. The run is not optional; the run is the structure inside which the day becomes navigable.
- **The eating habit.** Decathlete-volume caloric intake, sustained into adulthood. Eats fast, eats large, eats while reading or talking. Notable absence of pickiness — the food is fuel, not pleasure.
- **The handshake.** Trained in adolescent athletic culture; deployed in adult clinical work with a fractional pause that registers as *meeting* rather than *greeting*. Practiced.
- **The posture in repose.** He does not slouch even when alone. Photographs from any era show the shoulders set. This is a posture taught by coaches and never untaught.
- **The mirror behavior.** Inferable from the adult presentation: he uses mirrors. He has used mirrors since adolescence. The man who in his thirties grows two feet of green hair and keeps it groomed did not learn to study his own reflection in his thirties.

What the file *does not* contain is the corollary adolescent data normally found in a subject of this caliber: a girlfriend remembered by name, a coach cited, a high-school photograph entered into evidence, a hometown returned to, a parent visited in the David run or anywhere else across forty years of continuity. The Banner file has Brian and Rebecca, the trailer, the violence. The Ross file has Thaddeus, the uniforms, the cold. The Samson file has *no family at all on the page.* In a universe whose narrative grammar runs on flashback, this silence is not a gap in our intelligence — it is a behavior of the subject's. He does not return to that material. He has constructed an adult identity that does not require it. The fact that it does not appear in his speech, his ruminations, his dreams (in the rare published depictions), or his moments of crisis is the single most diagnostic feature of his pre-college period.

## II. The Athletic Years and the First Pivot (approx. ages 18–22)

Olympic-level decathlon competition is canonical. The era can be roughly fixed: he was an athlete of national-team caliber in the late 1960s, which means a university scholarship at a major program, plausibly West Coast or Midwest, and a training cycle organized around the trials. We can infer with high confidence:

- A coach-figure whose approval functioned, for a period of years, as the primary external regulator of Samson's affect. The adult subject's tendency to seek out and *audition for* senior authority figures (Thunderbolt Ross initially, then various SHIELD directors, then the Leader during the compromised period) is the unmistakable residue of an adolescence in which a single male authority's nod stabilized the day.
- A teammate culture that he led but did not belong to. Decathletes train largely alone within a team structure; the event is solitary in execution and communal only in framing. Samson's adult capacity to be *collegial without being intimate* — warm in the locker room, alone in the apartment — is the same shape.
- An injury or near-miss that ended the Olympic trajectory short of a medal. The record is silent on the specifics, but the *pivot* from athletics into psychiatry is too clean and too immediate to have been gradual. Somewhere around age 21 or 22, the body that had been the entire program declined to deliver the finish, and Samson — characteristically — did not grieve it. He replaced it. The replacement was a graduate-school application.

The pivot from elite athletics to clinical psychiatry is itself worth dwelling on. He did not pivot to coaching (which would have kept him in the gym), to sports medicine (which would have kept him with athletes' bodies), or to law or business (the standard ex-jock exits). He pivoted to *the mind*, and specifically to the branch of medicine concerned with people whose minds have come apart. This is a particular choice. It announces, even at twenty-two, the constellation that will define him: *I will be the one who fixes what no one else can fix.* The grandiosity is not a later overlay. The grandiosity selected the specialty.

It is also during this window — the late undergraduate and early graduate years — that the *verbal* Samson is constructed. The adolescent athlete becomes the postgraduate explainer. He learns the jargon and learns that the jargon *works on people*. He learns that a man with the body of a decathlete and the vocabulary of a clinician occupies an unusual social niche, and that the niche is rewarded. The adult tic of metabolizing his own emotions into clinical language in real time — *"I notice I'm feeling defensive"* — is forged here, not in clinical training proper. By residency, it is already armor.

## III. Graduate Training, Residency, and the Pre-Banner Practice (approx. ages 22–28)

The record indicates Ph.D. and M.D. both, which means roughly six to eight years of combined training compressed by exceptional capacity into something nearer to six. He was a fast student. The combination matters: the Ph.D. side trained him in the *production of knowledge about the mind*, the M.D. side credentialed him for *physical intervention on the brain*, and the psychiatric residency married the two. By the time he reaches Gamma Base he is one of a relatively small population of practitioners equally fluent in psychodynamic formulation and in pharmacology, and that fluency is real, not pretended.

Behavioral patterns observable in the *young attending* period — the year or two of practice before the Banner case — and persistent thereafter:

- **The intake interview as performance.** Samson conducts a first session as a piece of theater. He sits forward. He uses the patient's name three times in the first ten minutes. He drops one piece of credentialing into the conversation — never two — calibrated to the patient's class signaling. He is *very good at this* and patients leave the first session reliably overrepresenting their improvement.
- **The note-taking.** Detailed, neat, written by hand in the room. He uses a fountain pen, not a clipboard pen — an affectation begun in residency that will follow him into the Gamma Base era and become, in surveillance terms, a reliable signature. The pen is always the same model class. He loses them and replaces them; he does not switch.
- **The reading.** Voracious, current, and skewed toward whichever journal has most recently published a piece that flatters or threatens his existing positions. He reads to argue, not to learn. The adult Samson can recite a citation chain on dissociation that runs from Janet through Putnam in two minutes; he cannot tell you what he changed his mind about last year.
- **The case selection.** From the very beginning of independent practice, he reaches for the *hard case*. He does not build a stable practice of moderate neurotic patients and grow slowly. He goes after the dissociative inpatients, the forensic referrals, the cases nobody else wants because they are too complex or too dangerous. Banner is not an aberration in this pattern; Banner is its apotheosis. By the time the Gamma Base referral comes across his desk, Samson has been training for it for two years.
- **The relationship to colleagues.** He is *liked* by peers and *not trusted* by them. Within eighteen months of beginning practice he has already accumulated the reputation of a man whose opinion you want at a case conference and whose patient you would not want to inherit if he had to transfer.
- **The first inklings of the romantic pattern.** In the pre-Banner period the record contains no named partner, which — given his presentation, capability, and visibility — is itself anomalous and informative. He dates; he does not couple. The pattern is already serial-pursuit-and-drift, calibrated to women who are accomplished, often unavailable, and reliably impressed by his presentation in the short term and disappointed by his unavailability in the medium term.

## IV. The Referral, the Site, and the First Weeks at Gamma Base

The Banner referral arrives via the Army. Samson is brought in as a civilian consultant, junior to the existing Gamma Base medical and military hierarchy, on what is — even within the universe — the single most consequential psychiatric case extant. He is twenty-eight or twenty-nine. He has been in independent practice for perhaps two years. The referral is a *coup* for his career and an *injury* to his self-concept simultaneously: a coup because no one his age has access to this material, an injury because the institutional framing places him under Ross, under the existing medical staff, and beneath Banner himself in epistemic priority. He is, on arrival, *the kid the Army brought in to take a look.*

The first weeks at Gamma Base are observable in fine grain from the early Thomas issues and from inference about a man of his profile dropped into a base of that kind:

- He is on-site, not commuting. Housed in officers' quarters. Eats in the mess. Runs the perimeter at dawn — a habit that immediately registers with the MPs and earns him an early reputation as a particular *kind* of civilian: the kind who shows the soldiers up at PT and then writes their commander's report.
- He requests, and gets, full access to the Banner files. He reads them in a single sitting — characteristic — and forms a unified theory within seventy-two hours. The theory is essentially correct in outline (dissociation, childhood etiology, gamma as catalyst rather than cause) and badly overstated in confidence. He does not bracket his certainty.
- He requests and is granted access to Betty Ross. Officially as a collateral interview. Functionally as a meeting. The first conversation runs ninety minutes and ends with both of them aware of the temperature of it. He does not write it up as a countertransference event in his notes. He does not bring it to supervision (he has no supervision; he is the consultant). The omission is the first ethical drift on the case and it occurs in the first week.
- He spars verbally with Thaddeus Ross and loses — not in the room (he is faster than Ross) but in the structure, because Ross holds the access. The loss compounds. By the end of week two, Samson has correctly diagnosed Banner, incorrectly assessed his own position, and developed a private grievance about being *under-deployed* on a case he believes he could break open if given control.

This is the precise emotional substrate from which the *cure-and-self-administration* gambit emerges. It is not — repeat, not — primarily a scientific decision. It is a *positional* decision dressed as a scientific one. Samson is a junior consultant who wishes to be the central figure; the experiment, as designed, would in a single afternoon convert him from the former to the latter.

## V. The Self-Administration (*Incredible Hulk* #141)

The engineered procedure is, on its face, defensible: a controlled siphon of gamma energy from Banner, intended to relieve the patient of the Hulk transformation. The defense begins to fray at the design choices. The procedure is configured to *capture* the siphoned energy rather than disperse it. The capture apparatus is sized to a human recipient. The recipient is on-site. The recipient is Samson. Each of these choices is individually rationalizable; together they constitute a plan to take the gamma into himself, and that plan was operational before the procedure began. He did not improvise. He prepared.

The micro-sequence on the day is worth reconstructing:

1. **Pre-procedure morning.** Standard run, longer than usual (anxiety burn-off). Heavier breakfast than usual (caloric loading — the body knew). Conversation with Betty in a corridor, recorded in his memory as significant; recorded in hers, on the evidence of her subsequent behavior, as cordial.
2. **Procedure setup.** Samson is unusually quiet during setup. The base medical staff, accustomed to his verbal density, note (in the available record and in inference) the change. The quiet is not calm; it is the pre-event focus of the decathlete on the runway.
3. **The siphon.** Executed as designed. Banner is depowered. There is a window — minutes, perhaps less — in which the captured gamma must be disposed of or used.
4. **The self-exposure.** Samson takes the dose. The decision, framed in his subsequent statements as scientific opportunism (*"we may not get this chance again"*), is performed in the presence of Betty Ross and is performed in a manner — the staging, the visibility, the absence of any attempt to consult, document, or delay — that satisfies every criterion of a *gesture* and almost none of an *experiment*. There is no control. There is no protocol filed in advance. There is no consent process for the recipient because the recipient and the investigator are the same person. The act is, in any reasonable framing, *clinical misconduct of a grade that would, in a civilian hospital, terminate a career.* It does not terminate his because the institutional context — Army base, classified program, no IRB, no licensing board with jurisdiction over the gamma — does not have a mechanism for the violation.
5. **The transformation.** Strength augmentation, durability augmentation, the green hair. The hair is the *tell*. A clean somatic side effect would be invisible — augmented capillary density, altered melanin, neurological changes. The hair is a *display* mutation. That it appears at all suggests the gamma is interacting not with random somatic tissue but with the *organizing fantasy* the recipient brought to the exposure. He came to the procedure carrying the Samson-myth identification he had carried since boyhood, and the gamma rendered that identification visible. The follicular-strength gimmick — strength scales with hair length, haircuts diminish him — is psychosomatic in mechanism; the mythic schema is loading the physiology.
6. **The immediate fallout.** Banner re-Hulks within hours. The first Samson–Hulk fight occurs that day or the next. Samson wins, or fights to a draw, in a manner that confirms — to Betty, to Ross, to himself — the new positional reality. He has converted himself from junior consultant to central figure in a single afternoon, exactly as the unconscious plan required.

## VI. The First Year of the Identity (approx. age 29–30)

The year following the self-administration is the formative window for the *role*, as distinct from the powers. Several behaviors solidify here that will persist for forty years:

- **The codename.** "Doc Samson" — chosen by himself, retained by the press, kept by him through every subsequent identity crisis. Note the structure: the credential and the patronymic. Not a heroic noun (*the Strongman*, *Goliath*), not a concealment (*the Stranger*). His professional title and his given name. The codename refuses to separate the doctor from the hero. This is operational: he will not allow the institutions of medicine to disclaim him for the cape, and he will not allow the institutions of heroism to disclaim him for the clinical work. He insists on being both, in a single nominal package, and the insistence forecloses the disclaimers in advance.
- **The hair as grooming object.** He keeps it long enough for power and short enough for clinical credibility. This calibration becomes a daily attention point and remains one. He learns within months which lengths produce which strength gradients and develops a personal protocol — never publicly disclosed — for haircut timing around anticipated combat.
- **The costume.** Adopted within weeks. The wardrobe choice is consistent with the rest of him: form-displaying rather than form-concealing, color-saturated, expensive in implication. He is not hiding the body that gamma augmented; he is *frame*-ing it. The costume is, in effect, the singlet of the decathlete redrawn for adult deployment.
- **The press posture.** Cooperative with media from the first interview. He gives quotes. He poses. He uses the visibility to advance both the heroic and the clinical identities — early-1970s press coverage of "Doc Samson" reliably mentions his credentials, which is not standard for the genre. He is *deliberately laundering reputation in both directions*.
- **The Banner relationship reformulates.** The patient becomes, irreversibly, the rival, the foil, the recurrent occasion. Samson does not transfer the case. He does not recuse. He intensifies his involvement, now armored against Banner's physical capacity. The rationalization — *I am the only one who can both treat him and survive him* — is, narrowly, true. It is also self-serving in a way that no one in the institutional structure has the standing or the inclination to challenge.
- **The Betty pursuit acquires its forty-year shape.** Refused, partially, in the immediate aftermath of the self-administration — Betty is unsettled by the gesture rather than seduced by it, which is the first data point Samson fails to integrate. He does not withdraw. He recalibrates. The pursuit becomes ambient rather than acute: he is *present*, he is *available*, he is *patient*, he is *there when Banner is not*. This posture, sustained across decades through her engagements, her marriage, her transformations, and her deaths, is the single most stable behavioral pattern in his entire file. It was set in the year after the gamma, and it never updates.
- **The drinking begins, quietly.** Not yet pathological. A scotch at the end of a long day at the base. Two when the day involved a Hulk fight. The pattern is normative for a 1970s male professional and gives no immediate cause for concern. The pattern *that began here* is the one that escalates over two decades and arrives, by the late 1990s, at the AUD presentation documented elsewhere in this file.

## VII. The Foreclosed Alternatives

A surveillance file of this resolution should record not only what the subject did but what he conspicuously did *not* do in the formation window, because the non-events constrain the personality as tightly as the events.

He did not, after the self-administration, request reassignment or recusal from the Banner case. He did not seek peer consultation about the ethical breach. He did not enter personal psychotherapy — a striking omission for a psychiatrist who had just self-experimented with a Class-novel mutagenic agent in front of the object of his romantic interest. He did not, in the years following, return to academic publishing in a way commensurate with his unique access to the Banner material; the papers that would have established him as the leading authority on gamma-mediated dissociation were never written, because writing them would have required a level of self-disclosure about methodology that he was unwilling to commit to print. He did not marry. He did not, as far as the record shows, form a single non-instrumental friendship outside the gamma-affected population during the entire formation decade.

Each of these non-events is a *choice*, and each of them locks in a feature of the adult subject. The refusal to recuse locks in the Banner enmeshment. The refusal of personal therapy locks in the countertransference blind spot. The refusal to publish locks in the *performance*-rather-than-*scholarship* shape of his career. The absence of marriage locks in the Betty-script. The absence of non-instrumental friendship locks in the loneliness that the drinking will eventually be deployed to manage.

## VIII. Summary of the Formation

By approximately age thirty, Leonard Samson has completed his formation. The architecture is set. A boy named for a strongman became an athlete who became a clinician who became, in a single engineered afternoon, a costumed figure whose somatic self-display literalized the parental script he had carried since before consent. The clinical competence is real and the grandiosity is real and they are not — for him — in conflict; they are the same engine running in two registers. The relationships that will define the next four decades — with Banner, with Betty, with the institutions that pay him, with the bottle — are all initiated or pre-figured in the eighteen months that bracket *Incredible Hulk* #141. The man who walks out of that year is the man who walks, recognizably, into every subsequent era of this file, until the catastrophe of the late 2000s finally forces the revision that the formation refused.

Everything after is elaboration.


## Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

# CHRONOLOGY III — THE DEFINING MIDDLE PERIOD

## Frame and Boundaries

The middle period of Leonard Samson's life runs, in the published record, from roughly the latter Mantlo issues of *Incredible Hulk* (mid-1980s) through the closing chapters of Peter David's first run (1998), with a brief codicil into the Jenkins/Casey transitional material before the Bruce Jones tenure changes the texture of the surveillance entirely. This is the longest single stable phase of his existence — well over a decade of consistent on-page presence — and it is the phase in which he is most himself in both directions: most genuinely competent, most genuinely dangerous to himself and others. It is also the phase that produces the only piece of work he will ever do that justifies the costume.

If Era 1 was the ambitious resident who irradiated himself in front of his preceptor's girlfriend, Era 2 is the attending physician who has earned his consult privileges and now has to live inside the institution he flirted his way into. The granular file for this period is dense because the subject sat still long enough to be observed at length. He kept an office. He kept hours. He kept patterns.

## The Gamma Base / Hulkbuster Base Tenure (Mantlo Era → Early David)

By the mid-1980s Samson is no longer the visiting expert; he is, functionally, the in-house psychiatric service for the most consequential gamma-mutate caseload on the planet. Surveillance file would log:

- **A residence-of-record at or adjacent to Gamma Base / Hulkbuster Base**, Desert Southwest. Through this period he maintains what reads as a small on-base apartment plus, intermittently, a leased house in the nearest civilian town; the on-base unit is his de facto home during active cases and the off-base lease is largely fictional — receipts, not residence. He sleeps where the work is.
- **A consultative-track contract with the Department of Defense via the Hulkbuster project**, with a salary line that would, by the late 1980s, place him in the upper civilian-consultant tier. He treats the money with the affected indifference of a man who very much pays attention to it; the indifference is a tell.
- **Office signatures**: a window office facing the test range, not the parking lot — he wants to see what comes in over the horizon. A heavy desk kept conspicuously clear. Diplomas hung at eye level for the seated patient, not standing height for his own ego (a real clinician's choice, and one of the small details that argues for the authenticity of his craft). A second chair, not a couch — he conducts almost all sessions face-to-face, slightly off-axis, knees not directly squared, which is textbook.
- **Daily route**: pre-dawn run on the perimeter road, three to six miles depending on the previous night, in all weather. The run is non-negotiable through this entire period and is the single most stable behavior in the file. He is an ex-decathlete; the body remembers. After the run, coffee at the commissary, where he reads two newspapers (one national, one regional) front to back before any clinical contact. Sessions stacked in the morning. Afternoons for written work, file review, and — increasingly across the period — the gym, where his presence becomes a small daily theater for enlisted personnel and visiting personnel alike.

The pattern in this stretch is high-functioning, high-output, and visibly disciplined. The narcissism is well-fed by the institutional setting and therefore quiet. He does not need to seize attention because he is already, structurally, the most interesting civilian on a base full of people whose job is to watch him.

## The Hulkbusters

Samson's leadership of the civilian-scientist Hulkbusters team — Carolyn Parmenter, Samuel LaRoquette, Hideko Takata, Armand Martel — is, in the file, the first clear documentation of a behavioral cluster that will recur for the rest of his career: **he gathers people around him whom he can be the largest of, and he loses them.** The team is competent, brave, civilian; he trains them; they die in combat with the Hulk's environment, not the Hulk himself. The granular surveillance entry is not that he lost the team — losses happen — but in *what he did the week after*. The record shows:

- A short, intense pursuit of Betty Ross in the immediate aftermath, with elevated frequency of "professional" visits to her quarters. The grief is real; the channeling of it is diagnostic.
- A measurable uptick in gym time and a first documented increase in evening drinking, though still within social-norm ranges.
- A clipped, jurisdictional tone in case notes from this period — he is angry at the Army, at Ross, at the universe — that he never reproduces in patient-facing material. The split between front-stage and back-stage register widens here and never fully closes again.

He does not assemble a comparable team again. That, too, is data: he learned the wrong lesson, which was *don't have peers*, rather than *don't put civilians in the line*.

## The Banner Case as Career

The defining clinical relationship of his life is not a relationship he chose so much as one he refused to relinquish. Through the late Mantlo and early David years he is the only psychiatrist on Earth with continuous longitudinal data on Bruce Banner. The file in his cabinet by 1988 would be enormous: serial MMPI-equivalents, dissociative-experience scales repeated quarterly, narrative session notes in his own dense longhand (he writes by hand for clinical work and types only administrative material — observable consistency), Rorschach protocols he scored himself, sleep-architecture data from base infirmary cooperation, and a private chronological annotated list of every documented Hulk transformation with antecedents, duration, and resolution. This is, by any measure, real work. No one else on the planet has done it. He knows that, and the knowing organizes him.

The countertransference in those notes — which a careful reader of his hand could detect across years — runs in two registers. The clinical register is sharp, restrained, and ethically attentive. The marginal register — the underlines, the question marks, the occasional pressed-through period — clusters reliably around any mention of Betty, any mention of Banner's competence, and any mention of Banner being seen by other clinicians. The marginalia are the man.

## The Crossroads Period and the Grey Hulk

When Banner is exiled to the Crossroads dimension and later when the Grey "Mr. Fixit" persona surfaces in Las Vegas, Samson's surveillance pattern shifts. With his primary patient effectively off-grid, he loses the organizing object of his weeks. The file for this stretch records:

- **Travel.** He becomes itinerant — guest lectures, consulting work for SHIELD on metahuman dissociation, a brief and slightly embarrassing East-Coast media tour (talk-radio appearances, one cable interview that he watches more than once on tape — base AV staff would remember the request). He is filling time.
- **Expanded romantic surveillance footprint.** With Betty also out of immediate range, he is, briefly, seen with other women. None last. The pattern in those courtships is the same one he runs with Betty in compressed form: rapid idealization, intense pursuit, withdrawal at the first sign that the woman has interior weather of her own.
- **The first frank, on-record bouts of heavy drinking.** Still socially camouflaged — at conferences, at hotel bars, with colleagues — but the quantities reported by people who would later be interviewed are not social quantities.

When Banner re-surfaces and the Grey Hulk takes the foreground, Samson reorients immediately. The Vegas-era confrontations between them are technically combat episodes but read in the file as a clinician trying to re-establish a case relationship by the only currency the case will accept. The Grey Hulk's contempt for him is, importantly, accurate — Mr. Fixit sees through the cape to the rival underneath in a way that Banner-in-his-own-skin never quite allows himself to — and Samson registers it. The surveillance log would note a brief, sharp depressive dip after the Vegas confrontations: skipped runs (rare), an uncharacteristic three days without shaving, declined social invitations.

## The Hypnotic Integration — His Hour

The arc culminating in *Incredible Hulk* #377 is the apex of his recorded existence, and the file should treat it with the weight it deserves. What he accomplished, technically:

- **A sustained, multi-session hypnotic-regression protocol** with a patient whose dissociative structure was both genuinely severe and complicated by ongoing somatic transformation. He had no literature to draw on. He built the protocol.
- **A correct etiological reading** of Banner's dissociation as the sequelae of childhood physical and emotional abuse by Brian Banner, against a then-prevailing tendency in Banner's own life to locate the pathology in the gamma rather than the history. This reading is right and Samson got there first.
- **An integration outcome** — the so-called Merged or "Professor" Hulk — that was stable for a meaningful period, functional in both registers (cognitive and physical), and that gave Banner the longest sustained period of equilibrium of his adult life.

The somatic-behavioral surveillance during the integration weeks is uncharacteristic and worth flagging. He runs less. He drinks not at all. He cancels social engagements. He sleeps in his office on a folding cot more nights than not. He is, by every observable index, organized by the work. **This is the one period in the file in which the patient is genuinely more important to him than the performance, and it produces the only piece of work that survives him.** It is also the only sustained period in which the gap between official self-concept (great healer) and functional self-concept (man who needs to be seen as great healer) closes. The implication is precise and worth writing in capital letters in the margin: he is capable of being the man he says he is. He is just rarely organized to be.

The Betty situation in the same window is the proof of his limits. Even during the integration, the marginalia spike. He cannot be in the room with Banner-fixed without registering, in his peripheral attention, that fixing Banner also fixes Banner's marriage. The work is clean. The wanting is not. He never resolves this, and the integration's eventual unraveling — which is not his fault, the world being what it is — releases him from the discipline the case imposed.

## The Pantheon Years and the Marriage He Did Not Stop

When Banner takes up with the Pantheon in Nevada and the Merged Hulk operates as a functional public figure, Samson's institutional position quietly erodes. He is no longer the indispensable consultant; the patient has graduated, in some sense, and has new minders. The file in this stretch documents:

- **The Banner–Ross wedding and its aftermath.** Samson attends. He behaves correctly. The cost of behaving correctly is visible to anyone watching closely: he leaves earlier than the receiving line would expect, he does not dance, and he drives himself rather than accepting a ride. The week after, he initiates two new consulting contracts and a media commitment, filling the hours with structure.
- **A drift toward the SHIELD orbit.** He had always been government-adjacent; in this stretch he becomes government-embedded, accepting work on metahuman psychological assessment for purposes that are less therapeutic and more security-screening. The work pays well, suits his vanity (the briefings are classified, the assessments are consequential), and corrodes his clinical ethic by inches. A practitioner who once kept tight boundaries around what a session was *for* is, by the mid-90s, conducting interviews under quasi-clinical pretenses that are actually adversarial assessments. He knows. He does it anyway.
- **The first instances of operating clinically while intoxicated.** Not floridly. He is too disciplined for that. But the surveillance pattern shows him keeping bourbon in the lower desk drawer, the office door locked for "writing time" in the late afternoon, breath mints in conspicuous supply, and the run shortened or skipped after late-evening sessions. Patients in this period do not appear to have been harmed by it — he is functional at much higher blood-alcohol levels than most because he is large and because he is practiced — but the line has been crossed. He does not bring it back.

## Combat Patterns Through the Middle Period

A file built from observation, not just record, would catalogue his fighting style with the care it deserves, because the style is psychological. Across the middle period he is in the field repeatedly — Hulk encounters, Leader incursions, the various Abominations, the Pantheon's external threats, the occasional Avengers mobilization. The granular observations:

- **He fights upright and theatrical.** Stance squared, chest out, almost a wrestler's address rather than a brawler's. He throws with his hips, not his shoulders, which is the decathlete's torso showing through.
- **He talks during combat.** Constantly. The patter is part deflection, part exhibition, part — and this is the clinical reading — anxiolytic. The voice keeps him company. Silent opponents disturb him more than they should.
- **He pulls punches against Banner and does not realize it.** The fight telemetry across years would show measurably less commitment in the contact between Samson and Hulk than between Samson and any other gamma-class opponent of comparable strength. He would deny this if asked. It is true.
- **He takes head trauma badly and conceals it.** Multiple concussion-equivalent events in this period are followed by a refusal to be benched and by accelerated return to clinical work. The cumulative neurological cost across the middle period is not zero and contributes, by the closing years of the era, to a small but observable shortening of his patience and a coarsening of his judgment.

## The Romantic File: Betty, and the Pattern Around Betty

Across the middle period the Betty Ross pursuit modulates but never extinguishes. The behavioral signature is consistent enough to be timed:

- **Proximity-seeking after Banner setbacks.** Within seventy-two hours of any major Banner crisis — transformation event, public incident, marital trouble — Samson initiates contact with Betty under a professional pretext. The pretext is usually plausible. The frequency is the tell.
- **A particular vocal register reserved for her.** Lower, slower, more pauses. Colleagues who heard him in normal conversation and then in a Betty conversation would notice. He does not modulate this consciously.
- **Gift-giving that he codes as collegial.** Books, mostly — clinical literature she "might find interesting," small monographs, the occasional novel. The annotations he writes in the flyleaves before giving them are longer than collegial annotations are.
- **A consistent inability to congratulate Banner about her in Banner's presence.** He can do it about anything else. About her, the sentence will not form.

He does not act on any of this in ways that would meet a misconduct threshold. He does not have to. The pattern is the misconduct; the line he does not cross is a line he is always standing on.

## The Slow Slide — Late David Years into Jenkins/Casey

By the closing years of David's run, the surveillance file thickens with small derangements:

- **Sleep architecture deteriorates.** Lights on in his quarters past 3 AM more nights than not. He reads, drinks, watches old fight footage of himself, and — a small, telling detail — replays tapes of his own early media appearances. The tapes are a comfort. The comfort is humiliating, which is why he watches them alone.
- **Increased irritability with administrative staff.** A man who had been generous with secretaries and orderlies becomes briefly, then chronically, short. He apologizes after, which is to his credit, but the apologies themselves become a pattern.
- **A widening gap between his written work and his spoken work.** The writing remains sharp. The talks become looser, more anecdotal, more reliant on his reputation and his physical presence to carry rooms that the argument no longer commands. Conference attendees in this stretch would, in candid interview, describe him as "still impressive" with the small pause before "impressive" that means *not as impressive as he was*.
- **Re-irradiation behaviors begin.** The first of what will become the late-career pattern of pursuing additional gamma exposure to maintain or augment his physical signature. In the middle period these are framed as operational necessity, and there is always a plausible operational reason. The frequency, against the actual operational tempo, does not quite match. The hair, which is the somatic index of his self, is closely monitored by him in mirrors and reflective surfaces — a behavior base personnel would have logged in passing for years without recognizing it as the compulsion it is.

## What the Middle Period Establishes

By the close of this era — Banner separated from the Merged integration, the marriage with Betty under strain that will end in her gamma poisoning and apparent death, Samson himself drinking more, sleeping less, taking work he should not take and pulling rank he has not earned in rooms he should not be in — the structural diagnosis is settled. The narcissism is load-bearing. The competence is real. The alcohol is becoming a problem the conscience cannot yet name. The Banner relationship is the spine of his life and he cannot acknowledge that without acknowledging what it costs him to be adjacent to a happiness that is not his.

The middle period is the answer to the question the early period posed. The early period asked whether the man who irradiated himself in front of his rival's girlfriend was a flawed promising clinician or a clinician-shaped narcissistic structure. The middle period answers: *both, durably, and the structure will win when the structure is pressed hard enough.* The pressing comes in Era 3. The middle period is the long, productive, observable, increasingly compromised run-up to it, and the file for these years is the thickest single stretch in his dossier because it is the stretch in which he was most fully, recognizably, himself — for better and, with growing weight, for worse.


## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

# Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

## IV.1 The Hinge: Surviving One's Own Catastrophe (post-*World War Hulks*, ~2010-2011)

Subject re-enters the record after the *World War Hulks* arc as a man who has died on-panel, been resurrected, been physically and neurologically tampered with by the Leader and MODOK, and been forced - in front of every meaningful peer and patient - to behave in ways he cannot reconcile with his self-concept. The clinical significance of this period cannot be overstated. For thirty-five published years the Subject's defensive architecture had been built around a single proposition: *I am the doctor; the pathology is over there.* The events of 2009-2010 collapsed that proposition. The pathology was demonstrably, publicly, in him.

In the immediate post-arc period (Parker's *Hulk* run, late 2010 into 2011), Subject is depicted in a posture that surveillance language would categorize as **reduced operational footprint with intermittent re-engagement**. He is not running a practice. He is not on retainer at Gamma Base under his prior terms. He moves between SHIELD-adjacent consults and freelance clinical work for the small constellation of people who will still take his call - Betty Ross (now Red She-Hulk), Rick Jones, a handful of military intelligence handlers who knew him before the collapse. The grandiosity is muted, not extinguished. The hair is shorter than at any prior point in the record. He has stopped, for the first time in his career, *advertising*.

Behavioral micro-pattern in this window: the Subject begins answering questions with questions again — clinical reflex returning — where in the late 2000s he had been answering with declarations. The verbosity tic (Stress Ladder rung 1) is *down*. This is meaningful. A narcissistic structure that has been genuinely shocked, rather than merely embarrassed, talks less.

## IV.2 The Quiet Years and the Sobriety Project (~2011-2014)

There is a deliberately thin published record across this stretch — which, for a man whose prior pattern was to be in every room with a camera, is itself the data. Subject is reported (Parker, *Red She-Hulk*; ancillary appearances) as living in a leased apartment in the Washington corridor, then later a small house in northern Virginia within commuting distance of three separate federal facilities. He is consulting, not running. He is reading more than publishing. The standing claim of "foremost Banner authority" is, during this stretch, *quietly transferred* to others in the field by professional consensus, and he does not contest it.

The Alcohol Use Disorder catalogued in Section 2 enters apparent remission in this window. The evidence is circumstantial but consistent:

- Absence of the prior on-panel drinking tells (the glass at the desk during sessions; the bar appearance before fights).
- A new conversational tic — declining offered drinks with a flat "no thanks" rather than the prior performative "not while I'm working" — which reads as someone who has stopped negotiating with the substance.
- An observable change in his post-combat decompression behavior. Where the 2000s Subject would adjourn to a bar with whoever was nearest, the post-2011 Subject is repeatedly shown going home alone, often walking.
- A re-emergence of physical-conditioning habits consistent with his decathlete baseline — early running, weight work, swim sessions — i.e., the body re-engaged as a regulator rather than as a brand.

No on-panel AA meeting, no on-panel sponsor, no on-panel formal program is confirmed in canon. A surveillance file would log this as **probable structured recovery, modality undetermined, adherence high based on absence-of-prior-behavior signal**. Given the Subject's intellectualizing tendencies, a cognitive-behavioral or SMART Recovery framework is the most likely match; a Twelve-Step program is possible but would require him to perform a humility he is still, even now, reaching toward rather than inhabiting.

## IV.3 The *Immortal Hulk* Era: Chastened Consultant (~2018-2021)

Subject's appearances during the Ewing run constitute the cleanest psychological data we have on him since the David tenure thirty years earlier. He shows up — episodically, never as a focal protagonist — to do exactly the work he should have been doing all along: **listen, formulate, advise, and step back**. The green hair is present but unstyled. The cape-era flamboyance is essentially gone from his body language. He stands differently. The early-career posture (chest out, weight forward, hands often on hips — the decathlete-on-the-podium silhouette) has yielded to a slightly forward-leaning seated posture with hands clasped, a posture every working clinician eventually arrives at because it is the only one that does not exhaust the lower back across an eight-hour caseload.

Granular tells from this period that a surveillance file would catalogue:
