- **Mastery of a hard subspecialty.** Gamma-related dissociative pathology is a small, ferocious clinical field, and he is one of the two or three living experts. The mastery is real and self-esteem-stabilizing in healthy ways when he leans on it instead of on display.
- **Physical discipline.** The pre-existing athletic identity (the decathlete history) gives him a *non-pathological* container for somatic self-regard. Training, when not in the service of imminent re-irradiation, is genuinely regulating for him. A surveillance file should note the difference between *training* (regulating) and *grooming for display* (pre-acting-out).
- **Teaching and mentorship.** When he is in a teaching role with junior clinicians — not press, not patients — his grandiosity converts into generosity. He is, in those rooms, his best self. The compensation is functional because the audience is too junior to threaten him and too genuinely benefited by him for the exchange to be exploitative.
- **The chastening itself, post-2010.** Survival of his own catastrophe became, eventually, a compensation: he is now the man who knows what happens when this structure fails. That knowledge, held without grandiosity, is a stabilizer. The Ewing-era presentation suggests he has finally let the catastrophe *be his teacher* rather than another credential.

### Negative (maladaptive) Compensations

- **The costumed identity itself.** "Doc Samson" is, at root, a compensation for Leonard Samson — a man who feared being ordinary built a public self that could not be ignored. The green hair is signage. The name is a claim. The costume is the visible architecture of the need.
- **Pursuit of Betty Ross.** Forty years of unrequited pursuit functions as a compensation for an early, unspecified attachment wound: the unattainable woman whose eventual choosing of him would prove he was the better man. It is a self-esteem project transacted in the currency of someone else's body and time.
- **Power acquisition as mood regulation.** Re-irradiation events are, functionally, compensatory: they restore the visible specialness that loss has eroded. Each cycle increases dependence on the mechanism and decreases his capacity to tolerate the un-irradiated baseline.
- **Strategic proximity to power.** His drift toward SHIELD and government contracts in the 90s/2000s is partly compensatory — institutional affiliation as a prosthesis for stable self-worth. The compensation is negative because the institutions in question were, at intervals, actively predatory toward him and his patients, and his need for the affiliation reduced his capacity to refuse the bad bargains.
- **The press persona.** Willingness to be quoted, photographed, interviewed about cases (with appropriate confidentiality, but the *publicity itself* is the issue) compensates for ambient under-recognition. It is also where most of his ethical near-misses cluster.
- **Identification with the patient's largeness.** Treating the world's most consequential gamma case is, for him, partly a compensation for ordinariness: *I am the man who treats that man.* This is why he cannot hand the case off even when he should.

---

## THE COLLAPSE SEQUENCE (how the architecture fails, in order)

The forensic value of the above catalogue is that it predicts the order of failure. Samson does not collapse all at once; he descends the tiers in a sequence that is now well-documented across multiple decompensation events.

1. **Sublimation goes offline first** — productivity decreases, case notes get thinner, clinical writing stops.
2. **Intellectualization intensifies to compensate** — jargon density in speech rises, third-person self-reference increases, the diagnostic-interruption pattern becomes more frequent.
3. **Reaction formation visibly strains** — the over-warmth toward Banner becomes brittle, the smile holds half a beat too long.
4. **Displacement load increases** — combat enthusiasm rises, opponents are dispatched with disproportionate force, post-fight quips get sharper and less self-deflating.
5. **Somatization-via-augmentation begins** — hair grows, training intensifies, silhouette broadens, grooming becomes more deliberate.
6. **Substance use enters or escalates** — drinking moves from social to private to pre-shift.
7. **Acting out** — a major irreversible decision is made under the cover of rationalization.
8. **Omnipotent control** — the post-acting-out world is reorganized internally as one he can manage alone, and the catastrophic phase begins.

A surveillance apparatus monitoring Leonard Samson for clinical risk should set its tripwires at stages 2 and 5 — increased jargon and increased silhouette — because those are the earliest reliably observable indicators and the latest points at which intervention has historically been possible.

---

## CLOSING NOTE

The architecture is not, in the end, the architecture of a bad man. It is the architecture of a gifted one who was given a parental script about exceptionalism before he could refuse it, who was never taught self-deflating humor, who entered a profession that rewarded his intellectualization, and who acquired — at his own hand — a body that ratified every grandiose impulse he had ever had. The defenses are the marks of the wound, not the wound itself. The compensations are the visible shape of an interior that was never given permission to be ordinary. The clinical good news, attested by his late-period presentation, is that the architecture is in principle revisable; the clinical bad news is that revising it required nearly killing himself and several other people first.

He has, at last, the one defense he was missing for forty years: the knowledge of his own machinery. Whether that knowledge holds under the next major stressor is the open question of the file.


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE: LEONARD SAMSON, Ph.D.

## Preamble: Methodology and the Problem of the Missing Childhood

A longitudinal profile ordinarily begins in latency and tracks forward. The Samson file does not permit that: the pre-doctoral record is essentially blank on-page, and what we have begins with a man in his late twenties already credentialed, already armored, already in motion. This absence is itself the first datum. In a universe densely populated by characters whose childhoods are flashbacked obsessively — Banner's father, Stark's father, Richards's prodigy, Rogers's asthma — Samson does not return to source material. He has no flashback because the official self-narrative has no use for one. The boy is sealed off; the man stands fully assembled at the threshold of Gamma Base in 1971 and asks to be admired.

This profile therefore proceeds in four eras corresponding to the four phases of the documentary record, framed in terms of three running axes — **affect regulation, cognitive style, self-concept** — with subsidiary tracking of defenses, object-relations, and somatic-identity integration. Frameworks invoked are standard: Kernbergian structural diagnosis for the personality organization, Vaillant's hierarchy for defenses, Bowlby/Main for attachment, Kohut for the self-object dynamics with Banner and Betty, McWilliams for the high-functioning-narcissistic presentation specifically, and the Yale group's transference-focused formulation for tracking the rivalry-as-therapy problem with Banner across decades.

---

## Era 1 — The Arriving Self (1971 – c. 1979): Grandiosity as Operating System

### Affect regulation
At first contact (the Gamma Base consultancy, *Incredible Hulk* #141) Samson presents as enviably regulated. He is calm in rooms where colonels are shouting. He paces himself in clinical interviews. He produces measured, even elegant formulations of Banner's condition under time pressure. This is the surface. The behavioral record of the next eight years reveals the regulation is *brittle-stable* in Kernberg's sense — held by an integrated but inflexible self-structure that does fine until narcissistic supply is interrupted, at which point regulation collapses into action rather than affect.

The signature decompensation in this era is not tears, withdrawal, or rage in the ordinary sense. It is **immediate translation of injury into spectacular conduct**. The originating instance is paradigmatic: treated as a junior consultant by Ross and the gamma team, eclipsed in Betty's attention by a Banner who at least gets to be the patient, Samson does not sulk and he does not argue. He goes into the chamber. The gamma siphon is not a tantrum; it is a piece of theatre staged on his own body to restore status. Across the decade this pattern repeats in lower-stakes form — he upstages briefings, takes the field unbidden, picks fights he was supposed to mediate. The affect underneath these actions is almost never named on-page. He does not say "I felt humiliated." He says, in effect, "I have reassessed the tactical situation."

By Vaillant's hierarchy this is **acting-out at the immature pole, dressed in the language of sublimation**. The sublimation is partial and real (the work gets done) but the engine driving the action is unmetabolized shame.

### Cognitive style
Genuinely first-rate. The 70s record establishes — and never seriously contradicts — that Samson reads people fast and accurately. His formulations of Banner are good craft from the start: he sees the dissociative architecture before the field has language for it, he intuits the abuse history a decade before David's run confirms it. His pattern-recognition extends to the operational environment; he reads Ross's institutional politics, the Army's information hierarchy, the press's appetite. He is a natural clinician with a natural diagnostician's eye.

The blind spot is precisely shaped and visible from the beginning: **the apparatus does not turn on himself**. He can describe Banner's countertransference to Ross. He cannot describe his own countertransference to Banner, which by issue #150 is already structuring his clinical decisions. He cannot describe his pursuit of Betty in the same terms he would use if a patient described it. This is not deficit; it is *motivated non-knowing*. The cognitive style has a one-way valve.

### Self-concept
Official: brilliant young doctor, athletically exceptional, ethically serious, romantically eligible, professionally indispensable. Functional: a man whose name, hair, and physique are all being deployed simultaneously to keep an audience from leaving the room. The gap is large and entirely unconscious. He believes the official version without reservation.

The Biblical-Samson identification deserves note. Most superheroes acquire a mythic alias; very few are *born* with one. He carries a parental script before he carries powers, and when the powers arrive they slot precisely into the prefabricated identity. The strength-tied-to-hair phenomenon is almost certainly a psychosomatic articulation of that pre-existing identification — gamma is the medium, but the *form* the gamma takes in his body is dictated by a story told over his crib. The self-concept in Era 1 is therefore not constructed; it is *inherited and ratified*.

### Object-relations
Sparse and instrumental. Banner is already the central object — rival, patient, mirror, brother — and the inability to disambiguate these slots is established in the first arc and never resolved in this era. Betty is pursued as object of restoration: winning her would prove the official self-concept correct. Ross is a paternal-institutional figure handled with deference that masks contempt. There are no friendships in the record. No peer to whom he defers without rivalry. No mentor he claims. He arrives, in object-relational terms, *alone with his audience*.

---

## Era 2 — The Functioning Apex (c. 1980 – c. 1995): Mastery in the Service of an Unexamined Engine

### Affect regulation
This is his best decade and a half. The Mantlo and especially the Peter David runs document a Samson whose regulatory capacities have genuinely matured along the working surface. He tolerates extended therapeutic ambiguity. He sits with Banner through dissociative episodes that would have provoked Era-1 Samson into the chamber. The hypnotic regression work culminating in *Incredible Hulk* #377 requires — and gets — sustained, patient, non-grandiose presence over months of in-story time. This is the only extended period in the record where his behavior consistently meets criteria for *neurotic-level* rather than *narcissistic-level* personality organization in the Kernbergian sense.

The mechanism is interesting. The case is large enough to organize him. Banner's pathology is sufficiently spectacular, sufficiently public, and sufficiently identified with Samson personally that the work *itself* supplies the narcissistic provisioning that ordinarily has to be scavenged from rooms. He does not need to upstage the briefing because he is the briefing. Regulation, in other words, is purchased by the scale of the prize. This is **a stable adaptation under specific environmental conditions, not a structural change**. When the conditions later fail, the regulation will fail with them, and on schedule.

The brittle pole remains visible at the edges throughout. Betty's marriage to Banner is a sustained narcissistic injury that he never adequately processes; he simply re-pours it into the work. Power-loss episodes during this era produce reliable depressive withdrawals — short, masked, but real — followed by reliable re-acquisition behaviors. The pattern indistinguishable from relapse begins here; it does not begin in the 2000s when it becomes obvious.

### Cognitive style
Apex. The integration work on the Merged/Professor Hulk is not lucky; it is sophisticated, multi-stage, theoretically literate clinical work. It correctly reads Banner's structure as a dissociative response to childhood abuse (the canonical Brian Banner material), correctly identifies the affective contents partitioned into each alter, correctly sequences integration around containment of the rage-state, and correctly resists premature fusion. As craft it would be respectable on the cover of *JAACAP*.

The blind spot also matures. By Era 2 it is no longer simple non-seeing; it is *active reframing*. The Betty pursuit is now narrated to himself as a long-standing supportive friendship complicated by feeling; the rivalry with Banner is narrated as collegial concern; the impulse to be the one in the room is narrated as duty. He has, in short, developed a sophisticated case-formulation of his own conduct that is wrong in exactly the ways a clinician's self-formulation tends to be wrong — too generous about motive, too vague about pattern, too oriented toward *intent* and away from *consequence*. The one-way valve has become elegant plumbing.

### Self-concept
The Era-2 self-concept achieves its richest articulation. He is now publicly the foremost authority on Banner; he is genuinely heroic in repeated combat appearances; he is integrated into the larger superhuman institutional landscape (Avengers consultancies, SHIELD work begins in this period). The official narrative is, for the first time, *substantially supported by the evidence*. Real mastery. Real contribution. Real heroism.

What does not change is the underlying organization. He still cannot be ordinary; he still cannot tolerate Banner's primacy in Betty's life without restaging it as a clinical problem; he still locates self-worth in being visible. The apex is not transformation; it is *the most flattering possible expression of an unchanged structure*. Kohut's frame applies cleanly: the work with Banner is functioning as a sustained selfobject experience — Banner's need for Samson, Samson's perceived indispensability to Banner, regulates Samson's grandiose-self pole. When Banner stops needing him in that configuration, the regulation will fail.

### Object-relations and somatic identity
Banner is now formally a patient again and informally everything else. Betty's continued unavailability is partitioned off rather than processed. New objects — colleagues at SHIELD, occasional team-ups — are warm in first contact and rivalrous on second. The body remains an active site of identity: he is shown lifting, sparring, grooming the hair. The body is the brand and he tends to the brand. There is no period in the record where he allows the physical performance to lapse, which would be in his clinical interest and which he never does.

---

## Era 3 — The Decompensation (c. 1996 – 2010): Engine Without Track

### Affect regulation
This era is the long version of what Era-1 Samson did in single panels. The selfobject scaffolding of Era 2 erodes for multiple converging reasons: Banner's situation changes repeatedly (death of Betty, exile, the *Planet Hulk* / *World War Hulk* sequence), the integrated Professor Hulk fragments, Samson's clinical role becomes peripheral, the institutional landscape (SHIELD, then the post-*Civil War* security state) makes his consultancies more compromised and less prestigious. The provisioning fails. The structure that the provisioning had been supporting now shows.

Affect regulation degrades on a predictable schedule. The escalation ladder previously confined to single incidents (verbosity → field intervention → power-seeking → substance → catastrophic acting-out) now stretches across years. Verbosity becomes chronic — the David-era jargon-fluency curdles into the late-90s/2000s habit of meeting every question with a small lecture. Field intervention becomes default — he stops being asked to consult and starts inserting himself. Power-seeking takes the form of repeated re-irradiations and increasingly questionable contracts. Substance use is the headline finding of this era and is treated separately below. Catastrophic acting-out lands in *Fall of the Hulks*.

The alcohol pattern requires explicit calibration. The David run shows social drinking that does not yet meet criteria. By the late 90s the drinking is depicted in clinical contexts — before sessions, during paperwork. By the mid-2000s it is depicted after fights and before fights. The behavioral picture across the decade meets DSM-5 AUD criteria moderate-to-severe: tolerance (he is depicted handling volumes that would impair others), use in physically hazardous situations (operating clinically and combatively while intoxicated), continued use despite professional consequences (his work degrades visibly and he does not stop), role failure (consultancies lost, judgments criticized), and — crucially for the personality reading — *use to manage the gap between self-image and conduct*. This last is the diagnostic point. He is not drinking to feel pleasure; he is drinking to keep the official narrative intact against mounting counter-evidence.

### Cognitive style
Visibly degrades. The pattern-recognition that was his signature gift still flashes (his read on the Intelligencia faction in the *Fall* arc is partly correct even as he is being played by them), but the **filtering** has gone. He no longer distinguishes signal from supply. He takes contracts he should refuse because the contracts are flattering. He accepts gamma augmentation under pretexts a sober Era-2 Samson would have shredded in a paragraph. The motivated non-knowing that was elegant plumbing in Era 2 becomes, in Era 3, structural: he cannot afford to know what he is doing, and the alcohol is part of the apparatus that ensures he does not.

The cognitive picture is consistent with what the addictions literature calls **anosognosia of decompensation in a high-functioning personality** — the very skills that protect such individuals from being caught out by others become the skills that protect them from being caught out by themselves. He explains himself plausibly to colleagues throughout this period; he explains himself plausibly to himself; the plausibility is the disease.

### Self-concept
This is the era in which the gap between official and functional self becomes unsustainable. The official self — brilliant healer, hero, indispensable — is now contradicted by daily conduct, and the resulting cognitive dissonance is managed by the only tools the structure has ever possessed: more grandiosity, more substance, more spectacle. *World War Hulk* finds him institutionally weakened, publicly second-rank, and clinically estranged from his defining case. *Fall of the Hulks* finds him already psychologically pre-compromised when the Intelligencia get to him. The "heel turn" rationalized as therapeutic necessity is not a character break; it is the structure doing what the structure has always threatened to do under sufficient injury, finally finding sufficient injury. He is killed (briefly). The on-page death is symbolically exact — the Era-3 self has nowhere left to go.

### Object-relations
Banner is lost as selfobject. Betty's death and complex returns make her unavailable in even fantasy form. The Intelligencia alliances (Leader, MODOK) are object-relational catastrophes — he is partnering with patients' enemies, with figures he would have once formulated as case material, and he does so because they offer him the supply the legitimate field no longer provides. By the end of the era he has, in object-relational terms, run out of legitimate objects.

---

## Era 4 — The Chastening (c. 2011 – present): Knowledge of Self, Late and Costly

### Affect regulation
The post-*Fall* recovery period (Parker's *Hulk* / *Red She-Hulk*, then Ewing's *Immortal Hulk* appearances) shows a markedly different regulatory profile. The verbosity is reduced. The interventions are smaller. The visible drinking is largely absent on-page. He tolerates being secondary in rooms where he was once primary. He sits with Banner — and with the considerably stranger configurations Banner inhabits in the Ewing era — without restaging the encounter as a referendum on himself.

This reads as **post-catastrophic personality reorganization** of the sort the literature documents in narcissistic patients who have survived collapse: not structural change in the deep sense, but a chastened modus operandi in which the grandiose-self pole is held at lower amplitude because the patient has direct experiential knowledge of what high amplitude costs. The defenses have rebalanced toward the mature end of Vaillant's hierarchy — sublimation now genuine rather than partial, suppression deployed where acting-out used to be, and crucially the first emergence in the entire record of **humor as self-deflation**. Era 1–3 Samson made quips; Era 4 Samson, occasionally, makes jokes at his own expense. This is new and it is diagnostic of real movement.

The brittleness has not vanished. Ewing's depiction in particular shows a man who knows the structure is intact under the chastening, who is *managing* rather than *cured*. The sobriety reads as work being done, not as work completed. The grandiosity reads as banked rather than extinguished.

### Cognitive style
The pattern-recognition has recovered, and for the first time in the record it is **turned, with some consistency, on himself**. He acknowledges in late-era dialogue that he was compromised; he acknowledges the Betty pursuit was something other than what he had narrated; he acknowledges the rivalry with Banner. These are admissions an Era-2 Samson at the height of his clinical powers could not have produced. The one-way valve has, partially, opened.

What he sees when he looks does not appear to please him. The late-era affect is consistently more subdued, more tentative, less performative. This is consistent with what the developmental literature calls **earned insight** — late-acquired self-knowledge whose costs are visibly metabolized in the body language of the person who acquired it. He carries his own diagnosis now. He did not before.

### Self-concept
Substantially revised. The official narrative of Eras 1–3 (brilliant, indispensable, heroic, romantically central) has been retired or held in quieter form. The functional self — competent, compromised, fortunate to be alive, professionally diminished but professionally useful — has moved closer to the surface. The gap has narrowed not because the official self grew more accurate but because the functional self has been forced into the open by events the official self could not absorb.

The hair is still green. The body is still tended. The brand persists because the brand is the only continuous external referent he has, and at this point letting it lapse would itself be a destabilizing act. But the relationship to the brand is changed. He wears it now somewhat as a recovering performer wears a stage name off-stage: not without irony, not without continued attachment, and not without the awareness that it was once a great deal more than a name.

### Object-relations
Banner is restored as object, but in a different register: less selfobject, more colleague-and-patient with appropriate distance. The rivalry is acknowledged rather than enacted. Betty, where she appears, is handled without the old pursuit script — what replaces it is something closer to grief, which is the correct affect and which Era 1–3 could never reach. New objects in Era 4 are modest: a few collegial relationships held without the rivalrous edge, occasional mentorship of younger figures in which he is permitted, sometimes, to be the older man who knows things and does not need to prove them.

---

## Cross-Era Synthesis: The Three Axes Over Sixty Years

**Affect regulation** traces a long arc from *brittle-stable* (Era 1) through *environmentally-buffered apparent maturity* (Era 2) through *progressive failure* (Era 3) to *chastened post-catastrophic management* (Era 4). The underlying structure — vulnerability to narcissistic injury, translation of injury into action rather than affect, dependence on supply — is continuous. What changes is the size and quality of the buffers, and whether the patient is currently doing the work of being aware of the structure.

**Cognitive style** traces an arc from *high-functioning with a sealed blind spot* (Eras 1–2) through *degradation under decompensation and substance* (Era 3) to *recovery with the blind spot partially opened* (Era 4). The native intelligence is constant. The deployment of the intelligence on the self varies dramatically. The most striking single longitudinal finding in the file is that *his clinical apparatus was never turned on himself until catastrophe forced it*, and that when it was finally turned, it worked — late, but it worked.

**Self-concept** traces an arc from *inherited and ratified grandiosity* (Era 1) through *grandiosity substantially supported by genuine achievement* (Era 2) through *grandiosity contradicted by conduct and defended by substance* (Era 3) to *narrowed, chastened, more accurate self-account* (Era 4). The Biblical-Samson script installed in childhood was operative throughout Eras 1–3 and is, in Era 4, for the first time held at arm's length — not rejected, but no longer the entire frame.

The structural diagnosis (NPD, high-functioning exhibitionistic presentation, with a closed-out AUD episode in Era 3) is stable across the record. What moves is the *expression* of that structure under varying environmental and somatic conditions. The single most important environmental variable is **the size and dignity of the case he is working on**: organized by a sufficiently large patient (Banner at the height of the integration work), the structure produces some of the best clinical work in the field; deprived of that organization, the structure decompensates predictably and on its established escalation ladder.

The single most important developmental variable is **insight, late-acquired and survivor-grade**. He did not earn it the way the literature would prefer (through analysis, through patient self-examination, through the gradual maturation of defenses). He earned it the way most narcissistic patients who get any of it earn it: by surviving the collapse the structure was always heading toward, and being constitutionally unwilling, afterward, to fully look away from what he saw on the floor.

He is, at the end of the available record, a man who has finally become a competent observer of Leonard Samson. It took him forty years and a death. The work is not done. But it is, at last, being done by the man whose work it always was.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL
## Subject: SAMSON, Leonard, Ph.D. ("Doc Samson")
## Compiled: UATU / Watcher Protocols, Longitudinal File

---

## 0. Framing and Methodological Note

This assessment is constructed from approximately five decades of behavioral observation across professional, combat, social, romantic, and intoxicated states. The subject is himself a doctoral-level clinician (Ph.D., clinical psychology; postdoctoral training in psychiatric consultation; board-equivalent credentials in trauma and dissociation). This produces a specific evidentiary problem: Samson is fluent in the diagnostic language likely to be applied to him, has on multiple occasions used that fluency to pre-empt or redirect colleagues' assessments of him, and has demonstrated a stable lifetime pattern of self-presenting in the register he believes the listener wants. Any formulation must therefore weight *behavior under pressure* and *behavior when he believes he is unobserved* over verbal self-report.

The file uses DSM-5-TR and ICD-11 analog framings; where his clinical era used DSM-III or DSM-IV criteria the equivalents are noted. The differential is deliberately wide, because his presentation is the kind that attracts both over-pathologizing (the green hair, the costume, the operatic relationship history) and under-pathologizing (the credentials, the social fluency, the genuine therapeutic productivity). Both errors are documented in the SHIELD and Gamma Base personnel files. UATU's prior assessors over-corrected in one direction or the other; this section attempts neither.

---

## 1. Principal Diagnosis

### 1.1 Narcissistic Personality Disorder, high-functioning ("exhibitionist/grandiose" subtype with overt features)
**DSM-5-TR 301.81 / ICD-11 6D10.x with prominent narcissism trait domain**

This is the organizing diagnosis. Every other axis-listed condition is either downstream of it, comorbid with it, or has been ruled in/out against it.

**Criterion-by-criterion behavioral mapping:**

1. **Grandiose sense of self-importance.** The chosen professional alias is "Doc Samson." Not "Dr. Samson" — *Doc*, the familiar form, used in formal credentialing contexts where it is inappropriate. The costume is sleeveless across forty years of public appearances regardless of climate or tactical sense. The hair is not incidental; he has, on multiple post-depowering occasions, retained the green dye after his physiology no longer required it. He has accepted speaking honoraria for keynotes on the Banner case while still its primary treating clinician — a boundary violation of which he has never, in any recorded interview or session transcript, acknowledged the irregularity.

2. **Preoccupation with fantasies of unlimited success, brilliance, ideal love.** The Betty Ross pursuit, sustained across her engagement, marriage, transformation, death, and return, is the legible exemplar — an ideal-love fantasy that has demonstrably never accommodated empirical feedback. Less remarked: his repeated unsolicited overtures to consult on cases (Sentry, Wanda Maximoff, the Hood) outside his actual area of demonstrated competence, framed in correspondence as "I'm the only one who can." File search returns this exact phrase or close variants in his communications no fewer than eleven times.

3. **Belief in being "special" and understandable only by similarly special people.** His professional network is conspicuously thin in lateral peers and dense in either *patients of historic stature* (Banner) or *power-equivalent friends* (She-Hulk in her attorney era, Reed Richards on consult). He has no documented sustained collegial relationship with a non-powered, non-famous clinician of his own rank. This is not coincidence.

4. **Need for excessive admiration.** Press behavior is the cleanest data: he gives interviews readily, particularly to outlets that frame him as the *handsome* psychiatrist. He has been photographed, by his own apparent arrangement, mid-bench-press at Gamma Base on three separate occasions for general-circulation publications. The hair, again, functions as a continuous low-grade admiration-seeking signal in any room he enters.

5. **Sense of entitlement.** The originating act — siphoning gamma from a patient and self-administering it — is the purest single datum in this file. A clinician decided, unilaterally and without consultation or IRB equivalent, that *his* enhancement was a justified use of *his patient's* extracted pathology. The rationalization ("I can do more good") is structurally identical to the rationalizations he later produces for crossing Betty's marital boundary and, much later, for the *Fall of the Hulks* arc behaviors.

6. **Interpersonal exploitativeness.** Subtle, because he is a kind man by his own standards and by most observers'. But the Betty pattern is exploitative in structure — he persistently positions himself as her emotional alternative during her marital crises, offering clinical-tinted intimacy that she did not solicit. The pattern with junior colleagues at Gamma Base is to enlist them as audience and then credit them inconsistently in published work.

7. **Lack of empathy — specifically, an inability to *recognize* the inner states of those who threaten his self-image.** Note carefully: he has high empathy for *patients*, where the role is structurally subordinate to him. He has notably impaired empathy for Banner-as-rival (he consistently misreads Banner's distress at his presence as gratitude for it), for Betty-as-married-woman (he reads her warmth as latent receptivity), and for himself in the role of supplicant (he cannot perceive what he looks like to others when he is asking for something).

8. **Envy.** Less overt, more inferential. The envy is specifically of Banner — of Banner's intellect (which exceeds his), of Banner's monstrous specialness (which trumps his costume), and of Banner's marriage. The compensatory move is to position himself as Banner's *doctor*, which converts envy into hierarchy.

9. **Arrogant, haughty behaviors.** Modulated by training — he has been taught not to display this and usually doesn't. Surfaces under alcohol, fatigue, or following narcissistic injury; the change is then dramatic and noticed by subordinates within minutes.

**Subtype specification.** The DSM-5-TR Alternative Model (Section III) and ICD-11 trait-domain framing both capture him better than the categorical: *high negative affectivity (covert anxiety re: ordinariness), low detachment (he is engaged, not withdrawn), moderate antagonism (grandiosity, attention-seeking, manipulativeness in the romantic domain), low disinhibition (he is in fact disciplined and orderly), low psychoticism.* Grandiose features dominate; vulnerable features become visible during depowered intervals and are managed with alcohol.

**Severity.** Moderate. The disorder is ego-syntonic and largely undefended in his own mind, but he retains sufficient interpersonal function, conscience, and capacity for sustained work that the impairment is selective rather than global.

---

## 2. Comorbid Conditions

### 2.1 Alcohol Use Disorder, moderate-to-severe, episodic course, in sustained partial remission (later era)
**DSM-5-TR 303.90 / ICD-11 6C40.2**

Onset behaviorally datable to the mid-to-late 1990s — earlier social drinking is present in the record but does not meet criteria. The escalation is concurrent with: (a) the consolidation of Banner's marriage to Ross, (b) the achievement and then routinization of the Merged/Professor Hulk integration (i.e., the loss of the *case* that organized him), and (c) the first significant depowering arc of that era. Three losses, stacked.

**Criteria met during peak period (roughly 1998–2008):**

- Use in larger amounts/over longer periods than intended (file contains observation of him finishing bottles he had described as "a glass with dinner").
- Persistent desire and unsuccessful efforts to cut down (one documented private comment to a colleague at a Helicarrier briefing: "I'm going to stop after this contract." He did not.).
- Considerable time obtaining/using/recovering — masked by the powered metabolism, which clears ethanol faster than baseline and therefore *enables* a higher functional dose.
- Craving — inferred from behavior, not self-reported.
- Role failure — late sessions, irritable consultations, the late-era pattern of taking field assignments that should have gone to colleagues.
- Continued use despite interpersonal problems.
- Hazardous use — drinking before piloting, before combat deployment, before patient sessions. This is the most serious criterion he met.
- Tolerance — clear, complicated by gamma physiology.
- Withdrawal — uncertain; his physiology likely masked it.

**Course.** Episodic, mood-reactive, sharply worse during periods of professional eclipse. The post–*World War Hulks* presentation suggests genuine recovery work, possibly facilitated by the chastening of having been demonstrably manipulated while compromised. Late-era observation (post-2011) shows the orderly affect, slightly flat humor, and characteristic verbal carefulness of someone who has been sober long enough for it to be identity rather than effort, but not so long that he has stopped noticing.

### 2.2 Other Specified Trauma- and Stressor-Related Disorder (post–Fall of the Hulks sequelae)
**DSM-5-TR 309.89 / ICD-11 6B4Y**

Does not meet full PTSD criteria — re-experiencing is muted, avoidance is partial, hyperarousal is masked by baseline grandiosity. But the post-event presentation includes a documented narrowing of affect, a change in his relationship to his own body (he stops weight-training compulsively, an enormous behavioral shift), a new tentativeness in clinical assertion, and a recurrent rumination pattern around the question of what within him was *available* to that manipulation. The trauma is partly somatic (he was killed), partly moral-injury (he did harm while compromised), and partly narcissistic (the public knew). This last is, paradoxically, the dimension that has been most therapeutic for him.

### 2.3 Persistent Depressive Disorder, episodic, with mood-reactivity to power state
**DSM-5-TR 300.4 / ICD-11 6A72**

A low-grade dysthymic floor is visible across all eras between bursts of grandiose deployment. It is not endogenous; it is reliably worse during depowered intervals and reliably better during costumed activity. This pattern itself is diagnostic — his depression is the negative space around his narcissistic supplies.

---

## 3. Etiology

The canonical childhood record is sparse to the point of being itself a finding. In a milieu where extensive flashback material is standard for figures of his prominence, his is the silence of someone who does not return to the material. UATU's inference, weighted by adult pattern:

**The name is the wound.** "Leonard Samson" is a parental naming-as-prophecy. A child given the name of the Biblical strongman, by parents who then either reinforced or failed to relieve the burden, grows up performing exceptionality before he can evaluate it. The hair conceit and the literal hair-strength mechanism are not coincidental — they are the unconscious literalization of a script he has been carrying since pre-verbal life. His later choice of decathlon (the ten-event sport, the test of *general* exceptionalism rather than any specialty) and then of psychiatry (the *meta*-discipline, the one that looks down on the others) suggests a child who learned that to be ordinary was to be unloved, and who chose ladders that could in principle have no top.

**The absent family.** Most likely: a parent (probably father, by base-rate inference from the naming and the athletic pressure) who loved conditionally on performance, and a parent (possibly mother) whose response was either collusion or eclipse. The complete absence of siblings in the record may be real or may be a foreclosure of sibling rivalry that he could not afford to remember. His adult fixation on Banner — a fraternal-rivalrous relationship in everything but blood — strongly suggests a sibling-shaped hole.

**The absence of pre-Banner romantic history.** Adult intimacy seems to begin with Betty Ross, in his late twenties, and to fixate there for forty subsequent years. This is not the history of a man who has had ordinary romantic development; it is the history of a man for whom the first significant object also became the eternal one, because revising the script would require facing what made the script.

---

## 4. Symptom Presentation in Behavior — A Field Guide

Because Samson is a clinician who can pass standard interview, the file privileges *behaviorally observable* tells over self-report.

- **The verbosity-jargon escalator.** When stressed, sentence length increases and Latinate clinical vocabulary density rises. By the time he is using three polysyllabic technical terms in a single sentence, decompensation is roughly twenty minutes away.
- **The mirror-check.** A documented micro-tic: he runs a hand back through his hair (right hand, always) when he enters a room with new people in it. The gesture is calibration of the brand.
- **The flex-on-arrival.** In combat-adjacent contexts he plants his feet slightly wider than functional and squares his shoulders before speaking. The pose pre-dates the powers — it appears in his decathlon-era photographs.
- **The pronoun shift.** Under narcissistic injury, his "we" (collaborative) shifts to "I" (proprietary) within two or three exchanges.
- **The third drink.** His functional drinking threshold is approximately three measures of distilled spirit; the fourth, when it occurs, reliably precedes either a clinical mistake or an inappropriate communication to Betty Ross within twenty-four hours. This pattern is documented across at least nine independent incidents.
- **The vanishing humor.** When he is well, he makes self-deflating jokes. When he is unwell, his humor becomes purely performative — quips at others' expense, never his own. The disappearance of self-irony is the single most reliable early-warning indicator in the file.
- **The session over-run.** Healthy Samson keeps strict fifty-minute hours. Unhealthy Samson runs sessions long with patients who admire him and short with patients who challenge him.

---

## 5. Course Over Time

**Era 1 (1971–early 1980s):** NPD florid and unselfconscious. No substance use of note. Productivity high, ethics shaky, insight near zero. Functions as the "young brilliant consultant" archetype; the milieu rewards him for traits that should have been flagged.

**Era 2 (mid-1980s–mid-1990s):** NPD stable; sublimation channel is wide open and producing the best clinical work of his life (the Merged Hulk integration). Alcohol use present but subclinical. This is his healthiest period, and the mechanism of the health is that the case was big enough to make him forget himself. The diagnosis explains the success: a grandiose clinician given a grandiose-scale patient operates near his ceiling.

**Era 3 (late 1990s–2008):** Decompensation. The case stabilizes (loss of organizing object), the marriage solidifies (loss of fantasized future), and the alcohol fills the gap. NPD shifts toward vulnerable features under the surface while overt grandiosity intensifies as compensation. Ethical drift accelerates. Culminates in catastrophic acting-out under external manipulation (*Fall of the Hulks*) — note that the manipulation *worked* because the fault lines were already there; he was not made narcissistic by the Leader, he was *steered* by his narcissism.

**Era 4 (post-2010):** Survivor presentation. NPD attenuated, partly by chastening, partly by sobriety, partly by aging. The grandiosity is now visible *to him*; the disorder is less of an engine and more of a known terrain he navigates around. He is, for the first time in the file, capable of being the second-most-important person in a room without acting on the discomfort.

---

## 6. Differential Diagnosis — What He Is *Not*, and Why

### 6.1 Antisocial Personality Disorder — Ruled out.
Superficial appeal because of the ethical violations (the gamma self-administration, the Betty pursuit, the late-era ethical drift). But ASPD requires a pervasive disregard for the rights of others and an absent or sharply attenuated conscience. Samson has a functional, even hypertrophied, conscience — *which is why his violations require elaborate rationalization*. ASPD does not rationalize; it does not need to. Samson's guilt, when it surfaces, is real and somatically expressed (the post–*Fall of the Hulks* affect change is grief, not adjustment). His childhood conduct record, while sparse, contains no antecedents (no fire-setting, no cruelty, no theft). Rule out with confidence.

### 6.2 Bipolar I or II — Ruled out.
The pattern of high-energy productive periods alternating with withdrawn depressive ones superficially resembles bipolar spectrum. But: his "highs" are personality-congruent and stable in *quality* over decades (the same grandiosity, the same self-presentation), not episodic mood elevations with the characteristic features (decreased sleep need, pressured speech beyond his baseline, flight of ideas, hypersexual disinhibition beyond his stable pattern, goal-directed activity in domains outside his usual interests). His "lows" are reactive to identifiable losses (power, Betty, professional standing) and remit when the precipitant remits or is replaced. No documented hospitalization for mood. No medication response history suggesting mood-stabilizer benefit. Rule out.

### 6.3 Histrionic Personality Disorder — Considered, rejected as primary.
Real overlap: theatricality, attention-seeking, sexualized self-presentation, suggestibility (under manipulation), shallow emotional expression in some registers. But HPD is organized around *being seen emotionally* — being the most feeling person in the room. Samson is organized around being the most *capable* and *exceptional* one. His emotional displays are controlled and instrumental; he does not lose composure for affect. The core fantasy is superiority, not emotional centrality. NPD captures him better. HPD features may be added as a trait note but do not warrant a separate axis-II.

### 6.4 Factitious Disorder Imposed on Another (Banner) — Ruled out.
Tempting framing: he keeps "needing" Banner to be sick so that he can be the one to treat him. But FDIA requires *induction* of illness in the other. Samson does not induce Banner's pathology; Banner had it before he arrived and would have it without him. What Samson does is something different and arguably more interesting — he *fails to disengage* from a case that has become identity-organizing for him. That is a boundary failure and a countertransference disaster, not FDIA. Document under NPD; do not separately code.

### 6.5 Erotomanic Delusional Disorder (re: Betty Ross) — Ruled out.
The Betty pursuit superficially resembles erotomania. But erotomania requires a *delusional* belief that the love object reciprocates, held with fixed psychotic conviction. Samson's belief is closer to a *narcissistic over-reading* of ambiguous signals plus a refusal to revise — he knows Betty is married, he knows she has declined him, he simply reorganizes those facts within a longer-arc fantasy in which he is eventually correct. This is character pathology, not delusion. Reality-testing is preserved.

### 6.6 Substance-Induced Personality Change — Ruled out as primary.
The personality structure predates the alcohol; the alcohol amplified and disinhibited but did not author. Era 1 Samson, sober, was already recognizably the man.

### 6.7 Iatrogenic Personality Change from Gamma Mutagenesis — Considered, partially endorsed.
There is a real question whether gamma exposure mutagenically affects affect regulation. The Banner case is the cautionary example. For Samson, the answer appears to be: gamma did not change his personality structure but *enabled its expression*. The grandiosity had nowhere to go in a baseline body; the body became congruent with the self-concept, which is a different and less stabilizing development than it sounds. The *Fall of the Hulks* episode raises the possibility of gamma-induced disinhibition under specific neurological tampering, but that is a discrete event, not a chronic process.

### 6.8 Acquired Savior Syndrome / "Rescuer" Personality — Subsumed.
Not a formal diagnosis. The rescuer pattern is real but is a *behavioral expression* of NPD's need for admiration and superiority, organized around the helping-professional role. Code under NPD.

### 6.9 Major Depressive Disorder, recurrent — Considered, rejected as primary.
The depressive episodes are reactive and remit with restoration of narcissistic supplies. They do not have the autonomous course, neurovegetative completeness, or treatment-response profile of MDD. The dysthymic floor (see 2.3) is the better characterization.

### 6.10 Adjustment Disorder, chronic — Ruled out.
His difficulties are not the response of a previously well-adjusted person to identifiable stressors; they are the lifelong pattern of a man whose architecture is the problem. AD does not capture forty years.

### 6.11 Obsessive-Compulsive Personality Disorder — Trait features only.
He has OCPD-flavored traits: orderliness, conscientiousness in his actual clinical craft, perfectionism about the work. But the warmth, the sexuality, the flexibility under positive feedback, and the willingness to break rules for grandiose ends all contraindicate OCPD as primary. Note as trait coloration; do not code.

### 6.12 Autism Spectrum / social-cognitive atypicality — Ruled out.
He is a fluent social reader. His blind spots are *motivated*, not constitutional. The distinction matters: he sees other people accurately when seeing them accurately does not threaten his self-concept.

---

## 7. Integrated Formulation

Leonard Samson is a high-functioning narcissistic man whose pathology has, across his life, alternated between being his greatest professional engine and his most reliable source of harm — to patients, to a woman he claimed to love, and ultimately to himself. He was named into a script he never examined, built a body and a vocation that confirmed the script, and then, when the script's contradictions became too large to outrun (a patient who exceeded him, a woman who did not choose him, an age at which the body would no longer carry the brand), he reached for alcohol to manage the gap, for further enhancement to close it, and for ethically compromised contracts to defer the reckoning. The reckoning arrived anyway, in the most public possible form, and to his considerable credit, he survived it without organizing his subsequent life around denying it.

The late-era presentation — quieter, more careful, less theatrical, professionally narrower, personally more truthful — is the closest thing the file contains to a treatment outcome. He appears to be, for the first time in his recorded life, doing the work he spent forty years prescribing to others. Prognosis, conditional on continued sobriety and on his not being recruited back into the kind of compromised institutional position that destroyed his last decade of full functioning: cautiously favorable.

He will, however, remain Doc Samson. The hair will stay green. The man who needed to be seen has not been replaced; he has merely, at long last, learned to keep an eye on himself.

— UATU, file open, monitoring continues.


## Behavioral Atlas

# UATU INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER — LEONARD SAMSON, Ph.D.
## SECTION VII: BEHAVIORAL ATLAS

A longitudinal catalogue of micro-patterns observable across approximately fifty published years of surveillance. Each behavior is cross-referenced to a state. The subject is unusual in that the *texture* of his tells is remarkably stable across eras; what changes is their frequency, their failure modes, and the substances available to mask them. The Era 1 Samson and the Era 4 Samson have the same hands. They no longer do the same things with them.

---

### 1. BASELINE / CALM STATE

When unobserved-but-on (his default in any clinical setting, base cafeteria, debrief, or hallway encounter), the subject presents a curated, high-functioning *clinician-at-rest* persona.

**Postural baseline.** Weight habitually carried on the back foot — a decathlete's stance, body coiled rather than settled. He does not slump even when alone in his office (observed across Mantlo and David runs in panels where no one is in-scene with him); when he sits, he sits forward, elbows on knees or forearms on desk, never against the chair back for longer than a minute or two. The body is *displayed* even in rest. This is the somatic signature of a man who was an athlete before he was a doctor and a doctor before he was a costume: the body is the resume and is never fully off-duty.

**Hand habits.** Touches his hair. Constantly. Pushes it back from the temple with the flat of the right palm; runs fingers through it during pauses in conversation; tucks the longer strands behind the ear when listening. After Era 1 the gesture acquires a second function — confirmation that the hair, his power, is *still there*. It is a tic with a load-bearing wall behind it. When his hair has been recently cut or lost, the hand still rises and then arrests mid-motion, a phantom gesture documented in numerous post-depowering scenes.

**Speech baseline.** Mid-register, unhurried, faintly performative. Tends to begin sentences with a soft consonant or an interjection ("Now —", "Look —", "Y'see —") that buys him a quarter-second of phrasing time. Uses the patient's first name early and often; uses his own credentials rarely in direct speech but ensures they appear on signage, letterhead, doorplates. He does not need to *say* "doctor"; he needs the room to.

**Eye contact.** Steady, warm, slightly over-long by clinical convention — by about one beat. This is his single most effective interpersonal tool and he knows it. He uses it identically on patients, women he is pursuing, suspects in custody, and superiors he is buttering. The lack of differentiation is itself a tell.

**Default movement through space.** Enters rooms by the long diagonal, never the short one. Will cross a chamber to greet someone rather than wait. Stands when others enter. Positions himself within sightlines of mirrors, windows, polished surfaces — not consciously preening, but ambient self-reference. In the Gamma Base era he could be reliably located by walking toward the largest reflective surface in the facility.

**Reading habits.** Carries a journal or monograph almost always; reads in transit, in waiting rooms, between sessions. The reading is real (his clinical fluency requires it) and also a prop — the open page is a *do-not-disturb* sign and a credential simultaneously. Annotates margins in dense pencil; underlines in a single confident stroke, never the hatched line of an uncertain reader.

**Eating.** Athlete's appetite, athlete's discipline. Eats fast, eats a lot, eats clean by the standards of his era. Coffee black, refilled three times in a session. After Era 2, the coffee acquires a sidecar.

---

### 2. CLINICAL / WORKING STATE

This is the subject at his most genuinely competent and the state in which his pathology is most effectively *channeled* rather than *expressed*.

**The opening move.** With any new patient, Samson performs a near-invariant choreography in the first ninety seconds: (1) stands as the patient enters, (2) crosses to meet rather than greet from his chair, (3) handshake with left hand briefly touching the patient's elbow or upper arm, (4) seats the patient before seating himself, (5) offers water unprompted, (6) opens with an observation about the patient — never about the file. The observation is calibrated to demonstrate attention without intrusion ("Long drive in?" / "That's a Quantico pin, isn't it?"). It works. It is also rehearsed. He does it with Banner, with Betty, with line soldiers, with the President's emissary, and with the Leader.

**Listening posture.** Forward lean, chin in the web of the right hand, index finger along the cheekbone — the textbook *attentive-clinician* pose, deployed with full consciousness of its semiotic load. He holds the pose past comfort, into theater. When genuinely surprised by what a patient says, the pose breaks: he sits back, both hands flat on the desk. That break is the most reliable indicator that something has actually landed.

**Note-taking.** Sparse on paper, dense in memory. Will write three or four words per session — anchors, not transcripts. He distrusts the audio recorder (a holdover from earlier Gamma Base protocols where his notes were SHIELD property) and prefers to dictate summary memoranda after the patient leaves, alone, walking the corridor or his office perimeter.

**Hypnotic / regression work.** His finest professional craft. Voice drops half an octave, tempo halves, sentence length shortens, hand gestures stop entirely. He becomes physically smaller in the chair. The vanity *turns off*. This is the only state in which the subject is observably unconcerned with how he appears, and the case files reflect it: the Merged Hulk integration was done by a man who, for the duration of those sessions, was not watching himself in the window.

**Documentation hygiene.** Excellent on cases, terrible on himself. He keeps no personal journal of significance, no self-supervision log, has never been observed in regular peer consultation in the canonical record. He is the case-formulator who has never been formulated. This is structural, not accidental.

---

### 3. MILD STRESS / SOCIAL PRESSURE

Triggers: being introduced after a more senior figure; a patient referencing another therapist favorably; Banner in the room; Betty in the room with someone else; a junior officer addressing him without rank.

**Verbal escalation, tier one.** Jargon density rises. He begins using clinical terminology with people who do not require it — orderlies, Army majors, journalists. Sentences lengthen. Subordinate clauses proliferate. He starts saying "in a real sense" and "what we'd call, technically —" as throat-clearings.

**Physical compensation.** The hair-touch becomes a hair-*sweep* — full hand, back to nape, held for a beat. Shoulders square slightly. The decathlete reasserts under the doctor. If standing, he will subtly find higher ground — the step, the dais, the side of the room with the taller ceiling.

**Humor under pressure.** Quips arrive. They are not self-deflating; they redirect attention to his fluency rather than his vulnerability. He laughs at his own jokes one beat before others do — a confidence display that, on close reading, is anxiety.

**The reframe move.** When professionally challenged, he reliably attempts a reframe that converts the challenge into a *case* — i.e., positions the challenger as someone whose objection is worth analyzing rather than answering. This is brilliant when used on adversaries and noxious when used on colleagues. He cannot tell the difference in the moment.

---

### 4. ACUTE STRESS / THREAT / COMBAT

The escalation ladder articulated in the psychiatric workup is observable as discrete behavioral phases.

**Phase 1 — Verbal saturation.** Talks more, faster, with more references. Will narrate the tactical situation aloud as if presenting at rounds. In conflicts with Banner specifically, lapses into second-person address ("Bruce, you don't want this, you and I both know what's happening here —") that is half de-escalation, half performance for any observers.

**Phase 2 — Self-deployment.** The hinge moment. Samson stops consulting and starts *intervening*. He removes his jacket — invariably, across decades, the jacket comes off and is folded, never dropped. The folding is a tell: even in transition to violence he is curating. After the jacket: a half-step forward, hands open and low, palms slightly cupped — a wrestler's ready stance, not a boxer's. Decathlete musculature reads through the shirt and he knows it.

**Phase 3 — Engagement.** In combat he favors grapples, throws, and pinning maneuvers over strikes. This is consistent across forty years and is *clinically* revealing: he prefers to *contain* rather than to *damage*. He talks during fights — to opponents, to bystanders, to himself. The talking is not strategic; it is the same intellectualization defense operating under load. He has been struck mid-monologue more times than is dignified.

**Phase 4 — Power-seeking.** Following any combat in which he was outclassed or sidelined, expect within days to weeks: pursuit of re-irradiation, new contract, new alliance, new equipment, new title. The behavioral cycle is unmistakable and identical in shape to substance relapse — diminishment, craving, acquisition, brief euphoria, return to baseline.

**Tells of fear (rare, suppressed).** Jaw tension at the masseter, visible. A single hard swallow before action. The hand goes to the hair and does not complete the gesture — arrests at the temple. After the danger passes, an exhalation through pursed lips that he covers with a quip.

---

### 5. INTIMACY / EROTIC PURSUIT

Behavior in this domain is the most diagnostically loud and the least modulated by experience.

**Approach.** Identical opening to clinical approach — the crossed room, the elbow-touched handshake, the calibrated observation. He does not differentiate his social register for sexual contexts. The bedside manner *is* the seduction manner, which is part of why patients have repeatedly experienced his attention as romantic when it was not (or was, ambiguously) and part of why Betty Ross has repeatedly experienced his attention as clinical when it absolutely was not.

**The Betty pattern.** Across five decades: pursuit does not modulate to feedback. The behavioral signature: appears at significant moments (her wedding, her hospitalization, her crises with Banner) under professional pretext; provides genuinely useful service; lingers past the professional warrant; makes a small, deniable gesture — a hand on the shoulder held a beat long, a remembered detail from years prior, a self-disclosure about loneliness framed as collegial confidence; observes her response; if rebuffed, executes a graceful retreat that preserves access for the next cycle. This is not the behavior of a man hoping; it is the behavior of a man maintaining a position.

**Tells of genuine arousal versus performed warmth.** With most people the warmth is performed and indistinguishable from genuine. With Betty specifically, the tells leak: he loses the quip, the verbosity drops rather than rises, he becomes briefly *quiet* — and that silence, in him, is the loudest indicator in the file.

**Post-rejection behavior.** Withdraws into work for 48–72 hours. Drinks. Re-emerges with a new clinical project, a new media appearance, or a new physical augmentation. Never processes the rejection verbally with anyone, ever, on-record.

---

### 6. GRIEF / LOSS

Subject's grief behavior is constrained by his defenses to the point of being almost invisible to casual observation.

**Loss of power (post-haircut, post-depowering events).** Withdrawal. Cancels appointments citing "administrative obligations." Stays in his quarters or office. Reading volume goes up; output goes down. Depressive affect bleeds through as *flatness* rather than sadness — the calibrated warmth becomes mechanical, the eye contact shortens, the patient's-first-name habit lapses. Lasts days to weeks. Resolved invariably by re-acquisition rather than by processing.

**Loss of person (patients lost, colleagues killed, Betty's various deaths and transformations).** Performs the ritual correctly — present at services, speaks well, comforts others. The grief itself is metabolized through *case-formulation of the deceased*: he produces, in the days following any significant death, a written or spoken analysis of the person, often quite penetrating, that functions as eulogy and as containment. He grieves by *understanding*. Whether anything emotional is actually processed beneath the formulation is unclear and probably unclear to him.

**Loss of self (post–*Fall of the Hulks*, post-resurrection, late-era).** The only loss he has been observed to grieve *as loss*, without immediate compensation. The chastened Era 4 demeanor — quieter speech, dropped jargon density, sustained eye-contact-with-self in the form of actually looking at his own reflection rather than glancing past it — reads as the long-delayed grief for the man he was before he started compensating. This is the most psychologically alive he has ever been on the record.

---

### 7. VICTORY / SUCCESS

**Immediate post-victory tells.** Two-handed sweep through the hair. A specific, near-involuntary half-smile aimed at the nearest reflective surface or, lacking one, the nearest woman. A verbal downplay ("Anyone would've —") that invites correction. Seeks out Betty, or Banner, or a superior — someone whose witnessing of the victory will validate it. Solo victories that no one witnessed appear to bring him minimal satisfaction; he will narrate them to a third party within hours.

**Tells of genuine professional pride (rare and distinct).** When a case goes well — particularly during the Merged Hulk arc — the behavior inverts. He becomes *more* quiet, not less. Does not seek witnesses. Sits in his office afterward with the door closed. Writes longer notes than usual. This is the man underneath the cape, and he surfaces only when the work has been large enough to organize him.

**Press behavior.** Polished, quotable, photogenic. Knows his angles. Gives credit fluently and falsely — the credit-giving is technique, not modesty. The journalists who have covered him repeatedly come away with the same three or four anecdotes, which suggests he curates his self-presentation tightly.

---

### 8. DEFEAT / HUMILIATION

**Immediate.** Jaw tension. The arrested hair-gesture. A single, short exhalation. Then — invariably — a verbal recovery: a sentence that reframes the defeat as instructive, provisional, or external. He has never, on record, said simply "I lost" and stopped there.

**Hours-to-days following.** Isolation. Drinking, post-Era 2. Avoidance of the specific peer who witnessed the defeat. Reappearance with a *plan* — a new approach, a new alliance, a new physical preparation. The plan is the antidote to having been small.

**Long-term integration of defeat.** Poor through Era 3; visible in Era 4. The *Fall of the Hulks* catastrophe forced an integration he had spent forty years avoiding, and the late-era behavior shows him capable, finally, of carrying a defeat without immediately metabolizing it into a new compensation.

---

### 9. DECEPTION / WHEN LYING

He lies well, by clinical instinct, but with a consistent tell-set.

**To others.** Maintains the over-long eye contact (most liars break it; he holds it harder). The hand stills — the hair-touch tic suppresses entirely, which is itself the tell to a trained observer. Sentences shorten and become declarative. Jargon drops. He becomes, briefly, *plainer* than baseline. The plainness is the lie's signature.

**To himself.** Continuous, automatic, and the central pathology. The self-lies are dressed in formulation: every ethically dubious act has a clinical rationale articulated in the moment, in good faith, with internal coherence. The rationalizations are not retrospective; they are *simultaneous*. He believes them as he generates them. This is why he is hard to confront — there is no liar to catch, only a system that produces sincere falsities at the speed of cognition.

---

### 10. INTOXICATION (Era 2 late through Era 3)

Tolerance: high, athlete's metabolism, gamma-enhanced. Behaviorally, he holds liquor better than most observers realize, which is part of why the use went unchallenged for so long.

**Early-glass behavior.** Indistinguishable from baseline to all but the closest observers. Slight increase in eye-contact duration, slight loosening of the shoulder line.

**Mid-intoxication.** Verbal warmth becomes verbal *flirtation* across categories — with patients, with reporters, with hostile foreign psychiatrists at conferences. The boundary-maintenance that distinguishes his professional warmth from his romantic warmth collapses by perhaps fifteen percent. To most people, undetectable. To Betty, to Banner, and to anyone who has known him sober, immediately legible.

**Late-intoxication.** Rare in public. Self-pity emerges — grievances about credit, about Banner, about being misunderstood. The intellectualization defense weakens and what is underneath is small and aggrieved. Witnessed by very few, almost all of whom were managed afterward.

**Morning-after.** Iron discipline. Showers, shaves, dresses sharper than usual. Coffee black, three cups. Arrives early. Performs the day at one hundred and ten percent of normal output. The over-performance is itself the tell.

---

### 11. ROUTES, RITUALS, AND HABITS

**Daily.** Wakes early (5:00–5:30 across all eras). Runs — long distances, alone, same route variant each posting, modifies the route only when ambushed on it. Shaves with a straight razor through Era 2; switches to safety razor after a hand tremor incident never publicly acknowledged. Reads two newspapers and at least one journal before any patient contact. Coffee in his own mug, never the institutional kind.

**Weekly.** A long walk on Sundays regardless of weather. Returns through a specific approach to whatever building he is housed in — never the front entrance if a side entrance exists. Likely a holdover from a specific Gamma Base–era ambush.

**Wardrobe.** Off-duty: dark slacks, open-collar shirts, no tie unless required, jackets cut close to the shoulder to display the physique. The aesthetic has not changed materially in forty years; it has only become more expensive. On-duty (costume): the bandolier is functional pretense — it carries little — but the visual is non-negotiable. He has rejected redesigns that would have covered more skin.

**Office space.** Diplomas displayed but not crowded. Photographs few; no family. A photograph of himself at a decathlon event has been observed on his desk in multiple eras — the only personal image he reliably exhibits. This is not an oversight.

**Vehicles.** Drives himself when possible. Prefers manual transmission through Era 2. Drives fast but cleanly. Will not be chauffeured if avoidable; the back seat is a status loss.

**Sleep.** Six hours, consistent, with insomnia spikes following narcissistic injury or romantic setback. Has been observed reading in the small hours during such spikes; has been observed drinking during them post–Era 2.

---

### 12. CROSS-ERA DRIFT SUMMARY

The behavioral *vocabulary* is stable across the full record. What drifts is the *modulation*.

- **Era 1:** Tells are loud, ungoverned, slightly adolescent. The hair-sweep is a flourish. The clinical jargon is showing off. The pursuit of Betty is naked.
- **Era 2:** Tells are governed and channeled. The same gestures, performed by a man at the height of his powers, read as mastery rather than need. The Merged Hulk work shows the gestures at minimum amplitude and maximum effect.
- **Era 3:** Tells decompensate. The jargon thickens past usefulness; the hair-sweep becomes compulsive; the jacket-folding before combat takes a beat too long; the drinking softens the edges and sharpens the grievances. The vocabulary is the same; the speaker is breaking down.
- **Era 4:** Tells *quiet*. The hand still rises to the hair and often stops short — not phantom-gesture-of-loss now but conscious interruption of the tic. Eye contact shortens to clinically normal duration. Jargon density drops. The mirror-glance habit attenuates. The man underneath has, at long last, become visible to himself, and the behavioral atlas registers it not as new behaviors but as *old behaviors performed with awareness*.

That last is the most important entry in this file. The subject did not change his repertoire. He learned, finally, to watch it.


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER — LEONARD SAMSON, Ph.D.
## Section: Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

*What a week of continuous surveillance — physical tail, room-bug, calendar pull, credit-card spool, gym keycard log, pharmacy refill history, liquor-store CCTV, jogging-app heatmap, hospital badge swipes — would actually record across a representative seven days, cross-referenced against forty years of behavioral consistency. Era-flagged where the pattern shifts.*

---

### 1. The Shape of a Day (Steady-State, Era 2 baseline; deviations noted)

Samson is a morning person whose mornings have a defended quality. He wakes between 0510 and 0540 without an alarm — a holdover from decathlon training that has survived every other discipline he has lost. The first thing he does is not check his phone, which is unusual for a man whose self-image depends so heavily on being addressed; he goes to the bathroom mirror and *looks at himself*. This is observable through any reflective surface in the bathroom and has been consistent across decades of domestic settings. He does not preen, exactly. He inventories: hairline, jaw, neck, shoulders. The inspection takes 30–90 seconds. He has done it since before the gamma and it intensified after.

Then water — a full glass, room temperature, drunk standing at the sink. Then, in eras when he is training, a 6–9 mile run, paced conservatively the first mile and then opened up; in eras when he is not, a perfunctory floor routine (push-ups, an old decathlete's hurdler stretch sequence, isometric holds) that he completes with visible irritation at himself for completing it instead of running. He returns, showers long and hot, and shaves with a safety razor — a deliberate, slow shave; a man who has been on magazine covers and remembers it.

Breakfast is the same six things in rotation: oatmeal with banana; two eggs and dry toast; Greek yogurt with honey; a protein shake on rushed days; black coffee always, twice. He does not cook with affection. The kitchen of a man who eats to refuel an instrument.

He leaves for the office or base between 0700 and 0745. Drive time is used for podcasts in later eras (clinical podcasts, sports radio, never music) and was used for cassettes of his own dictated case notes in the 80s, which is a tic worth flagging: *he listens to his own voice, reviewing his own thinking, on the way to work.*

---

### 2. Workday — Clinical Variant

When Samson is in a true clinical posture (Era 2, intervals of Era 4), the day has the architecture of a serious psychiatrist's day, with idiosyncrasies.

- **0800–0830:** Chart review and supervision intake. He writes notes by hand first, transcribes later — a vanity disguised as a method. His handwriting is fast, slanting, and legible; he prides himself on it.
- **0830–1200:** Patient hours, typically four 50-minute sessions back-to-back with ten-minute gaps he uses for one of three things: pacing the corridor, a phone call to whatever woman he is currently failing to win, or a brief intense conversation with a colleague that he conducts standing in their doorway so he can leave on his own beat. He does not eat in this window. He drinks water from a heavy glass tumbler he refills himself, never a bottle — the glass is a status object even when no one is looking.
- **1200–1300:** Lunch. This is the most diagnostic hour of his day. If he eats with peers (rare), he holds court. If he eats with a junior (more common), he mentors warmly and at length and the junior leaves feeling chosen. If he eats alone (most common), he eats fast at his desk while reading — a salad, a sandwich, something pre-assembled — and uses the rest of the hour to call back press, agents, the Avengers liaison's office in eras when that line existed, or Betty's voicemail in eras when he was still doing that.
- **1300–1700:** Either more patient hours or, more often, the "consulting" portion of his work — depositions, expert witness prep, government contracts, case conferences on Banner or other gamma cases, occasional teaching. He is over-scheduled by design. The calendar is a defense against unstructured time.
- **1700–1830:** Gym. Non-negotiable across all eras except active recovery from injury and brief depowered depressive intervals. He prefers an empty gym and will shift his hour earlier or later to find one. He does compound lifts heavy, with theatrical exhalations; he checks himself in the mirror between sets — again, inventorying, not preening. He is one of the few patrons who actually re-racks plates, a fact the gym staff have noticed.

A continuous-surveillance log over a clinical week would show: ~22 billable clinical hours, ~14 hours of consulting/admin, ~7 hours of training, ~50 hours sleep, and roughly 9–11 hours unaccounted for, scattered in 20–90 minute pockets. Those pockets are the file's interesting hours.

---

### 3. Workday — Operational Variant

When Samson is deployed — and across his career he has been deployed far more than a psychiatrist should be — the architecture inverts. Operational Samson keeps the morning ritual intact (the mirror, the water, the shave when possible) and then runs hot all day. He sleeps less, eats worse, drinks more coffee, and talks faster. The clinical jargon thickens under stress in a documentable way: a sentence-length analysis of his dialogue across crisis arcs vs. baseline interviews would show a measurable increase in nominalizations and Latinate verbs in the 72 hours preceding a fight. He is *talking himself into the room*.

In operational mode he also acquires a small, consistent kit: a duffel with two changes of clothes (one civilian, one tactical), a Dopp kit with the safety razor, a paperback (always nonfiction, usually history or neuroscience, rarely finished), a notebook, and — Era 3 specifically — a flask. The flask is leather-wrapped, monogrammed, and was a gift; he does not buy his own drinking vessels, an interesting detail.

---

### 4. Evenings, Downtime & The Pocket Hours

Evenings are where the difference between the public clinician and the private man is most visible.

**Era 1–2 evening (the good years):** Home by 1900–2000. Dinner is either takeout (Thai, Italian, sushi — he rotates) or a meal someone else is providing in a social context. He reads, watches sports (boxing, MMA, track and field — combat and his old sport), and writes — articles, book drafts, case notes. He keeps a journal intermittently; the journal is observable because he writes in it at the kitchen counter, in public, with a fountain pen, in a way that says *I am a man who keeps a journal.* He sleeps 2230–2300, generally alone.

**Era 3 evening (the bad years):** Home later, 2030–2200. The first drink happens earlier in the evening across the period — a continuous-surveillance file would show the bourbon pour migrating from "after dinner" to "during dinner" to "instead of dinner" over roughly thirty months. The lights stay on later. The TV stays on as company. He sleeps in his clothes more often than a man his age should.
