There are nights he doesn't go home at all and the file would record hotel charges in his own city, a tell that does not require interpretation.

**Era 4 evening (the chastened years):** A reconstructed sobriety routine that is visibly effortful. AA-coded behaviors without confirmed AA attendance — a sponsor's number in his contacts under initials, a chip he handles when stressed, periods of conspicuous abstinence at events. Evenings now contain a long phone call (always the same number, never the same content), a half-hour of reading in a chair, and an early bed. He has gotten quieter. The TV is off more often than on.

**The pocket hours** — the unaccounted 9–11 hours a week — across all eras are spent in three ways: (1) **driving**, often without a destination, particularly when a case is breaking open or a relationship is closing; (2) **at the gym a second time**, late, when he cannot sleep; (3) **at Betty-adjacent locations** in eras when that surveillance line was warm — drives past her last known address, lunch at restaurants she frequented, "happening to be" at hospitals where Banner was a patient. This last pattern is the single most consistent behavioral signature in his life and the one he would most strenuously deny under direct questioning.

---

### 5. Habits of Place

Samson is a creature of *spatial repetition*. He uses the same three coffee shops near any workplace, in strict rotation. He sits with his back to a wall when possible and facing the door always — a habit from operational life that survived into civilian life and reads, to a trained observer, as exactly what it is. He tips well in cash. Staff at his regular places know him by name and order; he knows theirs back, and remembers details (a child's name, a finished degree) across visits — this is partly genuine warmth and partly a clinician's reflex toward rapport, and the two are not separable in him.

His office, across every era and institution, contains the same objects: a heavy desk (he refuses laminate); a leather chair he sits in and a leather chair patients sit in, the patient's chair slightly lower; framed diplomas hung at eye level for a seated patient, not for him; a single photograph of himself in competition, framed but placed where only he can see it from his desk chair; books shelved by topic and then by author, with the spines aligned forward — not flush with the shelf edge but a uniform half-inch back, a tic that maintenance staff have learned not to correct. A bottle of good bourbon in a desk drawer across Era 3, replaced by a bottle of mineral water across Era 4. A framed thank-you note from a non-famous patient, kept where he can see it, which is the most honest object in the room.

His apartments and houses across the decades have been *underfurnished for the square footage*. He buys big spaces and fills them late or not at all. The bedroom is monastic. The kitchen is well-equipped but lightly used. The bathroom mirror is oversized in every domicile on record. There is always a heavy bag somewhere — garage, basement, spare room — even in eras he is not using it.

---

### 6. Habits of Time

He is **on time**, aggressively. Five minutes early to everything, ten to anything that matters. Lateness in others he tolerates poorly and notes; he does not say anything but a continuous file would catch the micro-expression. He runs his sessions to the minute and ends them with a verbal cue he has used for decades ("Let's leave it there for today") — a small ritual that patients have remarked on.

He **avoids weekends as unstructured time**. Saturdays are gym, a long run, errands, and a social obligation he half-resents and half-needs (a fundraiser, a colleague's dinner, a lecture he is giving). Sundays are the most dangerous day in his week across all eras — the day he most often drank in Era 3, the day he most often drives without destination in Era 4, the day his Betty-adjacent surveillance pattern peaks across the entire record. An unstructured Sunday afternoon is where the man without a case to organize him goes looking for one.

He sleeps **5.5–6.5 hours** on workdays and pays for it on weekends with a single long sleep he resents needing.

---

### 7. The Body as Routine

The physical maintenance is its own daily liturgy and deserves its own paragraph. Beyond the morning inspection and the evening gym, there are: the **hair**, which he washes daily and which he has — observably — a barber for, on an every-three-weeks schedule, who knows not to take too much; the **skin**, which he protects (sunblock, a moisturizer, observable on the bathroom counter); the **posture**, which is *cultivated* — he does not slouch even when alone, a thing very few people manage; the **gait**, long-strided and slightly weight-forward, an athlete's walk that he has not let degrade. He stands when others sit. He sits when others stand. He uses height and frame as conversational instruments and is not unaware of doing it.

He carries minor old-athlete maintenance into the day: a knee that he rolls out in the morning, a shoulder he stretches in doorways, a habit of cracking his neck once, sharply, before a difficult conversation — a tell a trained interrogator would learn to read inside an hour.

---

### 8. Consumption, Acquisition & Money

A credit-card spool across a month would show: large grocery runs (single-man volumes, protein-heavy), frequent restaurant charges at the same six or eight establishments, gym dues, bookstore charges (he buys physical books, often more than he reads), occasional bespoke purchases (a good shirt, a good pen, a watch repair), professional society dues, conference travel, and — Era 3 — liquor-store charges at *three different stores in rotation*, which is the classic distribution pattern of a drinker who has noticed himself. Era 4 those charges vanish and are replaced by a flat monthly transfer to a recipient the file would, with work, identify as a sponsor or a treatment program.

He tips well. He pays his taxes early. His credit is excellent. He is generous in small public ways and tight in large private ones (his charitable giving is lower than his income would predict; the giving he does is to causes that involve his name on a wall).

---

### 9. Communications Rhythm

Phone use: heavy but patterned. He returns calls in batches twice a day (lunch and post-gym). He prefers voice to text and will call back rather than reply. He uses email like a professional of his generation — efficient, slightly formal, signed with credentials. He has, across every era, a small number of people he calls *unscheduled* — a sponsor in Era 4, a particular colleague across all eras, and Betty's number, which he has dialed and hung up on more times than any file could fully enumerate. The hang-ups are the data.

In public he is a fluent small-talker; in private, on the phone, he is *quieter than people expect*. The performance has an off-switch he uses when no one is watching.

---

### 10. What A Week of Surveillance Would Conclude

That the subject is a disciplined, high-functioning professional whose life is organized around a small number of fixed rituals (the morning mirror, the gym, the structured workday, the rotation of three coffee shops, the heavy desk and aligned spines, the hair) and a smaller number of unacknowledged ones (the Betty-adjacent drift, the second late-night gym session, the Sunday drives, the inventory in any reflective surface). That the public schedule is dense by design and that the private hours are where the pathology lives. That the rituals have a *protective* function — they hold him together — and that the moments his rituals break (a missed gym day, a deviation from the coffee rotation, an early drink) are leading indicators of trouble far more reliable than anything he would say in a clinical interview.

That the file's most useful real-time alarm would be a single composite metric: **rituals intact + Sunday accounted for + no liquor-store charges + gym attendance ≥ 5/week = stable.** Any two of those breaking in the same week predicts a bad month. Three predicts an arc.

He has, in his lifetime, lived weeks of all four conditions and weeks of none. The file knows the difference even when he does not.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# RELATIONSHIPS I — FAMILY & ORIGIN BONDS

## Prefatory Note on the Silence

The most striking feature of Leonard Samson's family record is its near-total absence from the canonical material. Across fifty years of published appearances — through Thomas, Englehart, Wein, Mantlo, the long Peter David tenure, Jenkins, Casey, Pak, Parker, and Ewing — Samson has no on-page parents, no siblings, no children, no aunts or cousins, no flashbacks to a childhood bedroom, no graveside scenes, no holidays, no inherited objects, no anecdotal "my mother used to say." For a character whose entire professional identity is built on excavating the family-of-origin material of others — most famously Bruce Banner's, where he correctly and with sustained competence identified Brian Banner's abuse as the etiological core of the dissociative structure — this silence is not incidental. It is the single most diagnostic fact about him.

In a universe whose narrative grammar runs almost entirely on origin flashbacks, where every recurring character eventually gets the issue that opens on a childhood kitchen, Samson has not received that issue and, more tellingly, has never narrated it himself in dialogue or in caption. His own internal monologues — and Peter David gave him many — touch on Banner's parents, on Betty's father, on the Leader's brother, on his own academic mentors, but never on Samson's. He has used the word "father" professionally hundreds of times and personally, on the page, essentially never.

A surveillance file must therefore work the way the FBI worked Malcolm Little before he was Malcolm X: by triangulating absence. What follows is reconstruction from what the man does, what he avoids, what he says when he means something else, and what he became.

---

## 1. THE FATHER (Unnamed, Presumed Deceased or Estranged)

### History

No name on record. No occupation on record. No image, photograph, or graveside reference in any canonical appearance. What can be asserted with high confidence is that someone — and given naming conventions across the relevant cohort, almost certainly a father or a father-surrogate of high authority within the household — affixed the name **Samson** to him before he was old enough to refuse it. The surname itself is patrilineal in the conventional sense, but it is the **given name "Leonard"** in combination with the surname **Samson** that produces the loaded signal: *Leonard* (lion-strong, lion-hearted) bracketing *Samson* (the Biblical strongman whose power resided in his hair, lost it to a woman, was blinded, and pulled the temple down on himself and his enemies). The composite is not an accident. Two strength-tropes stacked, one Germanic-chivalric and one Hebraic-mythic, with the Samson half loaded with a specifically tragic theology of strength-undone-by-intimacy.

A parent who selects that compound for a male child is **broadcasting an expectation** before the child has a phenotype. This is the foundational fact of Leonard Samson's psychic life.

### Dynamics (Inferred)

The adult behavioral product — Olympic-level decathlete by his twenties, doctorate in psychiatry shortly after, costumed strongman by his late twenties — is the behavioral fingerprint of a child raised under what clinicians call **conditional regard**: love and attention available in proportion to performance, withheld in proportion to ordinariness. The decathlon is the diagnostic event. It is the multi-event sport, the sport of generalists who must be excellent at ten things. Children do not gravitate to the decathlon; they are *built* into it, usually by a parent who is themselves a frustrated athlete or a frustrated polymath. That he then abandoned the somatic track for the most prestige-laden of the helping professions — psychiatry, not psychology, not social work — and then abandoned the consulting room for the cape, suggests a child who learned that **no single achievement secures the regard**, that the bar moves, and that the survival strategy is to keep producing escalating proofs.

The father (or father-figure) was, by inference, **intellectually demanding, athletically invested, and emotionally withholding** — the classic structure that produces high-functioning narcissistic adaptation in a child of real talent. Not abusive in the Brian Banner sense; if there had been overt abuse, Samson — who reads abuse fluently in others — would have either recognized and integrated it or, more likely given his defenses, sealed it behind a far more visible wall of avoidance than the smooth silence he actually maintains. The silence reads instead as the silence of a child who was *given everything that could be measured and nothing that couldn't*, and who experiences the absence of grievance as itself ungrievable. There is nothing to complain about. That is the complaint.

### Evolution

In Era 1 (the 1970s), Samson speaks of his credentials with a frequency and pride that suggest a recent audience — someone whose approval is still being sought, or whose approval was withdrawn so recently that the seeking has not yet adjusted. Through Era 2 (the David run), as Samson's clinical mastery actually catches up to his self-presentation, the credential-flashing decreases. By Era 3 (the decompensation), the drinking begins to function as a substitute for an internalized regulating presence that was never adequately installed — he is, behaviorally, looking for the off-switch that a securely attached child internalizes from a good-enough parent and finding only the bottle.

By Era 4 (Ewing-era chastening), Samson reads as a man who has, finally, in the absence of the original father, **become his own**. The sobriety, the quieter affect, the willingness to be a consulting presence rather than the largest object in the room — these are the markers of a man who has stopped seeking the approval and started administering it to himself.

### Trust / Safety

Untestable directly. The downstream proxy: Samson trusts male authority figures **structurally** (Thunderbolt Ross, the Army, SHIELD, the institutional apparatus around Gamma Base) more than the evidence warrants, and is repeatedly burned by that trust. The Leader's manipulation in *Fall of the Hulks* succeeds in part because Samson — who should know better, who has the diagnostic tools to see it — does not adequately interrogate male-coded authority that flatters him with importance. This is the residue of a father whose approval was the original currency.

### Failure Mode

The father is the source of the script Samson cannot revise: *be exceptional or be invisible*. The failure mode is the entire arc of decompensation in Era 3 — when exceptional becomes harder to sustain (Banner's care moves out of his hands, Betty marries and stays married, his standing in the metahuman-psychiatric field is challenged by younger and less encumbered clinicians), the script offers no third option between *exceptional* and *nothing*, and Samson, faced with nothing, reaches for the gamma, reaches for the bottle, reaches for the alliance with the Leader that promised to make him exceptional again.

### Leverage

For any actor seeking to move Samson: invoke the father-coded register. Frame a request as a test of whether he is up to it; frame a refusal as evidence that he never was. He will not recognize the manipulation in real time. The Leader used a version of this. So, less consciously, did Ross for thirty years. So, devastatingly, does Samson himself when he is alone with a mirror.

---

## 2. THE MOTHER (Unnamed, Status Unknown)

### History

If the father is a silence, the mother is a deeper silence. There is no canonical reference. None. Samson has not, in published material, said the word "mother" about his own mother. He has used it diagnostically about Banner's, about countless patients', about cultural archetypes. About his own: nothing.

### Dynamics (Inferred)

Two possibilities organize the inference, and they are not mutually exclusive.

**First**, the mother was a presence subordinated to the father's project — a woman who either co-signed the *be exceptional* script or who lacked standing within the household to interrupt it. In this configuration she would be the parent toward whom the child's unmet attachment needs were directed and frustrated. The downstream signature of that frustration is **the Betty Ross pattern**: forty years of pursuit of a woman who is not available, who has chosen another man (and not just any man — Banner, the patient, the rival, the structural double for the father-favored sibling Samson never had), and who Samson cannot stop pursuing because the pursuit is not actually about Betty. It is about a prior woman whose attention was always *almost* available, whose choosing of someone else over him is the original injury he is repeatedly restaging in the hope of a different outcome.

**Second**, the mother was absent — dead, departed, ill, withdrawn — early enough that the child organized around her absence as a constitutive fact rather than a grief. The clinical signature of this is the **overinvestment in healing women**: not just the romantic pursuit of Betty but the entire shape of Samson's clinical practice, which across the decades has skewed disproportionately toward female patients in distress (Betty herself, Jen Walters during her early She-Hulk integration work, various civilians and metahumans on the record), and toward a particular flavor of intervention — *I will be the one who finally sees you correctly* — that reads as reparative work directed at the wrong addressee.

The two possibilities converge on the same operational fact: **Samson does not have, and has never had, a stable internal representation of a securely loving female figure**. Every adult woman in his orbit is recruited, unconsciously, into either the role of the one who will finally provide it or the role of the one who will once again withhold it. Betty has been both, oscillating, for forty years.

### Evolution

Across Era 1-2, the mother-script runs hot under the Betty pursuit and is invisible to Samson. Across Era 3, as the Betty pursuit becomes untenable (her marriage stabilizes, his behavior becomes embarrassing even to him), the script displaces — into the drinking (a maternal substitute, oral, regulating, finally reliable in its non-rejection) and into the increasingly grandiose clinical postures that demand from the world the recognition the mother did not provide. Era 4 shows the beginnings of an internalized maternal function: self-soothing, self-permission to rest, the capacity to let a patient go without making the letting-go a performance.

### Trust / Safety

With women he is not pursuing erotically — older female colleagues, female patients above a certain age, female authority figures outside his romantic field — Samson is reliably warm, attentive, non-defensive, and easy in his body. With women inside his romantic field, every interaction is contaminated. He cannot tell the difference between care and pursuit; he routes one through the other.

### Failure Mode

The mother-shaped hole produces the **Betty pattern** in its entirety and the **drinking** in its later form. It is also the silent partner in every clinical decision Samson has made about a female patient, including some that have worked out well (his integration work with Jen Walters showed real restraint and skill) and some that have not (his treatment of Betty across the marriage years includes boundary violations that would, in any properly supervised practice, have ended his license).

### Leverage

A skilled operator working Samson would route requests through a female intermediary positioned as needing his help. He has, historically, been unable to refuse. The vulnerability is structural and persists into his current sobriety, though it has weakened.

---

## 3. SIBLINGS (None on Record)

### History

No siblings appear in the published material. The inference of only-child status is reasonable but not certain; it is possible there are siblings he simply does not speak of, which would itself be diagnostic in a different way.

### Dynamics

Functionally, Samson behaves as an only child of high-investment parents. The markers are consistent: comfort with adult attention from a young age (his ease with senior figures at Gamma Base in his earliest appearances, where he is the youngest person in the room and visibly enjoys it); discomfort with peer-level rivalry that is not also hierarchical (his relationship with Banner is rivalry he can metabolize *because* it is also structured by his role as the doctor); a tendency to recruit peer relationships into mentor/mentee shapes; and the specific brittleness around being **treated as one of several** rather than as the singular focus.

The Banner relationship — which will be treated in full in the next dossier section, as it is not a family bond but it shadows family bonds throughout — functions in Samson's psyche as the **sibling-rivalry he never had structurally and therefore cannot recognize when he is living it**. Banner is the *favored* one: he gets Betty, he gets the moral high ground, he gets the suffering that confers depth, he gets to be the patient (the child) while Samson must be the doctor (the parent), and Samson cannot stop competing with him for a prize that was never on offer.

### Failure Mode

The absence of sibling experience leaves Samson without the relational vocabulary for **horizontal** competition — the kind that resolves, the kind that ends in handshake and shared beer. All his competitions are vertical, status-coded, zero-sum. He does not know how to lose a round and come back next week. He loses a round and irradiates himself.

### Leverage

He is unprepared for genuinely peer-level allies who do not defer and do not compete for the same prize. Such an ally, deployed early in a stress sequence, can interrupt his escalation ladder in a way no superior or subordinate can. There are not many such people in his life. There has never been one for long.

---

## 4. CHILDREN (None on Record)

### History

No children. No reported pregnancies. No adopted, fostered, godparented, or surrogate children. The absence is striking for a man of his age, station, and apparent heterosexuality across a four-decade record. It is not for lack of opportunity in the genre's terms; it is for lack of pursuit.

### Dynamics

The childlessness is **chosen, though probably not consciously**. A man whose entire psychic structure is organized around being the most important person in the room does not have children, because children — actual children, not symbolic ones — demote you immediately and permanently. The narcissistic structure is allergic to the demotion.

The displacement is into **patients-as-children**. Banner is the most famous and most contaminated example: Samson's investment in Banner has the affective shape of a parent's investment in a difficult child, with all the corresponding pathologies (over-identification, refusal to let go, inability to tolerate the child's choosing of another caregiver, grief disguised as professional concern when the child outgrows the relationship). The Merged Hulk integration work, his finest hour, was in part the work of a man finally permitted to be the *good parent* he had not been parented by — and the wreckage that followed, when the integration unwound and Banner moved past him, was the wreckage of a parent who cannot release a child.

### Failure Mode

The absence of actual children means the parental drive has no legitimate object, and so it is routed entirely into the clinical relationships, contaminating them. A Samson with a child of his own would, by the basic operation of demoting his own importance, have been a less dangerous clinician and a healthier man. The structure that prevented him from having children is the same structure that made him a hazard inside the consulting room.

### Leverage

A young person, presented as needing tutelage and capable of being shaped into a credit to him, will move him. He has not, on the record, been worked through this vector, but it remains open.

---

## 5. THE DEAD

### History

There are no canonical dead in Samson's family of origin to which he has been observed grieving on the page. Given his age, the actuarial probability that both parents are deceased is substantial, and the absence of any grieving sequence is, again, diagnostic. The dead one has been is **himself** — killed during *Fall of the Hulks*, returned, and visibly altered by the experience. The closest thing to a graveside scene Samson has had is the scene with his own.

### Dynamics

A man who has been dead and come back, and who does not subsequently restructure his life around the fact, is a man who was already living at some distance from it. The post-resurrection Samson of the Ewing era reads as someone who finally permits himself the grieving he had not previously permitted — for the father he did not have, the mother he did not have, the brother he did not have, the children he did not have, the woman he could not have, and the version of himself that died trying to obtain any of them through escalation.

### Failure Mode

The unfinished grief, across decades, is the substrate the drinking ran on. Sobriety, when it took, took because the grieving finally began.

### Leverage

A man in active grief is not leverageable in the usual ways; he is, however, **reachable** in ways he was not before. An operator seeking to move the current Samson would do better with honesty than with manipulation. This is itself the measure of how much has changed.

---

## Synthesis: The Origin Bond That Was Never Made

The through-line of Samson's family-of-origin material is that **the bonds were structurally present and emotionally insufficient** — not absent enough to grieve, not present enough to nourish. A child raised in that specific configuration becomes an adult who cannot tell the difference between being known and being admired, who pursues admiration on the assumption that being known will arrive with it, and who is bewildered, across an entire adulthood, that it does not.

The name was the original wound and the original instruction. Leonard Samson has spent fifty years on the page trying to be worthy of it, and the most clinically interesting fact about his late period is that he has, finally, begun to suspect he was worthy of it the day it was given, and that the project of proving it was the trap.

The file on the family is short because the family was, functionally, short. Everything that should have been there and was not, became the cape.


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

## Preliminary Note on Catalog Scope

The subject's allied/chosen-family network is, on inspection, structurally thin for a man of his tenure, reach, and credentials. After fifty-plus years on the public record he can claim no godchildren, no roommates, no standing card game, no recurring co-author, no clinical partner in private practice. The relationships below are the substantive ones — those with documentable longitudinal contact, mutual self-disclosure (in at least one direction), and demonstrable behavioral influence on the subject. The list is shorter than it ought to be for a man this prominent. That brevity is itself the headline finding of this section: Samson maintains an unusually large *acquaintance surface* and an unusually small *intimacy core*, and the people inside the core are nearly all professional contacts who became personal contacts without ever fully shedding the professional frame. He does not appear to know how to make a friend who is not also a case, a colleague, a commanding officer, or a competitor.

---

## 1. BETTY ROSS BANNER — (cross-listed; treated fully under Relationships I, summarized here for network coherence)

Included here only because the subject would, if asked, name her as a friend. She is not. The relationship is catalogued in full in the prior section. Its presence in his self-reported "ally" column is itself a data point: he conflates pursuit-object with chosen family, and this conflation has distorted every other intimacy he has tried to build. Any reading of the relationships below must account for the fact that Samson allocates a disproportionate share of his emotional bandwidth to a woman who has, for forty years, been telling him in increasingly direct language that she is not available. The bandwidth he spends on her is bandwidth not spent on the people in this section.

---

## 2. BRUCE BANNER — Patient, Rival, and the Closest Thing to a Brother He Has

### History
First contact: Gamma Base intake, presented in the published record at *Incredible Hulk* #141 (1971). Samson was the consulting psychiatrist; Banner was the case. The relationship has run continuously for over five decades of in-universe time across nearly every major Hulk run — Thomas, Wein, Mantlo, David, Jones, Jenkins, Casey, Pak, Loeb, Parker, Aaron, Waid, Duggan, Ewing. There is no Banner-era of any length that does not feature Samson somewhere in the orbit.

### Dynamics
A four-way slot occupied by a single person: Banner is simultaneously (a) Samson's most important patient, (b) his romantic rival, (c) the source of his powers and therefore his costumed identity, and (d) the only peer in the world who can match him intellectually inside the gamma problem space. No one human being should be asked to hold four roles for another human being, and Samson has never disambiguated them. He oscillates among them, often within the same conversation. He will diagnose Banner in one breath, condescend to him as a romantic loser in the next, defer to him as a hard scientist in the third, and propose a joint experiment in the fourth.

Banner reciprocates with a calibrated wariness. The published record contains repeated instances of Banner accepting Samson's clinical interventions while declining to *trust* him — agreeing to the hypnosis in the Merged Hulk arc, for example, but with eyes open about who Samson is and what Samson wants. Banner is, of the two, by far the more emotionally honest about what the relationship is.

### Evolution
- **Era 1 (1970s):** Open antagonism dressed as treatment. Samson fights Banner regularly. Each fight is framed as a containment intervention; each contains an unmistakable element of "I am the better version of you, and I will demonstrate it now."
- **Era 2 (1980s–mid 90s):** Professionalization. Samson does his best clinical work on Banner in this period — the integration culminating in *Incredible Hulk* #377. The rivalry is sublimated, not resolved. He is genuinely useful and genuinely unable to step back.
- **Era 3 (late 90s–2000s):** Erosion. Samson's drinking and decompensation contaminate the relationship. He takes contracts that put him on the wrong side of Banner more than once. *World War Hulk* and *Fall of the Hulks* culminate in a position that, viewed from Banner's seat, looks like betrayal even though Samson was being manipulated.
- **Era 4 (2010s onward):** Quiet reconciliation. Samson is older, sober(er), chastened. Banner — and Banner's various successors and splits in the Ewing-era material — interact with him as an elder consultant whose knowledge is respected and whose proximity is permitted in measured doses.

### Trust / Safety
Asymmetric. Banner trusts Samson's *technique* and distrusts Samson's *motives* — correctly, on both counts. Samson believes he trusts Banner; what he actually does is rely on Banner to occupy the role that organizes his (Samson's) professional identity. Safety, in any clinical sense, has never been clean between them: the dual-relationship violation is foundational and never repaired.

### Failure Mode
Samson loses Banner when Banner finally and fully refuses the patient role with him. This has happened multiple times in micro and once or twice in macro. Each time it has happened, Samson has decompensated — sought a new high-profile case, accepted a compromising contract, or escalated his power level. The pattern is consistent enough to be predictive: take Banner out of Samson's caseload and watch the acting-out begin within weeks.

### Leverage
Banner can move Samson by appealing to the clinician, by appealing to the rival, or by appealing to the man who wants Betty's good opinion. Banner knows all three levers and uses them sparingly. Samson can move Banner only by being competent — when his work is good, Banner shows up; when his work is bad, Banner withdraws. The currency between them is craft.

---

## 3. RICK JONES — The Younger Brother He Did Not Earn

### History
Rick was already a Banner-orbit fixture when Samson arrived in 1971. They have been adjacent for the entirety of Samson's career. The relationship is not foregrounded the way the Banner one is, but it is consistent: Rick is present at Gamma Base, present in the Pantheon era, present in the *Hulk* runs through to the Ewing material in his various transformed and post-transformed states.

### Dynamics
Rick is one of the very few people in the published record who has seen every version of Samson — the eager 1971 consultant, the swaggering 80s hero, the brittle 90s drinker, the compromised 2000s asset, the chastened 2010s elder. Rick is also one of the very few people Samson does not appear to *perform* for. The dynamic is the closest thing in the file to an ordinary friendship: easy presence, low-stakes conversation, jokes that land without effort. Samson is visibly less verbose around Rick than around almost anyone else. The clinical jargon recedes. He uses contractions more. He sits down without arranging his posture first.

### Evolution
Early on, Samson treats Rick as a kid — pleasantly, not condescendingly, but as a junior. The shift is gradual and unmarked: by the David run he is treating Rick as a peer, and by the Pak/Loeb era he is treating Rick as one of the rare people whose read on Banner he respects without needing to one-up. By the Ewing era, when Rick's life has gone through its own catastrophes, Samson is — for the first time in the file — sometimes the steadier of the two.

### Trust / Safety
The highest trust score of any relationship in the dossier, and notably it is the relationship with the lowest stakes. Samson can be trusted not to hurt Rick because Rick is not in the slot of patient, rival, or romantic interest. The relationship is safe precisely because Samson has not loaded it with the roles he is bad at carrying. This is diagnostic: Samson is *capable* of decent, undefended friendship, but only with people who do not activate any of his organizing pathologies.

### Failure Mode
Inattention. Samson does not initiate with Rick. He shows up when their paths cross, he is glad to see him, and then he does not call. The friendship survives because Rick is generous about asymmetry and because their paths cross often. In a counterfactual where Rick left the gamma orbit entirely, the friendship would attenuate to holiday-card status within two years.

### Leverage
Rick is the only person in the network who can tell Samson the truth about himself and be heard without triggering defensive escalation. He has done so on the record more than once. The leverage is unused: Rick is by temperament not a confronter, and Samson has accordingly never been pressed on his pathology by the one ally most likely to land the punch.

---

## 4. JENNIFER WALTERS (SHE-HULK) — Peer, Equal, Mirror He Refuses to Look Into

### History
Walters enters Samson's orbit in the early 80s as Banner's cousin and an emergent gamma case in her own right. Their relationship has been continuous since. It includes professional collaboration (legal-clinical interface in multiple arcs), social proximity (gamma-family gatherings), and combat alongside (Pantheon, *World War Hulk*, various crossovers).

### Dynamics
Walters is the only person in the network who is Samson's peer on *every* axis simultaneously — credentialed professional, gamma-empowered, physically formidable, sexually self-possessed, comfortable in public, capable of holding a press conference and a clinical conversation in the same afternoon. She is what he would look like if his pathology had been organized as confidence rather than grandiosity.

He flirts with her, intermittently, across the entire record. She responds with a deflective good humor that has never tipped into either acceptance or refusal sharp enough to terminate the pattern. Crucially, the flirtation is qualitatively *different* from the Betty pursuit: it is lighter, lower-stakes, and Samson can stop when she signals stop. With Betty he cannot. With Jennifer he can.

### Evolution
Early years: collegial, with the flirtation as background hum. Middle period (David through Pak): increasingly the relationship in which Samson is most *himself* in a professional setting — he is competent, she is competent, they handle business and trade barbs. Late period (post-*Fall of the Hulks*, Ewing-era): Walters is one of the people who registers the change in him, treats him with a measured warmth that acknowledges the damage without reducing him to it.

### Trust / Safety
High, with one caveat. Walters trusts Samson clinically and tactically. She does not, on the available evidence, share personal material with him. The flow of disclosure is one-way and shallow — they talk shop, they joke, they fight side by side, and neither tells the other anything that would cost them to say.

### Failure Mode
The relationship's protective factor is also its limit: it has never been tested. Because neither has ever asked the other for something costly, neither knows what the other would do. The friendship is real but unstressed.

### Leverage
Walters can stop Samson from making a fool of himself in public faster than anyone else in the network — a raised eyebrow, a one-word interjection, and he will recalibrate. She is one of the very few people whose judgment he actively does not want to fail. The lever exists. She rarely pulls it.

---

## 5. CLAY QUARTERMAIN — The Operator Friend, Killed Mid-Era

### History
Quartermain, the long-serving SHIELD field agent attached to gamma-related operations across the 70s, 80s, and 90s, was Samson's most consistent non-clinical professional contact for nearly two decades. They worked dozens of operations together; they drank together; they were, by the standards of Samson's network, *friends* in the ordinary sense of the word.

### Dynamics
Quartermain occupied a slot no one else in the file ever filled: the colleague who was not a patient, not a rival, not a romantic interest, not a peer in psychiatry, and not a member of the gamma family. He was a competent operator who liked Samson's company, took his calls, ribbed him about the hair, and did not require anything from him except presence and reliability. The dynamic was easy because the stakes were professionally serious and personally low.

### Evolution
A flat curve, which is the rare and good thing. The relationship did not deepen dramatically and did not erode; it simply persisted at a stable level of warm professional companionship for the better part of twenty years. Samson's verbal register with Quartermain was the second-most-relaxed in the file, behind only Rick Jones.

### Trust / Safety
High mutual operational trust. Limited mutual personal disclosure, but more than Samson typically allowed — Quartermain is one of the few peers Samson is shown drinking *with* rather than drinking *around*, and the difference is meaningful.

### Failure Mode
Quartermain's death in the late 2000s removed from Samson's life the single most stabilizing peer relationship he had outside the gamma family proper. The loss is under-discussed in the published record but lines up chronologically with Samson's accelerating decompensation in the lead-up to *Fall of the Hulks*. A surveillance file would mark the death as a critical inflection point: a man with this thin a non-clinical social structure cannot afford to lose his one non-clinical friend without sequelae.

### Leverage
N/A, posthumous. While alive, Quartermain could redirect Samson with a phone call and a bar. Nobody has since occupied that slot.

---

## 6. THADDEUS "THUNDERBOLT" ROSS — Father-Figure, Commanding Officer, Hated and Needed

### History
Ross was the institutional power at Gamma Base when Samson arrived in 1971 and remained the dominant Army figure in the gamma file for decades. Samson's first sustained employment, his first sustained platform, and his first sustained adult environment were all under Ross's command.

### Dynamics
This is the closest thing in the file to a paternal transference, and Samson resents it accordingly. Ross is the older man whose approval Samson needed and never quite secured, the institutional power who paid him and disrespected him in the same breath, and — not least — the father of the woman Samson has spent forty years pursuing. The relationship is overdetermined.

Samson handled it, across Era 1 and Era 2, by performing competence and ignoring contempt. Ross handled it by using Samson's services and withholding regard. The arrangement was stable because it suited both.

### Evolution
- **Era 1:** Junior consultant to senior General. Samson swallows the slights.
- **Era 2:** Established expert. Samson begins to talk back, mildly. Ross continues to use him.
- **Era 3:** Both men compromised. Ross's own arc (Red Hulk transformation, institutional disgrace) inverts the power gradient. They are now peers in damage.
- **Era 4:** A wary, mutual, unspoken acknowledgment that they shared a long stretch of history and that neither came out of it well.

### Trust / Safety
Low in both directions and stable about it. Neither expected loyalty; neither received it; neither was surprised. This is the only relationship in the file that benefited from low expectations.

### Failure Mode
The failure already happened, repeatedly, and was metabolized as the structure of the relationship. There is no further failure mode because there is no further trust to break.

### Leverage
Ross could move Samson by invoking Betty, by invoking the contract, or by invoking institutional consequence. Samson could move Ross essentially not at all — and the asymmetry was a steady irritation that contributed nontrivially to the narcissistic injury reservoir Samson carried into Era 3.

---

## 7. THE PANTHEON / AGAMEMNON-ERA TEAMMATES — A Cohort He Joined and Did Not Belong To

### History
During the Peter David run, Samson briefly orbited the Pantheon — the family-operation that absorbed Banner for a substantial mid-90s arc. He was not a member; he was a frequent consultant and visitor, attached through Banner.

### Dynamics
The Pantheon was structured as a chosen family in the literal sense — a multigenerational kin-group operating as a team. Samson's behavior inside it is diagnostic: he was friendly with several members (Atalanta in particular), respectful of the elders, and entirely unable to convert proximity into belonging. He left the Pantheon's orbit with no sustained relationships from it. A man with a functioning chosen-family instinct would have come out of that period with at least one friend for life. He did not.

### Evolution
N/A — the cohort dissolved as Banner's arc moved on. Samson did not maintain.

### Trust / Safety
Adequate at the time; not tested by anything that survived the arc.

### Failure Mode
The diagnostic failure is the *non-conversion*. Samson encountered a fully formed chosen family, was welcomed at the threshold, and did not cross it. This is consistent with the broader pattern: he affiliates with institutions and individuals but not with *kin-structures*, because kin-structures require him to be ordinary inside them and ordinariness is the one demand he cannot meet.

### Leverage
N/A.

---

## 8. NICK FURY (CLASSIC ERA) — Institutional Patron Rather Than Friend

### History
Samson held SHIELD consultancies on and off across multiple decades. Fury was, for most of that span, the institutional principal. They were not close. They were functionally cordial.

### Dynamics
Fury read Samson accurately and used him accordingly: deployed where the credentials and the muscle were both needed, kept on a short leash, not invited into the inner circle. Samson — to his credit — appears to have understood this and not pretended otherwise. He treated Fury with the respect due to a power he could not move and did not try to charm him.

### Evolution
Flat, transactional, durable.

### Trust / Safety
Operational only.

### Failure Mode
The relationship's transactional character made Samson recruitable, in Era 3, by other institutional actors whose offers looked similar to Fury's. He did not have a Fury-equivalent saying *don't take that contract* during the lead-up to *Fall of the Hulks*. Quartermain might have, had he lived; Fury, who would have, was not in position.

### Leverage
Institutional pay and access. Used.

---

## 9. AMADEUS CHO — The Protégé He Did Not Quite Mentor

### History
Cho entered the gamma orbit in the mid-2000s as Banner's young genius adjacent. He has been continuously present since, including periods as Hulk himself. Samson's interactions with him are intermittent but consistent across that span.

### Dynamics
This is the only relationship in the file that could be classified as a *mentoring* relationship, and even here the label is generous. Samson treats Cho with respect, occasionally with genuine warmth, and consistently with the slight wariness of an older expert who recognizes that the younger man is, on the metric they share (raw cognitive horsepower), his superior. The mentoring is therefore lopsided: Samson can teach Cho about clinical work, about navigating institutions, about the psychology of the gamma cohort — and he does, in flashes — but he cannot offer Cho the standard mentor's gift of *being the bigger mind in the room*. He is not.

### Evolution
A relationship that has slowly warmed without ever becoming central to either party. In the late material Samson is shown taking Cho more seriously, and Cho extending more deference than the surface dynamic would predict — there is, between them, a quiet recognition of mutual usefulness.

### Trust / Safety
Moderate and rising. Cho is one of the few younger figures who has seen Samson at his worst and not written him off.

### Failure Mode
Samson does not put in the time. A real mentorship requires the older party to allocate attention as a recurring expense, and Samson's attentional budget is consumed by his own caseload, his own performance, and Betty. Cho gets the spare cycles. He has accepted this; a more demanding protégé would not.

### Leverage
Cho can move Samson by appealing to clinical pride and by being right about a case. Samson can move Cho by being demonstrably useful — same currency as Banner, slightly different denomination.

---

## 10. THE GAMMA-WORLD COHORT (DIFFUSE) — Skaar, Lyra, A-Bomb, the Wider Family

### History
Through the Pak era and after, Samson has been adjacent to the extended gamma family — Banner's literal son Skaar, his alternate-future daughter Lyra, Rick Jones in his transformed states, and the wider rotating cast of Hulks. He is the de facto family psychiatrist for a literal extended family of gamma-positive individuals.

### Dynamics
Samson handles this collective with surprising grace. The clinical work with the gamma cohort is some of the steadiest of his late career — he treats each of them as an individual case, does not impose Banner-frames where they do not fit, and is one of the few professionals in the Marvel Universe with the experience to know how the various gamma neuropsychiatric presentations differ. The cohort regards him as a fixture: not beloved, not feared, simply *the man you call*.

### Evolution
A late-career stabilization. The cohort grew up around him; he aged into the role of its consulting elder; the role suits him better than any he has previously occupied.

### Trust / Safety
Distributed and adequate. No single member of the cohort is a confidant; collectively they constitute the closest thing he has to professional family.

### Failure Mode
If the cohort collectively repudiated him — were a second *Fall of the Hulks*-type compromise to occur — he would have nowhere to land. The late-era stability is contingent on the cohort's continued willingness to grant him the elder-consultant slot.

### Leverage
Reciprocal and case-specific.

---

## 11. ABSENCES OF NOTE

A surveillance file would flag the following non-relationships as diagnostically significant:

- **No therapist of his own.** A psychiatrist of his tenure and exposure who has not been in his own therapy is a clinician with a structural blind spot. The published record contains no analyst, no supervisor, no consultation group. His insight has had no external check for fifty years.
- **No sponsor.** Through the Era 3 drinking, no AA contact, no recovery community, no named sober ally. The Era 4 sobriety, real as it appears, is undersupported by any visible recovery infrastructure.
- **No academic peers.** No co-author, no department, no recurring conference companion. He is a freelance superstar in a field that ordinarily runs on institutional affiliation, and the freelancing has cost him the peer-review function that ordinary academic life supplies.
- **No childhood friends.** The single most telling absence. Adults who have no contact with anyone who knew them as a child are adults who have, at some level, declined to be continuous with the child they were. Samson's flashback silence about his early life (noted in the etiology section of the primary workup) is doubled by the absence of any living witness to that period.
- **No clergy, no coach, no longtime barber, no doorman who knows his name.** The civilian texture of an ordinary life — the small recurring relationships that anchor a person — is not present in the file. He moves through cities as a professional, not as a resident.

The cumulative effect: a man whose ally network is *just large enough* to keep him operational and *just small enough* to keep him from being seen. This is consistent with the NPD frame elaborated in the primary workup. People with the subject's organization tend to curate networks of exactly this shape — wide enough to mirror the self, narrow enough to never contradict it. The two relationships in the file that come closest to contradicting the self — Rick Jones and the late Clay Quartermain — are notable for being the relationships in which Samson is most


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — RIVALS, ENEMIES & LOVERS

A note on taxonomy before the entries. With Samson the categories *rival*, *enemy*, and *lover* are not clean. His primary rival is also his primary patient; his primary lover is also his rival's wife; several of his enemies began as colleagues he respected and then envied. The structural fact of his interpersonal life is **category collapse**: he cannot keep relational roles separate, and the moments of his greatest professional failure are the moments in which those categories have folded into one another inside him without his noticing. The dossier preserves the collapse rather than tidying it.

---

## I. RIVALS

### Robert Bruce Banner

The keystone. Every other entry in this section is, to some degree, a displacement of this one.

**History.** First contact, *Incredible Hulk* #141, on Samson's terms: Banner is the patient, restrained and gamma-saturated; Samson is the brilliant young consultant brought in by Ross with a treatment plan. The clinical encounter inverts within hours — Samson siphons the gamma off Banner, ingests it himself, and meets Banner as a peer-in-power within the same arc. He has never recovered from the structural perfection of that first meeting: the only relationship in his life that began with him in unambiguous authority over another man, and which he immediately destroyed by making them equals on a battlefield rather than in a consulting room. The original sin is not the self-experiment; it is the refusal of asymmetry. He could not bear to remain the doctor while Banner remained the case.

**Dynamics.** Across forty publication years the relationship cycles a small set of moves: (1) Banner deteriorates, Samson is summoned, Samson does competent intake; (2) the case engages Samson's genuine clinical interest and his unacknowledged competitive interest in roughly equal measure; (3) intervention escalates; (4) Hulk emerges; (5) Samson fights him, often with relief — the fight resolves the ambivalence the consult could not; (6) post-combat, Samson resumes the clinician role and writes the encounter up as therapy. The Mantlo-era and David-era Merged Hulk work (#377) is the one occasion on which this loop is broken: Samson stays in the chair, does the hypnotic regression cleanly, refuses to make it about himself, and produces the best therapeutic outcome of Banner's life. It is not coincidence that this is also the period in which Betty is most decisively married to Banner; with the romantic competition settled (he tells himself), Samson can finally be the doctor. The settlement does not hold.

**Evolution.** Era 1 Samson approaches Banner as a problem to solve and a stage to perform on. Era 2 Samson approaches Banner as the case that justifies his career — and he is right to; the work is real. Era 3 Samson approaches Banner with a corrosion of envy that he cannot name, expressed as increasingly proprietary language about "my patient" and increasingly punitive interventions cosigned by SHIELD. Era 4 Samson approaches Banner with the chastened recognition of a man who tried to be his peer, his doctor, and his replacement simultaneously and now understands he was none of them.

**Trust/safety.** Asymmetric and inverse to what either man would say aloud. Banner trusts Samson's *technique* and distrusts his *motives* — correctly. Samson trusts Banner's *containment* (he genuinely believes Banner will not kill him, and Banner never has) and distrusts Banner's *uptake of the work*, which he reads as resistance when it is often just accurate reading of Samson's countertransference. The safest version of this relationship is consultative, time-limited, and supervised by a third party. None of those conditions has obtained for any extended period.

**Failure mode.** Samson translates clinical decisions into combat decisions under stress. When the therapeutic alliance is strained, he reaches for gamma and gear rather than supervision. The *Fall of the Hulks* turn is the worst version of this failure: with his judgment externally compromised, the pre-existing fault line opened along its own grain — he aligned with Banner's actual enemies and justified it as Banner's actual treatment. He could only be turned because he was already three-quarters turned.

**Leverage.** Banner's wellbeing. Banner's approval. Any framing in which Banner is "doing better without him." Inversely: any framing in which only Samson can reach Banner — this is the line that has pulled him back into harm's room every time.

---

### Samuel Sterns / The Leader

The mirror Samson cannot stop looking into. Sterns is what Samson would be if his grandiosity were uncomplicated by a conscience and his somatic gift had been intellect instead of athleticism. They are the same animal in different fur.

**History.** Recurring antagonist contact across the 70s and 80s, intermittent through the 90s, structurally central in *Fall of the Hulks*/*World War Hulks* (Pak/Parker, 2009–2010). The early encounters are conventional cape combat — Samson in the role of muscle for Banner's side, Sterns in the role of cerebral threat. The 2000s arcs revise the relationship retroactively: Sterns is shown to have been studying Samson for years, identifying the narcissistic substrate, and engineering the conditions under which Samson's compensatory power-acquisition would become useful to him.

**Dynamics.** Sterns flatters Samson's intellect in a register no one else does — peer-to-peer, post-doctoral, "you and I both know" — and Samson, starved for that register in a life spent surrounded by either soldiers or patients, drinks it. The flattery is technically accurate, which makes it more dangerous than ordinary flattery; Sterns really does respect Samson's mind, and he weaponizes the respect.

**Evolution.** What began as a combat rivalry became, in Era 3, a slow recruitment. By *Fall of the Hulks* Samson is functionally an asset Sterns has been cultivating across decades, although neither character would have described it that way at any specific moment. The recruitment succeeded because Sterns offered Samson the one thing Banner never could: unambiguous acknowledgement of Samson's superiority over the rest of the room.

**Trust/safety.** Catastrophically miscalibrated. Samson believes, in the Pak arcs, that he is using Sterns. He is not.

**Failure mode.** Samson cannot decline intellectual recognition from a peer-equivalent, and Sterns is the only peer-equivalent who has ever offered it without competitive subtext. The failure is that the absence of subtext is itself the subtext.

**Leverage.** Recognition. Specifically: being told, by someone qualified to know, that he is the smartest clinician in the gamma field. Secondarily: access to gamma technology framed as research rather than weaponization.

---

### George Tarleton / MODOK

A subsidiary rival, important mostly as a tell. Samson's distaste for MODOK is louder than his distaste for Sterns and disproportionate to the threat: Tarleton is the version of weaponized intellect that has visibly given up the body, and Samson — whose self-worth is rooted in somatic exceptionalism — cannot look at MODOK without flinching at a possible future. The aversion is phobic, not strategic. In the *World War Hulks* configuration he tolerates working alongside MODOK because Sterns has framed it as transitional; the tolerance is itself a measure of how compromised his judgment had become.

**Leverage.** Negligible in the direct sense — MODOK has no purchase on him personally — but useful as a *measurement instrument*: when Samson stops finding MODOK repulsive, he has stopped being himself.

---

### Emil Blonsky / The Abomination

A rivalry in the lowest key. Blonsky is the cautionary case Samson tells himself he is not — the man whose gamma exposure produced only monstrosity, no profession, no integration, no name to put after the transformation. Samson handles Blonsky competently in combat across multiple decades and condescends to him reflexively, even when Blonsky is the more honest about what gamma is. The condescension is the diagnostic feature: Samson needs Blonsky to be the lower term so that his own self-experiment can be the higher.

**Failure mode.** He will under-estimate Blonsky in any sustained engagement because he requires Blonsky to remain a category beneath him.

**Leverage.** None Blonsky has ever successfully exercised.

---

### Carl "Crusher" Creel, the Wrecking Crew, Glenn Talbot (in his Hulk-suited iterations), and the recurring rota of gamma-adjacent muscle

Aggregate entry. These are not rivals in any meaningful psychological sense; they are the steady state of opponents against which Samson maintains his physical fluency. Their function in his life is to be punched well. He treats them with a workmanlike courtesy in combat — almost sportsmanlike — and forgets them between encounters. The lack of personal animus is genuine.

**Significance.** That Samson can have purely transactional rivals at all is a protective fact. It means the personalized rivalries (Banner, Sterns) are bounded and not generalized to all comers. He is not, fundamentally, a man who needs every opponent to mean something. He is a man who needs *two* opponents to mean everything, and the rest can be exercise.

---

### Glenn Talbot (the man, before the suit)

A separate entry from the muscle-rota above. Talbot is the romantic rival who preceded Samson with Betty — the first husband, the soldier, the man whose claim on her was authorized by every institutional structure Samson respects. Samson's behavior toward Talbot in the early 70s issues is exemplary in its surface: collegial, deferential to rank, professionally appropriate. The behavior is also continuously, microscopically, competitive — Samson positions himself in rooms such that Betty's sightlines pass through him before they reach Talbot, offers clinical interpretations of Talbot's stress that are technically correct and tactically undermining, and is reliably present at moments of Talbot-Betty friction in a role of consoling third.

**Failure mode.** The conduct is deniable individually and damning cumulatively. Samson would, if asked, have offered a sincere defense of every act in isolation. The pattern is invisible to him because admitting it would require admitting the pursuit was active before Talbot's death freed it to become so officially.

**Leverage (posthumous).** Talbot retains leverage over Samson by being the man Betty grieved properly. Samson has never received that grade of grief from anyone and knows it.

---

## II. ENEMIES

### Thunderbolt Ross (in his adversarial phases, including Red Hulk)

Ross is not consistently an enemy. He is Samson's longest-running institutional patron, intermittent father-figure-by-proximity, and the man whose daughter Samson has pursued across the entirety of their acquaintance. The relationship cycles between employer, antagonist, and reluctant peer, depending on which Ross is in the chair.

**History.** Ross hires Samson onto the Gamma Base consult in #141 and re-hires him in some form across nearly every subsequent administration of the Hulk problem. He tolerates Samson's pursuit of Betty for one reason: Samson is, in Ross's military taxonomy, the *acceptable* civilian alternative to Banner — credentialed, employed, controllable, and not green most of the time. Ross's tolerance is conditional and Samson knows it; the knowledge sharpens the pursuit rather than restraining it.

**Dynamics.** Samson speaks to Ross in a register he uses with no one else — slightly deferential, more concrete than his usual jargon, calibrated to a man who will not tolerate being managed. Ross speaks to Samson with the contemptuous reliance of a commander toward a specialist whose expertise he needs and whose civilian softness he despises. The relationship works precisely because neither has illusions about the other's regard.

**Evolution.** Era 1: employer/employee with romantic complication. Era 2: tense alliance during Banner's marriage to Betty (Ross blames Samson less than he blames Banner; Samson is, briefly, the lesser threat). Era 3: ruptures repeatedly as Ross's own gamma transformation makes him a peer-in-monstrosity, a development Samson cannot metabolize because it scrambles the asymmetry he needs with Ross. Era 4: a wary professional respect, both men chastened, both having lost Betty in different registers.

**Trust/safety.** Operationally high, personally low. Samson trusts Ross to act in character; he does not trust Ross to refrain from killing him if mission logic required it. Ross trusts Samson to perform contracted work and does not trust him within fifty feet of his daughter.

**Failure mode.** Samson cannot sustain a clinical posture toward Ross post-Red Hulk because the gamma transformation has made Ross his *peer in the exact register Samson believed was his alone*. The reaction is envy disguised as concern. Ross perceives this immediately.

**Leverage.** Ross holds the institutional access — SHIELD/Army/Gamma Base contracts — that Samson needs for his self-concept as a player. Samson holds clinical readings of Ross that Ross does not want generated and does not want published. Mutual assured discomfort.

---

### Brian Banner (posthumous, by inference)

Samson never met him. Brian Banner is dead before Samson enters the case. He is, however, the most consequential antagonist in Samson's professional life, because the Merged Hulk integration is the work of slowly defeating a man Samson can only reach through his son's nervous system.

**Dynamics.** In session with Banner, particularly during the regression work, Samson is functionally in a long-form confrontation with Brian — extracting him from Bruce, naming him, refusing his terms. The work is the best of Samson's career and the most genuinely selfless: he does not get to win this fight in any room with witnesses. The victory, if it comes, comes inside another man.

**Significance.** This is the entry that complicates the rest of the dossier. Samson can do superb work against a target that offers him no personal glory. He simply rarely chooses to.

**Leverage.** Brian Banner has no leverage on Samson, which is exactly why Samson can do the work cleanly.

---

### His own corrupted self (during *Fall of the Hulks* / *World War Hulks*)

Listed as an enemy because the dossier requires honesty. The Samson who acted during that arc was Samson plus external compromise, but the compromise found purchase. Post-event, the surviving Samson treats the corrupted Samson as a discrete adversary — a man he was, briefly, whose decisions he now spends professional capital undoing. This is the closest he has come to genuine reflective insight, and it arrived via the only route his defenses would permit: framing the failure as someone else.

**Failure mode of the framing.** Useful in the short term, limiting in the long term. As long as the *Fall of the Hulks* Samson is an enemy rather than an aspect, the etiological work remains uncompleted.

**Leverage.** The chastening is genuine. He will not, going forward, accept gamma augmentation offered by a peer-equivalent without supervision. The lesson is bought. Whether it generalizes to the underlying narcissistic substrate is the open question of Era 4.

---

### The Intelligencia (collectively)

Sterns, MODOK, the Wizard, the Mad Thinker, the Red Ghost, et al. Samson's nominal allies during the compromised period and his enemies before and after. The collective is significant less for any individual member than for what it represented to him: a *peer group of intellects*, the cohort he had spent his career not having. Gamma Base gave him soldiers and patients. The Intelligencia, briefly, gave him colleagues. That the colleagues were villains was, to the compromised Samson, a secondary detail. To the chastened Samson it is the central detail and the source of the shame.

**Leverage.** None remaining, post-arc. He will not accept that bid again. He will, however, remain susceptible to *one-on-one* intellectual recognition from individual members, particularly Sterns. The cohort effect is broken; the dyadic vulnerability is not.

---

## III. LOVERS AND INTIMATES

### Elizabeth "Betty" Ross Talbot Banner

The defining intimate relationship of his life, by a margin that itself is diagnostic.

**History.** First contact at Gamma Base, #141 and adjacent issues. Betty is, at the moment of meeting, an Army general's daughter married to (or recently widowed by) a soldier, in love with a fugitive scientist who turns into a monster, and surrounded by men who variously want to use, save, contain, or possess her. Samson enters this configuration as the *reasonable* option — credentialed, articulate, present, not currently green. His pursuit begins in the same arc in which he becomes a superhero and is not separable from that decision; the gamma self-administration in #141 is, among other things, a courtship display performed in her sightline.

**Dynamics.** Samson's mode with Betty is *sustained attentive presence calibrated to her stated and unstated distress*, a mode he is professionally trained to deploy and which he cannot, in her case, switch off. Every conversation is a low-grade therapeutic intervention plus a low-grade flirtation, the two indistinguishable to him and increasingly distinguishable to her. He listens well. He remembers details. He shows up at correct moments with correct affect. The pursuit is, in the granular sense, *competent* — which is part of what makes it so durable a category violation. He is not a clumsy suitor. He is a skilled one who has refused to hear no for forty years of publication time.

**Evolution.** Era 1: open pursuit, intermittently reciprocated, Betty's actual ambivalence read by Samson as available signal. Era 2: pursuit continues across her marriage to Banner, modulated downward in overt expression and upward in proprietary clinical concern. The Merged Hulk work of this period is partly a gift to her and partly an attempt to make her husband into the version of her husband she might leave for him; Samson would deny the second clause and the denial would be sincere. Era 3: pursuit becomes erratic and substance-shadowed; he is less skilled at the long game, more prone to ill-timed declarations. Era 4: visibly relinquished, possibly genuinely. The relinquishment reads as grief work he should have done in Era 1.

**Trust/safety.** Betty's trust in Samson is real and bounded — she trusts him with her brother-thoughts, her father-thoughts, her fear-thoughts, and not with the part of herself she gave to Banner. The boundary is stable on her side. It is not stable on his.

**Failure mode.** He cannot read "no, and also I value you" as a steady-state. He metabolizes the second clause and discounts the first; each renewed contact resets his hopes to baseline. The countertransference he diagnoses easily in trainees he cannot see in himself with her.

**Leverage.** Total, and largely unexercised. Betty has never used the leverage she has. The non-use is one of the things he loves about her and one of the things he has never been able to reciprocate at scale.

---

### Leonard Skivorski Jr. / Doc Sasquatch (and other professional-erotic adjacencies of Era 3)

A category placeholder more than a person. The David and post-David runs hint at a series of brief, undocumented entanglements during Samson's decompensating period — colleagues, fellow consultants, women met at conferences and crisis sites. The record is thin because the encounters were thin: short-duration, mutually professional-adjacent, ending without follow-through on his side. The pattern is diagnostically louder than any individual instance: he sought interchangeable partners during the period in which the non-interchangeable one was unavailable, and discarded each as soon as the absence of Betty became salient in her presence.

**Failure mode across the set.** Inability to escalate or to clearly end. The partners drifted away rather than being released. He would, if asked, have called several of them friends.

**Leverage.** None retained by any party. The clean break that would have generated leverage was the break he could not perform.

---

### Carolyn Parmenter (and other early-Era patients-adjacent entanglements)

Where the record indicates patient-adjacent intimacies — civilians met through the Hulk caseload, briefly involved with Samson and subsequently endangered or killed by Hulk-related events — the dossier flags an ethical category that Samson does not, in those years, treat as a category. He does not sleep with his patients; he is rigorous about that line. He does, however, repeatedly form intimacies with women he met *because of* a patient, in a workplace where the patient population and the civilian-adjacent population overlap heavily. The proper professional standard would have required more distance than he kept.

**Failure mode.** The losses, when they came, were processed as tragedies that happened to him rather than as foreseeable consequences of his proximity practices. The grief was real. The structural learning did not occur until Era 4.

**Leverage.** Held by their memories, in the chastened period. He revisits them in the privacy his sobriety now affords. No external party currently holds operational leverage from this set.

---

### Self-as-intimate (the cape, the hair, the body)

Listed last and listed deliberately. Samson's most stable intimate relationship across the entire record is with his own augmented body and the persona attached to it. He grooms the hair attentively. He maintains the physique at a level beyond clinical necessity. He selects costuming that displays both. The relationship has the rhythms of a partnership: he attends to it, he relapses into it after losses, he negotiates with it about how visible to be on a given day. When he loses powers, the depressive withdrawal that follows is *bereavement-coded* — not the loss of a tool but the loss of a presence.

**Failure mode.** As long as the body is the primary intimate, no human intimate can compete on terms he would notice losing. Betty was always going to lose to a partner who never said no and whose hair grew back.

**Leverage.** Held by anyone who can credibly threaten the body or the persona — which is why depowering events hit him harder than near-deaths, and why the *Fall of the Hulks* compromise took the form it did: not a threat to his life but a redesign of his augmentation, offered as enhancement. The bid was made to the partner, not the man, and the partner accepted before the man had finished reading the contract.

---

*End Section.*


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# POWERS, ABILITIES & THEIR LIMITS

## 6.1 Inventory and Mechanism

Leonard Samson's capability set divides cleanly into three strata: (a) the pre-gamma somatic and intellectual baseline, (b) the gamma-derived superhuman augmentation, and (c) the clinical/professional skill stack he built on top of both. The error most observers make - and which Samson himself encourages by costume and bearing - is to treat (b) as the primary asset. The record does not support that. The gamma is the loudest of the three and the least decisive; his baseline athletic gift and his clinical instrument are what have actually produced his on-page wins, including the one that matters (the Merged Hulk integration, achieved in a chair, sober, with a notepad).

### (a) Baseline somatic substrate

Samson was a competitive decathlete at the elite amateur tier before psychiatry - established in the early Thomas issues and reinforced quietly across decades by the way he *moves* on panel. The decathlon background is not flavor text; it is mechanically load-bearing. The ten-event athlete is selected for a specific cognitive-somatic profile: high baseline strength, high baseline endurance, exceptional proprioception, the ability to switch motor programs across radically different demands within minutes, and - distinctively - a tolerance for being merely *very good* at ten things rather than world-class at one. That tolerance shapes how he carries gamma augmentation: he does not fight like a power-bruiser who recently acquired strength; he fights like an athlete who happens to be very strong, with footwork, spacing, and tempo control most super-strong characters never develop. He throws weight from the hips. He recovers stance after a missed blow. He paces a long engagement. None of this is gamma. All of this is 1965-era track-and-field coaching written into the nervous system before he ever met Banner.

Resting parameters, inferred from longitudinal depiction: 6'4"-ish, ~190 lbs pre-gamma (lean decathlete build), reading 240-260 in costume across most eras as the gamma musculature thickens him. Resting heart rate low; thermoregulation excellent; sleep architecture - this is the surveillance-grade inference - almost certainly disturbed across the 90s-2000s on the basis of his drinking pattern and the visible eye/posture changes in late David and Pak issues.

### (b) Gamma augmentation

Acquired *Incredible Hulk* #141 via siphon-and-self-administer of energy drawn from Banner. The exposure was deliberate, single-source, and - critically - *Banner's own gamma*, which makes Samson's powers a derivative of Banner's in a way the published record never quite makes him reckon with. He is, mechanically, drinking from the same well as the patient he is supposed to be treating.

Observed parameters:

- **Strength:** Hovers around the 75-ton ceiling in his prime, lower at short-hair states, briefly higher (Class-100 adjacent) after the Leader's forced re-irradiation in *Fall of the Hulks*. Crucially, he does *not* scale with rage the way Banner does. His strength curve is flat - what you see at fight start is what you get at fight end. This is a significant tactical limit against anyone Hulk-class.
- **Durability:** Sufficient to trade blows with Hulk for short windows, insufficient to win those exchanges. The concussive record across forty years says so. He has been knocked unconscious by Banner in dozens of stories and has never put Banner down in a fair fight without an external assist (drug, machine, ally, manipulation).
- **Healing/recovery:** Above human baseline, well below Banner's. He has needed actual medical care after major fights more than once - he is not self-repairing on a Hulk timetable.
- **Stamina:** Genuinely elite. The decathlete substrate plus gamma metabolism gives him a fight-window measured in hours rather than minutes. This is one of his most underutilized assets and one he himself does not seem to value, because endurance does not photograph.
- **The hair gimmick:** Strength scales with hair length. Cut, he depowers; grown, he reactivates. The mechanism is *almost certainly* psychosomatic - a gamma mutagen finding a pre-existing identification with the Samson myth and routing the somatic expression through it. The clinical reading is that his body is doing what his self-concept tells it to do; the mythic name his parents gave him is operating as an embodied schema with biochemical consequences. No other gamma mutate has anything like this. It is bespoke to *him*, which means it is bespoke to his *psychology*, which means **the power is a symptom**.

### (c) Clinical skill stack

Board-eligible psychiatrist with a doctorate, decades of clinical practice, and the single most sophisticated case file in the Marvel Universe (Banner) as both his teacher and his trophy. His specific competencies, derived from on-page work:

- **Diagnostic interview.** Fast, fluent, accurate. Reads affect, posture, micro-expression, vocal prosody. Gets to formulation in one or two sessions where most clinicians need six.
- **Hypnotic technique.** Genuinely advanced. The Merged Hulk integration (*Incredible Hulk* #377) is not a parlor trick; it is sustained hypnotic work on a dissociative structure with three distinct alters and a trauma origin (Brian Banner). He executes it without supervision because there is no one qualified to supervise him on this case, which is itself a structural problem.
- **Trauma formulation.** He correctly identifies childhood abuse as the etiology of Banner's dissociation years before that became canon-default reading. This is real clinical instinct.
- **Crisis containment.** He can hold a decompensating gamma-mutate in a room and talk them down. He has done it for Betty, for Rick Jones, for a parade of secondary Hulks, and intermittently for Banner.
- **Forensic/consulting work.** Government-grade. SHIELD-, Army-, and later Initiative-cleared. He produces reports that hold up.
