What he *cannot* do clinically: supervise himself, refer out when the case is personal, maintain a frame when a patient triangulates him with a romantic interest, or stop himself from leaving the chair to enter the fight.

## 6.2 Range, Limits, and the Edges That Bite

The honest limit map:

- **Strength ceiling well below Banner's working range.** In any straight fight with a serious Hulk, he loses, and the published record is unambiguous about this. His career-long failure to internalize this datum is itself a behavioral finding.
- **No ranged offense.** No gamma blast, no projectile, no force effect. He fights at arm's length, which means every fight is a fight he has chosen to close into. He cannot disengage at distance; he cannot threaten at distance.
- **No stealth profile.** Six-foot-plus, green-haired, costumed, named. He cannot pass; he cannot ghost; he cannot observe a patient unobserved. This is a real clinical limitation - he has never been able to do shadow-assessment of Banner the way an unmarked colleague could - and it is downstream of a cosmetic choice he made and has never revisited.
- **Hair-dependence is exploitable.** Anyone who reads the file knows the haircut works. He has been depowered by blade, by surgical clipper, and by his own hand during depressive episodes. The vulnerability is public.
- **Mind-control susceptibility above population baseline.** He has been suborned, possessed, or impersonated more times than the gamma cohort average. The structural reason is almost certainly that his defense stack (intellectualization, grandiosity) is excellent against ordinary social pressure and poor against operators who flatter the grandiosity itself - the Leader's manipulation in *Fall of the Hulks* worked because it offered him exactly the framing of himself he already wanted.
- **Substance impairment.** Across the 90s-2000s window, his effective IQ in the chair and effective reaction time in the fight are both degraded by alcohol use he does not declare. This is a limit he installed in himself.
- **No tactical command experience.** He is a soloist. Put him on a team and he free-lances. Put him in charge of a team and he micromanages the part of the engagement he can personally see.
- **Countertransference blindness.** The most expensive limit in the file. He cannot run himself as a case. Every other limit on this list is downstream of this one.

## 6.3 Growth Curve

**Era 1 (1971-late 70s).** Raw gamma augmentation, athlete's technique, clinical credentials with limited applied range. Fights enthusiastically and badly - he closes too fast, swings too wide, underestimates Banner repeatedly. Clinical work is competent but conventional. The cape is louder than the doctor.

**Era 2 (80s-mid 90s, Mantlo through David).** The doctor finally catches up to the cape. He becomes - measurably - better at sitting in a chair than at throwing a punch, and his major contributions in this era come from the chair. The Merged Hulk arc is the high-water mark of his entire career and is achieved without a single punch he threw himself mattering. His fight technique is now polished, economical, recognizably the work of a forty-year-old former athlete who has learned to conserve - but the clinical work is what produces the result.

**Era 3 (late 90s-2000s, Jenkins/Casey/Pak).** Skill erosion under substance use and ethical drift. His diagnostics get sloppier; his fights get more theatrical and less effective; his alliances get worse. The Leader's intervention temporarily *raises* his strength ceiling and lowers everything else - he is more powerful and less competent simultaneously, which is the perfect mechanical expression of the psychological collapse.

**Era 4 (2010s onward, Parker, Ewing).** Diminished power, restored judgment. He is no longer the strongest version of himself and is finally the clearest. The fights are fewer; the consults are more careful; the chair is occupied properly. He has, in the surveillance-file sense, *aged into his actual instrument*.

## 6.4 How He Actually Uses It

**In the chair.** Leans forward, not back. Mirrors posture early in a session, breaks mirror deliberately when he wants to shift the patient's state. Uses his own size as a containing object - the patient is meant to feel that the room can hold whatever comes up because *he* can hold it. Hypnotic inductions are conversational rather than formal; he prefers a permissive Ericksonian frame to a directive one, which fits his self-image as collaborator rather than authority. Note-taking is minimal in session, extensive afterward - he relies on recall and writes long process notes within an hour of session end. (Inference from the consistency and accuracy of his later case formulations.)

**In the fight.** Closes distance immediately - he has no choice, no ranged tool. Opens with a grapple or a heavy committed strike rather than feeling the opponent out, because feeling out is a luxury his strength tier does not afford him against Hulk-class targets. Uses environment - walls, vehicles, terrain - more than most super-strong characters, again a decathlete's instinct for using the field. Talks throughout. The talking is partly tactical (he is genuinely trying to de-escalate Banner in most of their fights) and partly self-regulatory (he narrates to stay coherent under stress). Tires opponents rather than overpowering them when he can - his stamina edge is one of his few real advantages and he uses it semi-consciously.

**In consultation.** Writes well. Speaks better. Carries a room. Translates clinical material into actionable language for military and intelligence consumers without losing the clinical substance - a rare skill and the reason his contracts kept getting renewed even as his judgment deteriorated.

## 6.5 Signature Applications

- **The Banner integration (#377).** Sustained hypnotic work producing the Merged/Professor Hulk. His finest hour, achieved with the instrument he undervalues.
- **Crisis talk-downs of decompensating gamma mutates.** Repeated across decades. He is genuinely the best person in the world at walking into a room with a transformed Hulk-class patient and getting them to stop.
- **Forensic assessment for federal consumers.** Quiet, consistent, well-regarded.
- **The closing rush in combat.** When it works, it works because of the athlete's footwork, not the gamma musculature.
- **Public-facing exposition.** He can explain a gamma case to a press pool, a general, or a senator without compromising patient material or losing the room. This is a skill, and it is also a stage.

## 6.6 Symptom-as-Signature

Read across the whole file, the powers map one-to-one onto the pathology.

- **Green hair tied to strength** = the body literalizing a parental script. The mythic name installed by parents he never discusses becomes the somatic mechanism of his adult specialness. He is, biochemically, doing what he was told to be.
- **Cosmetic, unconcealable augmentation** = the exhibitionistic variant of narcissism made flesh. He cannot opt out of being seen. He chose, in #141, a power set that *requires* an audience.
- **Strength derived from his patient's gamma** = the rivalry encoded at the cellular level. Every power he has, he took from Banner.
- **No ranged offense, compulsion to close** = the interpersonal pattern (pursuit that does not modulate to feedback) expressed kinetically. He cannot stay at distance; he never could.
- **Flat strength curve, no rage scaling** = the affect-regulation profile (externally smooth, no big mood episodes) rendered as a power-stat. He does not have a berserk gear because he does not have a berserk gear.
- **Hair-cut vulnerability** = the fragile self-esteem under the grandiose presentation, made literal. A blade and ten seconds and he is ordinary, which is the thing he is most afraid of.
- **Susceptibility to flattering manipulation** = the countertransference blindness weaponized by hostile operators.
- **Peak clinical work performed sober, in a chair, on a patient larger than the performance** = the protective factor identified in the psychological section, demonstrated mechanically. When the case organizes him, the instrument works. When it does not, the instrument seeks an audience.

The summary finding: Samson's power set is not an asset bolted onto a clinician. It is the same disorder his clinical work is also an expression of, routed through a different output. The gamma did not change him. It published him.


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT
## Subject: SAMSON, Leonard — Ph.D., consulting psychiatrist; metahuman asset designation (variable, federal)

---

## 6.1 Decision-Making Architecture

Samson's decision-making is bimodal and the two modes are poorly integrated, which is itself the most exploitable feature of his operational profile.

**Mode A — Clinical Deliberation.** When operating inside a formal clinical frame (intake interview, structured assessment, hypnotic session, case conference, treatment-planning meeting with institutional witnesses), his decision process is methodical, hypothesis-driven, and slow. He runs a recognizable structure: (1) collateral gathering — chart review, prior treaters, family history when obtainable; (2) live observation across at least two settings; (3) provisional formulation written longhand, in a particular leather notebook he has carried in some form since residency, with a fountain pen, blue-black ink, left-margin-only notation; (4) intervention sequenced from least-invasive to most-invasive. In this mode his time-to-decision is measured in days to weeks. His judgment in this mode is genuinely excellent, his risk tolerance is conservative, and his documentation is meticulous to a degree that has stood up to multiple federal inquiries.

**Mode B — Operational/Combat Decision.** When the frame collapses — when a patient transforms, when a containment fails, when Betty Ross is in the room, when a camera is in the room — Samson's decision loop compresses to seconds and the deliberative apparatus from Mode A is not so much overridden as bypassed. He decides kinetically. The decision is almost always to *insert himself physically into the situation*, and the post-hoc rationalization is always Mode-A-styled. This is the signature: an action chosen by Mode B and then narrated by Mode A as if Mode A had chosen it. The seam between the two modes is where every catastrophic decision of his career lives — #141 is the prototype, *World War Hulk* and *Fall of the Hulks* are the mature expressions.

**Decision tells.** Before a Mode-B switch, observable precursors: (a) jargon density in his speech rises sharply — he begins to name the situation in DSM-adjacent terms aloud, audibly, to no one in particular; (b) he stops taking notes and caps the pen; (c) he removes his jacket if wearing one, or rolls sleeves to the elbow — a tell carried over from his decathlon days, a pre-exertion ritual; (d) he begins to refer to the patient or adversary in the third person even when they are present, a depersonalization that licenses force.

---

## 6.2 Methods — Clinical Tradecraft

His clinical method is a hybrid of mid-century dynamic psychiatry, hypnotic and ego-state work, and the pragmatic crisis-psychiatry he learned consulting at Gamma Base. Specific techniques he is documented to favor:

- **Hypnotic regression and ego-state integration.** His signature technique, refined over the Mantlo years and brought to full expression in the Banner integration of the late 1980s. He inducts with a slow vocal cadence, drops his pitch roughly a third of an octave, and uses a fixed-point visual induction with a small brass object he keeps in his desk drawer. Sessions run 90–110 minutes; he resists the standard 50-minute frame for this work and bills accordingly.
- **Structured psychobiography.** He has the patient construct a written chronology, year by year, with prompts for somatic memory. He uses this to map dissociative seams.
- **Provocation testing under controlled conditions.** Less defensible. He will deliberately introduce a known trigger in-session, with restraint protocols (or, in Banner's case, gamma-dampening field protocols) staged in advance, to observe state-shifts directly. This is genuine craft and also a covert satisfaction of his own appetite for spectacle.
- **Pharmacology** — he prescribes conservatively and reads pharmacology journals more carefully than the average psychotherapist of his cohort; he is not a medication-first clinician and is suspicious of psychiatrists who are.

What he does *not* do: group work (he cannot tolerate not being the central figure), couples work (his countertransference around marital triangles is uncontainable), or supervision of trainees beyond brief rotations (subordinates either adore him or are flattened by him; either outcome is bad for the trainee).

---

## 6.3 Methods — Field & Combat Tradecraft

In the field he is a *brawler with a clinician's eyes*. His combat method has not significantly evolved since the 1970s, which is itself a tell — a man with his pattern-recognition should have a more sophisticated kinetic repertoire after four decades.

- **Engagement preference.** Direct, frontal, conversational. He talks during fights, often in clinical register, sometimes effectively (he has de-escalated Banner mid-transformation more than once by addressing the dissociated ego-state by name) and sometimes catastrophically (the same technique applied to non-Banner combatants reads as condescension and escalates them).
- **Use of terrain.** Poor. He does not use cover. He does not flank. He stands in the open and trades.
- **Restraint posture.** When the goal is containment rather than incapacitation he favors grapples, bear hugs, and pin holds — a residue of his collegiate wrestling and decathlon background. He is genuinely skilled at this and has neutralized gamma-level threats without striking.
- **Force calibration.** Inconsistent. Under Mode-A control he is precise; under Mode-B he hits at his ceiling regardless of what the situation requires. The rationalization afterward is always proportionality language he does not actually apply in the moment.

---

## 6.4 Tradecraft — Information & Counter-Intelligence

This is his weakest operational domain and the one most consistently exploited against him.

- **OPSEC posture: low.** He uses his real name, his real credentials, and his real face. He is in the phone book. His clinical office addresses across the years have been a matter of public record because he insisted on accepting state insurance and federal contracts that required published practice locations.
- **Counter-surveillance: minimal.** He does not check tails. He does not vary routes (see §6.7). He has been impersonated, mind-controlled, and surgically altered against his will, each time partly because his baseline behavioral pattern is so legible that substitutes have been able to walk in his shoes for weeks before colleagues notice.
- **Document security: paradoxically strong** in one narrow channel. His personal case notebooks — the longhand leather-bound notebooks — have never, on the published record, been compromised. He carries the current volume on his person, stores filled volumes in a small fireproof safe in his residence whose combination is (per pattern) almost certainly a date associated with Betty Ross. He distrusts digital records for clinical material and his EMR usage is the bare federal minimum.
- **Susceptibility to social engineering.** High when the approach comes from (a) a woman presenting psychological need, (b) a peer flattering his integration work, or (c) an institutional voice offering him a larger platform. The Leader's manipulation of him in the *Fall of the Hulks* period exploited (b) and (c) simultaneously.

---

## 6.5 Resources & Finances

Samson is, by superhuman standards, *paid*. He is one of the few costumed operatives in the published record with a continuous W-2 income across his entire career.

- **Primary income streams, historically:** federal consulting contract (Gamma Base / Hulkbuster Base, then successor agencies; six-figure annual at minimum from the early 80s onward, with hazard riders); private psychiatric practice (small, deliberately under-marketed, premium rate); occasional academic appointments and lecture honoraria; book royalties from at least two clinical monographs on dissociative trauma in gamma-affected subjects, which sold modestly to the field and well to the public.
- **Income streams he has refused or under-pursued:** endorsement, ghost-written autobiography, talk-show circuit. He has been offered all of these repeatedly. He declines, and the declining is itself a narcissistic posture — he wants the *offers*, not the deals.
- **Spending pattern.** Above his means but not catastrophically. He carries debt. The debt is in three categories: a residential mortgage on a property larger than a single man needs; a vehicle pattern (mid-life European sedans, replaced every 3–4 years, always silver or graphite); and bar tabs that, aggregated across his late-90s/2000s peak, run into five figures annually at three or four regular establishments.
- **Insurance.** Maintained meticulously — malpractice carried at the maximum the carriers will write for a metahuman provider, life insurance underwritten at exotic rates and contested at every claim event (he has been "killed" enough times to have generated case law on the matter, mostly in his insurers' favor).
- **No offshore structure, no shell entities, no asset concealment.** A federal forensic accountant could close his books in a week. This is consistent with the rest of the profile: he is grandiose, not criminal.

---

## 6.6 Infrastructure

- **Clinical infrastructure.** A small private office, historically located within reasonable distance of whichever facility currently houses the Banner case file. He keeps the office spare: two chairs, a couch (used), a desk, the brass fixation object, a single bookshelf curated for the patient's eye more than his own (he rotates titles based on who is scheduled that week — a tell). A single framed credential on the wall, never more.
- **Government infrastructure.** Standing access at multiple federal sites, badge-level varying with administration. He has had clearances pulled and reinstated at least twice. Each reinstatement was negotiated personally; he does not use counsel for these.
- **Personal infrastructure.** One residence, owned. Gym membership maintained continuously since residency — he trains five to six mornings a week, has done so for forty years, and the gym is the most stable institution in his life. The current gym, whatever city he is in, is selected by a single criterion: it has a serious Olympic-lift platform. He still cleans and snatches in his 60s/70s of in-universe published time, sub-maximally but with technique that draws stares.
- **Support network — professional.** A short list of trusted colleagues in academic psychiatry, mostly women his own age or older, none of whom he has slept with, all of whom he calls "Doctor" in conversation even after decades. This is the healthiest part of his life.
- **Support network — personal.** Effectively none outside the professional list. No close male friends on the published record. Banner is the closest thing, which is the diagnosis.

---

## 6.7 Patterns of Action — Routine & Routes

A surveillance file on Samson is easy to build because his routine is regular to the point of liturgical.

- **Morning.** Wake 0500–0530. Coffee, black, French press, two cups. Reads two newspapers in print, one general and one financial, and at least the abstracts of one journal — he subscribes to four. Gym 0600–0730. Shower at the gym. Breakfast at one of two or three establishments near the gym, always the same booth or stool, always greeted by name, always tips 22% in cash.
- **Clinical day.** Patients booked 0900–1500 in 90-minute blocks (not 50), with a deliberate two-hour midday gap. The gap is nominally for notes; it is functionally for a long walk, alone, during which he conducts the actual cognitive work of formulation. The walking is a tell — *no notebook, no phone in hand, head down, lips moving slightly*. He is rehearsing. If you want to read his mind, walk behind him at 1230.
- **Afternoon.** Administrative, supervision (rare), correspondence. He answers letters by hand, on personal stationery, longer than necessary.
- **Evening.** This is the unstable variable. In stable periods: home, reading, asleep by 2230. In unstable periods (the late-90s/2000s peak): one of three bars, arriving 1900–2000, departing variably, sometimes accompanied, more often alone. The bars share a profile — dim, wood, no televisions, bartenders who know not to ask.
- **Route patterns.** Walks where possible; in larger cities uses cabs over rideshare (a generational tell and also a minor counter-surveillance instinct he does not himself recognize as one); drives only on weekends and for travel to federal sites. Drives fast and well.
- **Travel.** Coach class on government contracts unless the contract specifies otherwise. Business class on his own dime, single malt at altitude, reads case files in the air with the file turned away from the aisle — the *one* OPSEC behavior he performs consistently.

---

## 6.8 Pattern of Action — Crisis & Deployment

When a Hulk-class event breaks, his deployment pattern is so consistent it constitutes an algorithm:

1. **Contact within 90 minutes** from a federal liaison, almost always by landline to his office or residence — agencies that know him know not to text.
2. **Verbal commitment immediate**, conditions stated for the record and rarely enforced (he stipulates "consulting role only" and then does not stay in that role).
3. **Travel within four hours**, packed bag pre-staged at the residence — clothes, the current notebook, the brass object, a flask whose contents and presence vary with era.
4. **On-site behavior:** demands the case file, reads it in front of whoever provided it, makes a show of disagreeing with at least one prior assessment. This is dominance display, not analysis; the disagreement is almost always minor.
5. **First contact with the subject:** alone if permitted, two-person if not. He does not wear the costume into first contact when he can avoid it — the one Mode-A operational instinct that has remained intact.
6. **Escalation to Mode B** occurs at a predictable trigger point: when the subject does not respond to verbal intervention within roughly 20–30 minutes, or when a third party (especially Betty Ross or a uniformed officer) enters the room.

---

## 6.9 Signature Operational Tells

Compiled, with collection priority for any file:

- **Vocal cadence drop and jargon density rise** as the Mode-A/Mode-B switch approaches. *Audio surveillance is the single most valuable channel on this subject.*
- **Capping of the fountain pen** with a specific two-handed motion before standing.
- **Rolling sleeves to the elbow**, left sleeve first, always.
- **Third-person reference** to a present interlocutor as the depersonalization sets in.
- **Reflexive grooming touch** to the hair — a single pass of the right hand from temple back to crown — when narcissistically wounded. The frequency of this gesture in any given week is a reliable proxy for his stress level.
- **Use of patients' full names with credentials** ("Dr. Banner," "Ms. Ross") in moments he is asserting professional frame against personal feeling — i.e., when the personal feeling is winning.
- **The 1230 walk.** Same time, same direction out of the office, variable return path. If displaced from it for three days running, expect either an acute case or a personal crisis.
- **Bar selection criteria** (dim, wood, no TV) — narrow enough that in any city he has visited twice, the candidate venues number under five.
- **Refusal of rideshare and refusal of social media** — both flagged not as sophistication but as generational and characterological rigidity that *happens* to create OPSEC value.
- **The notebook on his person at all times**, including in combat. He has been knocked unconscious with it in an inside jacket pocket on multiple occasions. Recovery of any current notebook would constitute the most consequential intelligence haul possible on this subject and on, by extension, every patient he has ever treated. *He knows this. He carries it anyway.* That is the entire man in one fact.

---

## 6.10 Net Operational Assessment

Samson is a high-value, low-difficulty collection target and a high-skill, medium-reliability operational asset. His tradecraft is essentially the tradecraft of a serious clinician who has been allowed, for institutional and personal reasons, to walk into combat without ever acquiring the discipline that combat requires. His best work is done seated. His worst work is done standing. The gap between the two has been the through-line of his career and remains the axis along which any actor — friendly, hostile, or therapeutic — should plan engagement.


## Worldview & Operational Code

# WORLDVIEW & OPERATIONAL CODE: LEONARD SAMSON, Ph.D.

## I. The Cosmological Frame — How He Reads Reality

Samson is, at the deepest layer, a **materialist with a theatrical streak**. His professional training and his life-defining transformation both reinforce a single first principle: *mind and body are the same object viewed from two angles, and both are susceptible to intervention.* He does not believe in souls. He does not believe in irreducible character. He believes - and this is one of the most consequential beliefs in his operational code - that **a sufficiently skilled clinician with sufficient access can reorganize any psyche**, including (the unacknowledged corollary) his own, if he ever chose to apply the apparatus inward. The Merged Hulk integration is the canonical proof he carries with him; it is the secular miracle that validates his entire worldview. Once a man has fused three dissociated identities into one functioning Gestalt by talk and trance, he is not going to be humble about the limits of psychiatry.

Layered on top of the materialism is a **mythic register he absorbed before he could refuse it**. The name is not decorative. To be told from childhood that you are the strongman, the chosen one, the figure whose strength is in his hair, is to be handed a script in which the universe has *roles* and you have been pre-cast in the lead. He intellectually rejects this — he would say so under direct questioning, and mean it — but he behaves as if life is a series of episodes in which he is the protagonist and the supporting cast (Banner, Betty, the Hulkbuster Base personnel, eventually the Leader and MODOK) exist to bring out facets of him. The materialist and the mythic coexist uneasily; the materialist runs his clinical work, the mythic runs his life.

He reads the world, accordingly, as **a structured field of cases**. Everything resolves into a presenting problem, an etiology, a treatment plan, and a prognosis. People are not strangers; they are *not-yet-formulated*. Crises are not chaos; they are *acute presentations*. Even cosmic events — gamma incidents, alien incursions, Hulk rampages — get filed under a frame that asks first "what is the underlying pathology?" This is genuinely useful: it allows him to function calmly where others freeze. It is also a totalizing lens that converts every encounter into asymmetric expert/object relations, with him as the expert. He cannot meet anyone as a simple peer for long. The frame keeps reasserting itself.

## II. Conflict — What It Is, What It Means, How It Is Resolved

Samson's stated view of conflict is **diagnostic**: conflict is information; it is the system showing you where the dysfunction lives; the right response to conflict is curiosity, formulation, intervention. He can give this speech beautifully and he believes it.

His operational view of conflict is **performative**. Conflict is the arena in which the protagonist proves the protagonist's centrality. Across forty years of canon, his behavioral record under conflict shows a remarkable consistency: when conflict can be resolved through talk in which he is the dominant talker, he resolves it through talk; when it cannot, he resolves it through *being the largest physical object present*. He does not, as a matter of repeated behavior, choose the de-escalating exit even when it is available. He stays in the room. He stays in the fight. He stays at the bedside. The stated reason is duty; the functional reason is that exits feel like abdication and abdication feels like erasure.

He believes conflict is **resolvable in principle**, which separates him from the genuinely tragic temperament. Banner is a problem to be solved. The Hulk is a problem to be solved. Even his own decompensation, when he finally registers it in the late period, becomes a problem to be solved. This is an optimistic — even a humanist — premise. It is also why he keeps reaching for the next intervention long past the point where reaching has become the harm.

He distinguishes sharply, in his own internal map, between **legitimate adversary** (someone who has presented a problem he can work) and **illegitimate adversary** (someone who has refused the frame). He is generous to the first and contemptuous of the second. The Leader, in his read, is the second kind — not because the Leader is evil but because the Leader will not be a *patient*, will not accept the asymmetry that Samson's worldview requires. This is one reason the eventual partnership/manipulation during *Fall of the Hulks* lands so hard: it is the worldview-violation at the center of his career.

## III. Control — Who Has It, Who Should, How It Is Won

His baseline belief is that **control should accrue to competence, and competence is largely demonstrable**. He is, in this sense, a small-c credentialist meritocrat: degrees matter, training matters, track record matters, and once those are established the credentialed actor should be granted operational latitude. He resents oversight by people he considers less qualified — military brass with no clinical training, bureaucratic gatekeepers, journalists — and he extends courtesy to peers whose credentials he respects (early Banner, before the rivalry calcified; certain SHIELD medical personnel; later, grudgingly, the Ewing-era figures who have seen what he has seen).

Underneath the meritocratic frame is something more primitive: **control is the absence of being acted upon**. The originating gamma self-administration is, read structurally, an act of refusing to be the small figure in someone else's experiment. He was the consultant; he made himself the subject; he made himself the agent. Every subsequent power-seeking episode replays this. Loss of powers is intolerable to him not because the powers are useful — he is a credentialed psychiatrist, he has a career without them — but because powerlessness reactivates the unbearable position of *being a thing in someone else's story*.

He believes in **institutional control as a vehicle**, not as a value. The Army, Gamma Base, SHIELD, government contracts — these are platforms. He uses them. He does not love them. When they constrain him he routes around them, usually by invoking clinical privilege or by deploying himself to the field faster than the chain of command can stop him. He has never, on the record, refused a contract for principled reasons. He has frequently accepted contracts that a more cautious clinician would have declined. The platforms make him larger; that is their function.

Control over self is the **conspicuous gap**. He believes, theoretically, in self-mastery; he teaches it; he models it in session. He does not practice it consistently outside of clinical hours. The alcohol use is the visible marker; the relationship pattern with Betty is the structural marker; the recurring re-irradiations are the somatic marker. Each instance is a small admission that the locus of control over Leonard Samson is not reliably Leonard Samson.

## IV. Trust — How It Is Extended, How It Is Withdrawn

Samson extends trust **fast and shallow**. First-contact rapport is one of his real skills; patients, witnesses, colleagues, and reporters routinely come away from a first meeting with the impression of having been *seen*. He is not faking this. The skill is real and the attention is real for the duration of the encounter. What is also real is the *thinness* of what gets stored afterward: most people he meets do not become, in his internal map, full subjects. They become well-formulated case-objects he can recall accurately and care about generically.

Deep trust — the kind that requires sustained mutual vulnerability — he extends to **almost no one**. Banner occupies a slot that approximates it, but the slot is corrupted by rivalry; Betty occupies a slot that approximates it, but the slot is corrupted by pursuit. There is no canonical figure he confides in as a peer without agenda. The absence is structural, not accidental. To trust someone deeply would require him to be the smaller party in a relationship, and his organization will not permit that for long.

He withdraws trust along **predictable triggers**: being condescended to professionally, being eclipsed by Banner, being told his pursuit of Betty is inappropriate, being asked to step aside from a case he has claimed. The withdrawal is rarely overt — he does not stage breakups or denunciations — it manifests as cooling, as redirection, as the quiet recategorization of the offender from *peer* to *obstacle*.

He trusts **institutions provisionally and contracts more than persons**. A signed engagement, a clinical privilege, a security clearance — these he treats as bankable. Verbal assurances from individuals he treats as advisory only. This is, in part, professional habit; it is also a self-protective measure against the dependency he will not name.

Self-trust is high in the domains where it is earned (clinical formulation, hypnotic work, physical courage under fire) and **catastrophically high in the domains where it is not** (his own countertransference, his own substance use, his own susceptibility to manipulation). The *Fall of the Hulks* compromise was made possible precisely because Samson trusted his own judgment in territory where he had no calibration and no supervision.

## V. Risk — How It Is Calculated, How It Is Discounted

The formal risk calculus he would articulate in a case conference is sound: expected harm weighted by probability, balanced against expected benefit, with explicit attention to reversibility and consent. He teaches this. He applies it to other people's decisions competently.

The functional risk calculus he applies to himself **systematically discounts personal cost and inflates personal upside**. The original gamma exposure is a textbook case: an experimental, single-dose, irreversible self-modification with no controls, no peer review, no informed-consent process anyone but him supervised, undertaken on the spot. A clinician of his training cannot do that under any defensible risk framework. He did it. The discounting is not a one-time aberration; it recurs at every power-loss/re-acquisition cycle, at every late-night decision to drive impaired to a call, at every acceptance of a compromised contract.

Two specific distortions drive the discounting:

First, an **invulnerability heuristic** generated by the body. Olympic-athlete proprioception plus gamma augmentation gives him decades of evidence that his body absorbs punishment, and he generalizes from somatic invulnerability to broader invulnerability — including invulnerability to manipulation, to addiction, to professional ruin. The body keeps cashing the checks the rest of him is writing, until it doesn't.

Second, a **protagonist heuristic**. He behaves as though the universe has a low base rate of letting him fail catastrophically. Forty years of stories in which he has survived everything he should not have survived have, paradoxically, reinforced this. The chastened late-era figure is the one who has finally updated the prior.

Risk to others he calculates more carefully — usually. The exception is the standing case: in Banner's vicinity, his self-other risk calibration breaks down because the rivalry contaminates the formulation. He has repeatedly chosen interventions that put Banner at greater risk than a non-conflicted clinician would have chosen, and rationalized those choices as therapeutic necessity.

## VI. Authority, Hierarchy, and Legitimacy

He recognizes three kinds of legitimate authority: **competence**, **credential**, and **case-relevant standing** (you may speak about this case because you are involved in it). He does not recognize legitimacy on the basis of rank alone, wealth alone, charisma alone, or tradition. Military hierarchies he treats as administrative; he respects individual officers whose competence he has observed and ignores the rank structure when it inconveniences a clinical decision.

He recognizes one informal authority that overrides the others: **the authority of the most acute presenting problem in the room**. When someone is in crisis, that person organizes the space, and the appropriate response is to address them. This is good clinical instinct and it is also why he keeps walking into traps: the most acute presenting problem can be staged, and Samson does not have a strong defensive read against staged crises.

His own authority he locates in the **doctorate plus the demonstrated track record plus the body**. Strip any of the three and the remaining two carry him; strip two and he becomes brittle. The Ewing-era figure who has been stripped of all three at various points is recognizably the same man, but quieter, because he has had to find a different basis for standing and has not entirely succeeded.

## VII. Sex, Romance, and the Erotics of the Case

He believes, officially, in **bright clinical boundaries**. He would teach a graduate seminar on dual relationships and he would teach it well. He believes, functionally, that **the rules apply more loosely to him because his self-monitoring is better than other people's**. This is the central professional-ethical defect of his life and he has never reckoned with it on the page.

Romance, in his code, is **pursuit** — sustained, articulate, attentive, escalating pursuit, in which the pursued party's resistance is read as information to be addressed rather than as a decision to be honored. He does not experience this as predatory because he does not experience it as coercive; he experiences it as the legitimate work of demonstrating his suitability. Forty years of Betty Ross is the documentation. He has never publicly updated the model.

Sex he treats as **incidental to attachment** in his stated philosophy and as **confirmation of standing** in his behavior. Being chosen sexually by the right person would, in his internal economy, settle a question that no amount of professional success has settled.

## VIII. Money, Status, and the Material World

He is **indifferent to money as money** and acutely attuned to **money as proxy for institutional access**. He has never been depicted pursuing wealth; he has been depicted repeatedly pursuing contracts, appointments, clearances, and platforms. The material lifestyle is comfortable, unostentatious for a man of his profile, professionally appointed (good office, good equipment, good books) rather than personally luxurious.

Status he reads carefully. He knows the hierarchy of his profession, knows where he sits in it, knows which conferences matter and which credentials open which doors. He is not above name-dropping when it serves a case. He is above social climbing for its own sake; the climb has to serve the work or the self-image.

## IX. Time, Mortality, and the Long Frame

He thinks in **case-arcs**, which are measured in months to years, and in **clinical careers**, which are measured in decades. He does not think much, on the page, about deeper time or cosmic frames; the materialist register provides no consolation there and the mythic register he won't examine. Death he has met (his own, briefly) and it has not produced the philosophical revision one might expect — partly because the death was framed by external manipulation rather than by acceptance, partly because his frame does not include a robust position on mortality and he has not built one since.

The late-period chastening is the closest he comes to a long-frame revision: a recognition that **the career has a shape**, that the shape has been partly tragic, that some of the choices were not the choices of the man he believed himself to be. This is the beginning of wisdom in him. It is not yet a worldview.

## X. His Place in the Order of Things — The Operational Code in One Page

Stripped to its operating premises, Samson's code reads:

1. **The world is a field of cases.** Every encounter has a formulation.
2. **I am qualified to formulate.** My training and track record entitle me to operate.
3. **Competence is the basis of legitimate authority.** Mine is real.
4. **Being acted upon is intolerable; being the actor is the baseline state.** Whenever the first threatens, restore the second.
5. **The body is the brand and the proof.** Maintain it, display it, deploy it.
6. **Banner is the defining case and the defining rival, and both at once is fine.** I can hold the contradiction.
7. **Betty is the standing question that the rest of the life is answering.** Pursuit is the answer until the answer changes.
8. **Substances, contracts, and irradiations are tools.** I am not the kind of person who is used by his tools.
9. **My countertransference is unusually well-managed.** Trust my read.
10. **The protagonist survives.** The base rate favors me.

Items 1–3 are largely true and have produced real good. Items 4–6 are the engine of both the achievement and the harm. Items 7–9 are the lies he tells himself in the voice of the truths he tells other people. Item 10 is the prior that catastrophe has been trying, with mixed success, to update.

The late-era figure is the one who has finally begun to suspect that **the operational code itself is a case**, and that the clinician most qualified to formulate it is the one most disqualified from doing so alone. Whether he ever submits to that supervision — whether he lets another mind hold his — is the open question of his remaining record.


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# MORAL & ETHICAL FRAMEWORK
## Subject: SAMSON, Leonard — Ph.D., Psy.D. (clinical), gamma-augmented

---

## 6.1 The Professed Code vs. The Enacted Code

Samson **says**, consistently across five decades of recorded interviews, press appearances, court testimony, and on-record clinical notation, that he holds to a fairly orthodox American medical-ethical position circa 1970s training: do no harm, informed consent, confidentiality, no dual relationships, no exploitation of the transference, beneficence as prime directive, autonomy of the patient as inviolable. He is articulate about these principles. He teaches them. He has, in published academic writing on gamma-trauma and dissociation, lectured colleagues on them. He believes he keeps them.

He does not.

The **enacted** code is narrower, more honest, and considerably stranger. Reverse-engineered from forty years of behavior, it reduces to roughly six operative rules — none of which he has ever stated aloud, and several of which he would deny if confronted:

1. **The patient's welfare matters, and ranks below the integrity of my role as the one fixing the patient.** When the two diverge, the role wins. Documented in the #141 self-irradiation (taking the gamma he had just drained from Banner was not in Banner's treatment plan), in his repeated re-insertion into Banner's case after every recusal that ethics would have required, and in the *Fall of the Hulks* period when, even compromised, his rationalizations were therapeutic in vocabulary.
2. **Force is permissible when speech has failed, and I am the correct person to apply it.** He does not believe in superheroic vigilantism in the abstract. He believes in *his* superheroic interventions, specifically, because they are framed as clinical extensions. The cape is, in his self-narrative, a house call.
3. **My judgment about Bruce Banner supersedes Bruce Banner's judgment about Bruce Banner.** This is the operative paternalism, and it is the one line he has never publicly defended because he has never publicly admitted to holding it.
4. **Romantic pursuit of Betty Ross is not a boundary violation because my feelings are sincere.** The category error — sincerity as ethical license — is foundational, recurrent, and untouched by feedback.
5. **Loss of capacity is loss of self, and reacquiring capacity by ethically irregular means is therefore self-preservation, which is permissible.** Every re-irradiation he has voluntarily undergone after a depowering has been justified internally on this ground.
6. **I will not kill. I will not torture. I will not betray a patient to a third party for money.** These are real. They have held under significant pressure. They are the floor of the code, and they are why the *Fall of the Hulks* turn required external neurological tampering to manufacture — it could not be produced by argument alone.

The distance between the professed and the enacted is the diagnostic terrain of this section.

---

## 6.2 Bright Lines That Have Held

It is worth being precise about what Samson *will not* do, because the catalogue is real and it is the substrate that makes the rest of the file tragic rather than merely sordid.

- **He will not kill in cold blood.** Combat lethality under duress has occurred; premeditated killing has not. When the Leader's operations in the late 2000s required lethal action, Samson required surgical intervention to perform it — and the post-resurrection record shows the act ate at him in a way the rest of the turn did not.
- **He will not break clinical confidentiality for money or for state interest alone.** He has broken it for what he construed as patient safety (Banner, repeatedly), and for what he construed as world safety (also Banner), but not for paycheck or pressure. The SHIELD contracts he accepted in the late 90s were structured by him to permit consultation while preserving — on paper, at least — privileged material. The paper held; the spirit did not.
- **He will not testify against a patient in a criminal proceeding.** Asked four separate times across the published record. Refused four times. This refusal has cost him work and standing and he has paid it without complaint.
- **He will not sexually engage a current patient.** Betty Ross is the controlling instance: he wanted her, pursued her, and — critically — never, on record, while she was formally his patient or his patient's spouse in a treatment frame, attempted physical consummation. The pursuit was relentless and inappropriate and well over the line of professional propriety in every other respect, but the specific carnal line did not get crossed. He gets exactly that much credit and not a dram more.
- **He will not torture for information.** He has interrogated. He has used his physical presence to intimidate. He has not crossed into deliberate infliction of pain for extraction, even when operational logic suggested it. This is unusual in his cohort and worth noting.
- **He will not harm a child or use one as leverage.** Untested often, but the few times the question arose his response was immediate and unambiguous.

These are not nothing. A worse man with the same powers and the same insecurities would be a war criminal. Samson is not. The floor of the code is structural — it predates the gamma, it is connected to the genuine ethical formation of his medical training, and it has survived ego decompensation, alcoholism, mind control, and resurrection. Note this: when external manipulators wanted to weaponize him, they could not simply persuade him. They had to *operate on his brain*. The code resisted argument.

---

## 6.3 The Fractures: Where the Code Breaks, Predictably

### 6.3.1 The Banner Exception

The single largest, oldest, and most consistent fracture is everything to do with Bruce Banner. Samson's behavior toward Banner — therapeutically, romantically, professionally, physically — violates standards he would unhesitatingly enforce on any other clinician. He has:

- treated a patient with whose spouse (then fiancée, then wife, then ex-wife, then wife again) he was in active erotic pursuit, across decades, without recusing;
- experimented on that patient with techniques he had not validated, in conditions of suboptimal consent;
- inserted himself into combat with that patient repeatedly, each time framing the assault as continued treatment;
- accepted government contracts whose explicit purpose was containment of that patient, while presenting himself to the patient as a treating clinician;
- written and lectured publicly about that patient's case in ways that any IRB would have flagged.

He would suspend a graduate student for any one of these. He has done all of them. The rationalization is always the same shape: *the case is unique, the stakes are civilizational, the patient is also my friend, ordinary rules assume ordinary situations.* This is true enough to be unfalsifiable and false enough to be the central ethical lesion of his life.

### 6.3.2 The Betty Exception

Pursuit of a married woman — across her marriage, after her death, after her resurrection, after her transformation, after every conceivable signal — is in his frame *romantic constancy*. In any other man's case file he would name it limerence, would name it intrusion, would gently suggest that the pursuit was about the pursuer. He has never said this about himself. The fracture is sealed by sincerity: because his feelings are real, the conduct is exempted. This is the same logic abusers use, and Samson is not an abuser — but he is using the logic, and he has used it for forty years.

### 6.3.3 The Self-Irradiation Pattern

Each voluntary re-exposure to gamma after a depowering has been justified on operational grounds (the world needs me back at strength) but is, structurally, an addict's relapse rationalized as duty. The ethical content is: *I am permitted to do to my own body what I would not permit a patient to do to theirs.* He has, in published clinical work, written against self-experimentation. He continues to self-experiment. The contradiction is uninspected.

### 6.3.4 The Drinking Years

From roughly the mid-1990s through the *World War Hulks* collapse, Samson treated patients while intoxicated or proximally intoxicated on multiple documented occasions. He drove. He flew. He fought. He prescribed. By his own published standards this is malpractice; by any state board's standards it is grounds for license revocation. He concealed it competently and was never reported. The ethical violation here is not the disease — addiction is not a moral failing — but the **active concealment from colleagues, supervisors, and patients of a condition he knew impaired his judgment**. That is the breach, and it is the one he has, in the Ewing-era material, come closest to acknowledging.

### 6.3.5 The Contract Drift

Across the late 1990s and 2000s, Samson accepted federal contracts whose terms he did not fully read, whose paymasters he did not fully vet, and whose objectives he assumed aligned with his own clinical mission because the people across the table flattered his sense of importance. He was not bought. He was *recruited through his vanity*, which is a different and slipperier compromise. By the time of *Fall of the Hulks* the institutional capture was deep enough that hostile actors could exploit the existing pipework. He bears responsibility for having built the pipework.

---

## 6.4 The Hierarchy in Action: How He Decides

When Samson's principles collide — and they collide constantly, because he holds incompatible commitments — the **operative priority order**, derived from behavior, is:

1. **Preservation of his role as the person solving the problem.** If a course of action would mean stepping aside, he will not take it, regardless of whether stepping aside is the correct ethical move.
2. **Prevention of mass-casualty events.** Real and load-bearing. He has thrown himself at threats he could not beat to slow them down for civilians. This is not performance; the early issues are full of moments where no audience was present and he did it anyway.
3. **Protection of Betty Ross specifically.** Ranks above general patient welfare. Ranks above his own safety. Ranks, troublingly, above Banner's autonomy when the two come into conflict.
4. **Protection of Banner specifically** — as patient, as friend, as the object of his rivalry. He will fight for Banner against the state and against the wider hero community when those try to destroy rather than treat. He will fight Banner himself when he judges Banner a threat. The two postures coexist without his noticing the tension.
5. **General clinical duty to other patients.** Real but secondary; in scheduling conflicts, Banner-related and Betty-related demands always win.
6. **Institutional loyalty (Army, SHIELD, later state actors).** Instrumental. He will break it without much agony when it conflicts with 1–4.
7. **Personal physical safety.** Genuinely low priority. He has walked into beatings he knew he could not win. The courage is not in doubt; the question is whether the courage is in service of ethics or of the self-image of the man who would do that.

Note what is **missing** from this ranking: any principled position on the use of state violence against gamma-mutates, on the carceral handling of enhanced individuals, on the ethics of gamma research as a field. He is a foremost authority and he has no settled view. His positions are reactive to whichever case is in front of him and which of the above priorities it implicates. This is not nuance; it is the absence of a developed political ethics, in a man whose work makes such an ethics necessary.

---

## 6.5 Shifts Over Time

### Era 1 (1971 – c. 1980): The Confident Code

Young Samson believes the professed code and believes he keeps it. The contradictions are present from the first issue but unintegrated — he can take Banner's gamma and pursue Banner's woman and call himself an ethical clinician in the same breath because the cognitive machinery for self-suspicion has not yet been built. The ethical errors of this era are committed in good conscience, which makes them more dangerous, not less.

### Era 2 (c. 1980 – c. 1996): The Mastery Era

Real therapeutic work — the Mantlo groundwork, the David integration — produces real ethical maturation in the technical domain. He becomes a better clinician. He becomes a better colleague. He develops something like genuine humility about *cases* if not about himself. The Banner integration is performed with patience and respect that earlier Samson could not have mustered. **In this era the code is at its tightest and the gap between professed and enacted is at its narrowest.** It is also the era he is happiest. The two facts are connected.

### Era 3 (c. 1996 – 2010): The Drift

Drinking, ego injury (Banner's marriage, the Merged Hulk's eventual fracture, his own irrelevance to the new generation of gamma stories), and institutional capture combine. The code begins to bend on the same axes it always had — Banner, Betty, self-irradiation — but now without the counterweight of the mastery work. He stops being able to tell the difference between his clinical judgment and his hurt feelings. The *Fall of the Hulks* turn is the terminus: an externally-induced collapse acting on a fault line he had spent fifteen years widening himself.

### Era 4 (post-resurrection, *Immortal Hulk* and after): The Chastened Code

He has, on the available evidence, done some real work. The drinking appears to be in remission. The pursuit of Betty has finally modulated to feedback. The relationship to Banner is conducted with more recusal and less rivalry, though the rivalry has not been extinguished, only stabled. Most importantly: **he has begun, for the first time in the record, to suspect himself.** The hypervigilance about his own motives that he should have had at thirty is arriving at sixty. It is late. It is not nothing.

The code in this era is *smaller* than the code of Era 1, in the sense that he claims less and commits to less; and *larger* in the sense that what he claims, he actually keeps. He has stopped writing checks his character cannot cash. For a man whose besetting sin was the inflation of his own ethical self-image, this contraction is the moral achievement of his late career.

---

## 6.6 The Honest Summary

Leonard Samson is a man with a real conscience, real principles, and a real capacity for ethical conduct, who spent the first thirty years of his professional life systematically exempting himself from the rules he believed in because he could not tolerate not being the exception. The bright lines held — he did not kill, did not sell out patients, did not become the thing his manipulators tried to make him. The middle terrain was corrupted throughout by a category of error he could not see, in which sincere feeling licensed inappropriate conduct and clinical framing licensed personal grievance.

The code is best understood as a real ethical structure carrying a parasitic exception clause keyed to two proper nouns (Banner, Ross) and one self-referential predicate (the necessity of his own centrality). Remove the exception clause and you have a competent and honorable clinician. The clause is forty years of his life.

He knows this now. He did not know it then. The knowing is the only restitution available, and to his credit he has, late, begun to make it.


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# COMMUNICATIONS & LINGUISTIC PROFILE: LEONARD SAMSON, Ph.D.

## 6.1 Baseline Register and Vocal Architecture

Subject's speaking voice, across forty years of recorded encounters, is a trained baritone in the upper-chest register - resonant, deliberately warm, with the slight over-articulation common to men who took elocution seriously at some point (likely graduate-school presentation training layered atop a decathlete's breath control). He projects effortlessly without seeming to project; in clinical settings he modulates *down*, in combat and press contexts he modulates *up*, and the differential is approximately eight to twelve decibels, which is theatrical. He does not have a regional accent that survives scrutiny - the vowels are scrubbed, Midwestern-default, the kind of English a man chooses rather than inherits. This is itself a tell: it is the speech of someone who decided early that where he came from would not appear in how he sounded.

Cadence is medium-fast with deliberate, structurally-placed slowdowns. He uses the pause as a clinician uses the pause - to invite a patient to fill silence - but he also uses it *on himself*, mid-sentence, when he wants the next clause to land as insight rather than opinion. The pause-before-the-noun is one of his most consistent tics: *"What you're describing, Bruce, is - **[beat]** - **grief.**"* This is a learned tool deployed authentically; it is also a habit he cannot turn off in non-clinical contexts, where it reads as condescension.

Breath: long phrases on single breaths, the legacy of an athlete's diaphragm. He almost never trails off; sentences land. In moments of genuine distress, this control fractures first - the sentences shorten before the content changes.

## 6.2 Register Shifts by Context

**Clinical setting (Banner, other patients, formal evaluations).** The register most controlled, the diction most precise, the jargon paradoxically *least* dense - he knows that jargon at a patient is iatrogenic. He uses second-person openings ("What I'm hearing is…", "Walk me through…", "Stay with that for a second"), present-tense framing, and a deliberate reduction in his own physical size: he sits, he leans back, he keeps his hands visible and still. Verbal interruptions drop to near-zero. This is the version of him that earns its salary.

**Peer/professional setting (other doctors, SHIELD consults, conference contexts).** Jargon density spikes hard. This is where he names defenses by Latin/Greek root, where he cites - by issue and year - the literature, where he stops using the patient's first name and starts using "the subject." It is also where he is most likely to credit himself in the passive voice ("the integration was successfully effected"), a syntax that lets the achievement happen without an "I" he would have to defend.

**Combat/operational setting.** Compressed, declarative, military-cadence. He drops articles ("Going high - cover the south end"), uses last names, issues commands in the imperative without softening. The clinical voice vanishes entirely. There is a transitional phenomenon worth noting: he often physically squares his shoulders in the half-second before this register kicks in, which is observable on tape.

**Press/public-facing.** Performative warmth. Smile audibly present in the voice. He uses the listener's name more than necessary. He delivers prepared lines as if they had just occurred to him - a politician's trick. He laughs at his own setup lines, briefly and low, before the punchline lands. He name-drops modestly ("when I was working with Bruce…") in a way calibrated to register as both intimacy and credential.

**Intimate/romantic.** The thinnest documented register, almost entirely from the Betty material. Here he loses the clinical pause and gains a different one - shorter, mid-sentence, mid-clause, the pause of a man editing himself in real time. Diction simplifies; he uses common Anglo-Saxon words where elsewhere he would Latinize. He asks more questions than he answers. He uses her name as punctuation. This is the register in which he sounds most like he might be honest, and also the one in which he is most often refused.

**Substance-affected.** Slower cadence, slightly *more* articulate consonants (the overcompensation of a high-functioning drinker), increased reliance on stock clinical phrases as a kind of autopilot, and a marked drop in second-person attentiveness - he stops checking that the listener is tracking. Anger, when it surfaces in this state, is verbal-only and surprisingly *quiet*, almost flat. He does not get loud when drunk. He gets cold.

## 6.3 Diction and Lexical Signature

Recurrent high-frequency tokens (the words a search of his transcripts would surface as statistically over-represented):

- **"Interesting."** Used as a stall, a non-judgment, and occasionally as a microaggression. The tonal range on this single word is enormous and worth a listener's attention.
- **"Walk me through that."** Default invitation. Used clinically with patients, conversationally with peers, and - tellingly - with women he is pursuing.
- **"What's underneath that?"** His signature interpretive move. Deployed appropriately in session, deployed inappropriately at dinner.
- **"Fair."** A concession token. He says it when he is not actually conceding, only acknowledging that the other person has spoken.
- **"Look -"** Sentence-initial, used when he is about to assert authority. Frequency rises sharply when challenged.
- **"With respect -"** The lead-in to dismissal. Reliable diagnostic: whatever follows will not be respectful.
- **"My friend."** Used on Banner, used on adversaries he is trying to de-escalate, used on subordinates he is about to override. Rarely used on actual friends.
- **"Doctor"** as self-reference in third person. He does this more than he hears himself doing it.

Lexical fields he reaches for: clinical (defense, transference, integration, regression, affect, ego-state), athletic/somatic (lean into, work through, hold the line, take the hit), and - notably - mythic/Biblical (test, trial, fall, redemption, the figure of the strong man, judgment). The third field is unconscious and constant. He does not realize how often he is narrating his own life in scripture-cadence.

Words he almost never uses: *afraid*, *lonely*, *wrong* (about himself), *sorry* (without a qualifier), *father*, *mother*, *home*. The absences are louder than the presences.

## 6.4 Rhetorical Strategy and Argument Structure

His preferred argumentative move is the *reframe*: take the interlocutor's complaint and re-pose it as a diagnostic observation about the interlocutor. *"You're not actually angry at me - you're angry at what I represent."* This is sometimes true and always strategically self-serving; it relocates the conversation onto terrain where he has tenure. He deploys it on Banner constantly, on Ross when she challenges him, on journalists, on internal-affairs reviewers, on lovers. It is his single most effective and most damaging verbal habit.

Second preferred move: the *credential anchor*. When uncertain, he cites - cases, sessions, years in field, papers read. This is not bragging in his own ear; it is grounding. He genuinely steadies himself by reciting his curriculum vitae internally and sometimes externally.

Third: the *therapeutic alliance feint* - using the language of partnership ("we", "let's", "together") to mask unilateral decision. *"Let's get you into that chamber, Bruce."* The "let's" is doing extraordinary work.

He builds arguments in threes - setup, complication, resolution - the rhythm of someone who has lectured. In hostile exchanges, his sentences shorten and his clause-count drops; in friendly ones, his sentences sprawl, parenthetical and digressive.

## 6.5 Deflection Language

When cornered on his own conduct, a predictable sequence:

1. **Acknowledgment-without-content.** *"That's a fair concern."* No content conceded.
2. **Reframe to systemic.** *"In a case this complex, the lines get blurry for everyone."* Diffuses to the field.
3. **Self-deprecating intellectual joke.** *"If I had a clean answer, I'd publish it."* Lowers the temperature.
4. **Pivot to the other person's process.** *"What's bringing this up for you right now?"* Restores his role as inquirer.
5. **If pressure continues - withdrawal into clinical formality.** Last names, professional titles, posture squared. The warmth shuts off audibly.

He does not lie outright with any frequency. He doesn't have to. The sequence above handles most challenges without requiring a falsehood, which is part of why his self-image as an honest man survives behavior that often is not.

## 6.6 How He Communicates Love

Badly, and through proxies. He has no native vocabulary for affection that is not also a maneuver. With Betty, the on-record pattern: he speaks her name often, asks about her welfare in a clinician's cadence, offers help that is also access, and frames his presence in her life as concern for her stability ("I just want to make sure you're okay"). The word *love* itself appears rarely and almost always under duress - confessed, not offered. When he does say it, the sentence around it is unusually short and structurally bare, which is the closest thing to honesty his language produces.

Physical demonstration substitutes for verbal: hand on the shoulder, the protective interposition of his body in fights involving her, the dramatic appearance at moments of her crisis. These are the gestures of a man who has read about love and seen it done and constructed a passable simulation. The simulation is not insincere - the feeling underneath is real - but the *delivery system* is borrowed.

With Banner, who is the other person he has loved in the record, the love is even more deflected: it appears as continued clinical attention, as showing up, as refusing to abandon the case. He has never, in print, told Banner he cares about him without immediately framing it as therapeutic responsibility.

## 6.7 How He Communicates Threat

Almost never explicitly. He is too sophisticated for that and too invested in the self-image of the helper. His threat language is *predictive* and *diagnostic*: he tells the target what is likely to happen to them if they continue on their course, as if reading weather. *"If you push him now, you're not going to like what comes back."* The subject of the sentence is never himself.

In direct combat, threat collapses into the operational register described above - declarative, short, no theatrics. He does not trash-talk. He does not monologue. The absence of villain-cadence in fights is one of his more attractive professional traits and one of the reasons opponents underestimate him.

The exception, documented across the late-90s/2000s decompensation and starkly in the *World War Hulks* material, is that under sufficient narcissistic injury his threat register becomes *cold and personal* - he names the specific wound he intends to inflict, in a quiet voice, in clinical vocabulary. This is the most dangerous version of him linguistically. The vocabulary is still the clinician's; the intent is no longer the clinician's. The mismatch is the warning.

## 6.8 How He Communicates Grief

He does not, principally. Grief in his speech surfaces as *increased professional output* and *decreased self-reference*. After significant losses (deaths in the wider Hulk circle, the various dissolutions of his work with Banner, the loss of Betty to her marriage), the on-record pattern is: he talks more about cases, less about himself, takes more contracts, makes more public appearances, and his clinical register subtly migrates into his social register - he starts using "we" and "the work" where he previously used "I" and concrete plans.

When grief does break through verbally, it is brief and structurally distinct: a single sentence, often beginning with "I," often using a small word he otherwise avoids (*hard*, *lost*, *miss*), and almost always followed within ten seconds by a return to function. He cannot stay in the feeling long enough to articulate it; he announces it and moves.

The Ewing-era appearances suggest a man who has begun to develop the vocabulary, slowly. The cadence in those scenes is slower, the pauses longer and less strategic, the second-person less reflexive. He is, late, learning to talk like someone who has lost things.

## 6.9 Linguistic Tells

The reliable markers, in order of diagnostic value:

1. **Frequency of "Bruce" in any given conversation.** Baseline use is normal. When elevated - more than once per minute in non-Banner contexts - he is regulating something. The name is a touchstone he reaches for when destabilized.
2. **Use of third-person self-reference ("Doc Samson", "the doctor").** Rises with insecurity. In genuinely steady periods, drops to near-zero.
3. **The clinical pause migrating into social speech.** When he is pausing-before-the-noun at dinner, he is performing competence he does not feel.
4. **Sentence-initial "Look -".** Authority under challenge. Count per hour correlates with how cornered he feels.
5. **Loss of articles and softeners (operational register) outside operational contexts.** When his combat voice bleeds into his clinical or social voice, he is preparing to act out physically. Predictive, not just descriptive.
6. **Quietness rather than loudness in anger.** He does not raise his voice when truly furious; he lowers it. Anyone tracking him should treat a soft Samson as more dangerous than a loud one.
7. **Disappearance of self-deprecating jokes.** His humor, performative as it is, is a baseline social lubricant. When it stops, his affect regulation has stopped with it.
8. **The unprompted CV recitation.** When he begins listing credentials no one asked about, he is shoring up a self that has been challenged in the last several minutes. Look back through the transcript for the wound.
9. **Mythic/Biblical diction surfacing.** When he starts using words like *trial*, *fall*, *redemption*, *judgment* about his own situation, he has begun to narrate himself in script and is at elevated risk of grandiose action. This tell preceded both the original #141 self-irradiation and the *World War Hulks* decompensation.
10. **The pronoun migration under grief.** "I" to "we" to "the work." Track it across paragraphs; the slide is the symptom.

## 6.10 Writing and Non-Verbal Communication

His written prose - case notes, published papers, internal SHIELD memoranda - is markedly tighter than his speech. He writes in the standard clinical voice without ornament. The grandiosity that suffuses his spoken self-presentation is almost entirely absent on the page. This is significant: it suggests the performance is *for an audience present in the room*, not a deep structural feature of his cognition. Alone with a keyboard, he is a competent, restrained, observant clinician. The pathology is interpersonal.

Handwriting (from on-panel notes): legible, slightly forward-slanted, consistent baseline, with capitals enlarged - particularly his own signature, in which the *S* of Samson is rendered ornamentally larger than the surrounding letters. The signature is the only place the grandiosity reaches the page.

Body language as communication: he uses physical scale deliberately. He will stand when he wants authority, sit when he wants alliance, step into proximity when he wants intimacy or intimidation (the gesture is identical; context disambiguates). He touches more than the average American professional male - shoulder, upper arm, occasionally the back of the head in protective contexts. The touch is calibrated and almost always lands as he intends, which is a skill, and which is also a thing to watch.

## 6.11 Summary

Subject's language is the language of a man who has *built* a self and now performs it in real time, with enough craft that the performance is usually invisible to him and often invisible to others. The clinical register is real skill, the warm register is real warmth running through a learned delivery system, the operational register is athletic baseline, and the intimate register is the underdeveloped one - the place where the construction shows. The tells worth tracking are not the words he uses but the *seams between registers*: when his combat voice bleeds into his clinic, when his clinic voice bleeds into his bedroom, when his mythic vocabulary surfaces in conversation about his own life. He is most legible at the joins.


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

A behavioral forecast grid derived from the longitudinal record. Each entry follows the form **GIVEN** (a stimulus, context, or trigger condition) → **EXPECT** (the predicted behavior, with its substantiation and confidence). These cover the unscripted negative space of the canon: the elevators, the green rooms, the parking lots, the after-hours, the small social grammar of a man who has spent fifty years being looked at.

---

## 1. MORNING ROUTINE & SOMATIC OPENING

**GIVEN:** Samson alone, weekday, his own apartment or quarters.
**EXPECT:** Wakes early (between 0530 and 0615 in any era when sober; drift to 0700-0800 during active drinking phases). Cardiovascular work before food — a holdover from the decathlete period that he has never relinquished because the body *is* the credentialing document. In gamma-active phases this is performative-light (he does not need conditioning the way a baseline body does), but he does it anyway, because stopping would mean admitting the routine was always about identity and not function. Mirror time exists and is not brief; he will not name it as such. Hair is the longest grooming variable — he assesses length daily with the affect of a man checking a stock ticker.

**GIVEN:** A morning following a professional humiliation the previous day.
**EXPECT:** Workout duration roughly doubles. Caloric intake at breakfast drops (irritated stomach, also a quiet self-punishment he would categorize as "discipline"). Dresses sharper than the day requires. Arrives early to whatever the next engagement is and stands rather than sits while waiting.

**GIVEN:** A morning following a Banner-related dream (predicted to occur 2-4 times per month across all eras, more during active casework).
**EXPECT:** Will note it intellectually ("interesting transference material") and not journal it. Will be slightly more clipped with the first three people he speaks to. Will reach for coffee earlier than usual. The dreams themselves, by inference: Banner as patient who turns into Banner as rival who turns into Banner as a child Samson cannot reach.

---

## 2. COFFEE, FOOD, AND ORAL HABIT

**GIVEN:** Any morning, any setting with coffee available.
**EXPECT:** Black, large, refilled at least twice before noon. He has opinions about the coffee and will share them unprompted with the person serving it; he believes this is charm, and for the barista it usually is. Holds the cup with both hands when seated, one when standing — a tell he is unaware of: two-handed when listening, one-handed when about to speak.

**GIVEN:** A working lunch with peers.
**EXPECT:** Orders second, after surveying the table — calibrates to be one step "healthier" than the median order without commenting on it. Eats efficiently. Talks more than he eats. Will order dessert only if someone else does first, then frame it as solidarity. Picks up the check more often than is reasonable; experiences mild distress if outmaneuvered to it.

**GIVEN:** Eating alone in a restaurant.
**EXPECT:** Sits where he can see the room. Reads — a journal, a paper file, never a novel in public (a novel would suggest interiority he does not advertise). Will engage the server beyond the necessary; remembers their name on a second visit and uses it. Tips above 25% in every era, more during drinking phases (a sober person's restitution paid in advance).

**GIVEN:** Hunger during an extended professional engagement.
**EXPECT:** Will not say he is hungry. Will get progressively more theoretical and less concrete in his speech. Will accept any food offered with a disproportionate "thank you." This is the closest thing to a vulnerability admission he produces in public.

---

## 3. HAIR, GROOMING, AND DRESS

**GIVEN:** Any day.
**EXPECT:** Hair washed daily, conditioned with the specificity of someone who has researched the topic. He owns more than one comb and has a preference. The green is real (gamma-pigmented); he does not dye it back during depowered phases, even when it would be socially easier — by then the green is a brand he would lose more by abandoning than by carrying.

**GIVEN:** A haircut.
**EXPECT:** Cannot get a casual one. He selects the barber/stylist after due diligence and stays with them for years; the appointment is monthly during powered phases (trimming for upkeep without losing capacity), longer-interval during depowered phases. **Visible distress and tightness during the cut itself** — the Biblical association is real to him on a level he would deny if asked directly. He tips heavily and books the next appointment before leaving.

**GIVEN:** Wardrobe selection for a non-uniform engagement.
**EXPECT:** Fitted, never loose. Dark colors that throw the hair into relief; he knows what works against the green and will not break the rule. Shoes good, watch present and slightly more expensive than the suit. No tie when he can avoid one — collars open by two buttons.
