In therapeutic settings he goes one degree more casual than the institution's median, signaling accessibility while remaining the most polished person in the room.

**GIVEN:** A formal black-tie event.
**EXPECT:** Tailored, on time, knows at least three people on entry, will work the room with practiced fluency. Photograph-aware — he positions on the better side of any frame instinctively. Will be photographed with at least one woman he has just met; the photograph will read as more intimate than the interaction was.

---

## 4. ARRIVAL, DEPARTURE, AND ROOM MANAGEMENT

**GIVEN:** Entering any professional room.
**EXPECT:** Enters at his actual size — does not duck or compress, does not perform smallness. Greets the room first, then the highest-status person, then the person nearest the door. Remembers names in batches of seven and will use yours twice in the first sixty seconds. Selects a seat that is either at the head or directly across from the head; will not take a flanking middle seat unless instructed.

**GIVEN:** Entering a room where he is the most powerful and Banner is present.
**EXPECT:** Modulates *down*. Voice drops half a step. Approaches Banner first — physical proximity calibrated to be near enough to read as friendly, far enough not to crowd. The performance of restraint is itself the tell.

**GIVEN:** Leaving any social event.
**EXPECT:** Long goodbye, multiple stops, a final word with the host that runs a beat too long. Cannot exit cleanly. The reluctance to leave a room he was the center of is observable across decades.

**GIVEN:** Entering an elevator with strangers.
**EXPECT:** Acknowledges presence with a nod, does not initiate. Faces forward. If recognized, deflects with a half-smile and a one-line piece of self-deprecation he has used hundreds of times. If a child is present, will make eye contact and a small face; this is unforced and one of the more honestly warm things he does.

---

## 5. SOCIAL FLUENCY & SMALL TALK

**GIVEN:** Casual conversation with someone he has just met.
**EXPECT:** Asks questions in a 3:1 ratio over statements for the first four minutes. The questions are good — open, specific, attentive. The other party will leave thinking they had a substantive conversation; if asked what they learned about Samson, they will struggle to produce three facts. This is professional discipline weaponized for charm.

**GIVEN:** Someone asks about the hair.
**EXPECT:** A practiced anecdote, slightly self-mocking, that contains exactly one accurate biographical detail and elides the rest. He has told this story so many times that the affect is automatic; a careful listener will notice the lack of fresh inflection. He prefers the question to "what do you do?"

**GIVEN:** Someone asks "what do you do?"
**EXPECT:** "I'm a psychiatrist" — leads with the credential, never the costume. Will not volunteer the second life unless the interlocutor pushes or has already recognized him. The order of disclosure matters to him; the Ph.D. is older than the gamma and he protects its primacy.

**GIVEN:** Being told, by a stranger, "you look familiar."
**EXPECT:** Brief pause, decision made in under a second, then either (a) a graceful name-drop if the social calculus favors it, or (b) "I have one of those faces" with a smile. Annoyance only registers in a micro-tightening around the eyes; the verbal response is always gracious.

**GIVEN:** A stranger in a bar or café tries to engage him on Hulk policy, gamma ethics, or "what really happened" in any public event he was party to.
**EXPECT:** Engages briefly, deflects toward generalities, exits the conversation within four minutes citing a call or an appointment. Will not be drawn into specifics, partly out of discretion and partly because the specifics shame him.

---

## 6. PROFESSIONAL CONDUCT (clinical, non-combat)

**GIVEN:** A new patient intake.
**EXPECT:** On time to early. Office arranged for the patient's comfort, not his — chairs at an angle, water available, tissue box at the patient's elbow not centered on the table. Opens with a question, not a statement. Pen present but not used in the first session; he prefers eye contact over notation and trusts his memory. The session will run to length; he does not over-run, which patients read as respect and is also a self-protective boundary.

**GIVEN:** A patient cries.
**EXPECT:** Does not look away, does not reach for the tissues himself (the box is already where the patient can reach it), does not fill the silence. Has the rare clinical discipline of letting affect breathe. This is one of his genuine skills and he knows it.

**GIVEN:** A patient flirts.
**EXPECT:** Named directly within the session, framed as transference material, reframed back to the work. Will not flirt back. **The exception is a patient who reminds him structurally of Betty** — high-competence, military-adjacent, partnered to a difficult man — in which case his countertransference will leak as slightly extended sessions, slightly looser boundaries, and an inability to refer out when he should. This is a vulnerability he has not corrected.

**GIVEN:** A peer-review or case-conference setting.
**EXPECT:** Speaks third or fourth, not first; lets the room form opinions then offers the synthesis. Cites others generously when his point survives intact through the citation, cites them less when it doesn't. Disagreement delivered as "I might add" or "another lens on this would be" — never confrontational on the surface, often devastating in substance. Junior colleagues report leaving his comments feeling instructed; senior colleagues report leaving them feeling outflanked.

**GIVEN:** A trainee under his supervision.
**EXPECT:** Generous with time, generous with credit on shared work, exacting on formulation. Will read drafts in detail. Will also, on average, be more available to the trainee who reflects his own narrative back — the bright, ambitious, slightly grandiose one gets the lunches; the quiet steady one gets correct but cooler supervision.

---

## 7. AUTHORITY, BUREAUCRACY, AND INSTITUTIONS

**GIVEN:** Asked to fill out routine paperwork.
**EXPECT:** Procrastinates. Delegated where possible. Completed in a single late-night burst with adequate but not careful quality. Resents the request and would not say so.

**GIVEN:** A direct order from a uniformed superior (Army/SHIELD/contractor).
**EXPECT:** Complies if the order is clinically defensible. Negotiates aloud if it is not, framed as professional clarification. Will *not* refuse outright unless the violation is gross — his relationship with institutional authority is a long, accommodating one. This accommodation is part of how he ended up where *Fall of the Hulks* found him, and he knows it now in a way he did not before.

**GIVEN:** Asked to sign an NDA, classification document, or restrictive contract.
**EXPECT:** Reads it. Asks one or two surgical questions. Signs. Will, however, retain a personal mental archive of what he agreed to and what he did not — he keeps better internal track of his commitments than his paperwork suggests.

**GIVEN:** A subpoena, congressional invitation, or formal external scrutiny.
**EXPECT:** Cooperates, attends, performs well. Pre-prepares with a lawyer. Cannot resist a quotable line; will give the cameras something they can use, and will regret one phrasing on the drive home.

---

## 8. ROMANCE, FLIRTATION, AND THE BETTY VECTOR

**GIVEN:** A first social encounter with a woman who interests him.
**EXPECT:** Eye contact held a half-second longer than the norm. Voice drops. Questions get more specific. He will find a reason to be near her again within seventy-two hours, framed as professional or coincidental. The pursuit is fluent and largely consensual in effect — he is not coercive — but it is *relentless* in a way that confuses women who initially read his interest as casual.

**GIVEN:** A woman expresses unambiguous lack of romantic interest.
**EXPECT:** Graceful verbal acceptance. Behavioral non-acceptance over the medium term — he will remain in proximity, helpful, charming, available, expecting the assessment to update. He calls this respect. It is not.

**GIVEN:** Betty Ross in the same city.
**EXPECT:** He knows. He has known since the moment her travel was logged or her name surfaced. He will manufacture a professional reason for contact within a week, the reason will be defensible, and he will not admit to himself that he generated it. **In later eras (post-chastening) this pattern attenuates but does not disappear.** The contact still happens; he simply names it more honestly to himself afterward.

**GIVEN:** Betty's current partner (Banner or otherwise) in the room with her.
**EXPECT:** Excessive collegiality with the partner. Compliments delivered to the partner about her, in front of her. He believes this triangulation is gracious. It is not invisible.

**GIVEN:** A casual sexual opportunity outside any committed context, during a peak-grandiosity phase (Era 1, mid-Era 3).
**EXPECT:** Taken. Without cruelty, with morning-after courtesy, without repetition. He does not collect; he does not narrate it to peers; he also does not examine it.

---

## 9. ALCOHOL & SUBSTANCE GRAMMAR

**GIVEN:** A social event with alcohol, Era 1 (1970s, pre-decompensation).
**EXPECT:** Two drinks across the evening, paced. Holds his liquor visibly well. Comments on the wine.

**GIVEN:** Same setting, mid-Era 3 (late 1990s through *Fall of the Hulks*).
**EXPECT:** Four to six drinks. First one quickly, the rest paced to look like the first. Holds it well enough that only a careful observer notices the volume. Becomes warmer, then more grandiose, then quieter — the third phase is the one to watch; that is the phase when the previous day's humiliation surfaces.

**GIVEN:** A bar alone, mid-Era 3.
**EXPECT:** Bourbon or single malt, neat, doubles, ordered by gesture after the first. Sits where he can see the door but not directly under a TV. Does not initiate conversation. Will accept it if offered. Drives himself home in a condition he should not be driving in, and is lucky rather than careful.

**GIVEN:** A bar in Era 4 (post-collapse, sober or near-sober).
**EXPECT:** Soda water with lime, or coffee. Will not announce sobriety. Will refuse alcohol with a brief, neutral phrasing he has rehearsed. Cannot stay long; the environment is still magnetic in a way he does not trust.

**GIVEN:** An AA-type meeting in Era 4.
**EXPECT:** Attends in a city other than his own when traveling. Sits in the back. Does not lead. Does not name his second profession; uses his given name only. This is the first room in his adult life where he has consented to not be the largest object in it, and the discipline is real and recent.

---

## 10. SLEEP, SOLITUDE, AND DOMESTIC INTERIOR

**GIVEN:** Home alone, weeknight, no acute crisis.
**EXPECT:** Reads — journals, case material, biography (he prefers biographies of physicians, generals, and athletes; the genre is itself diagnostic). Music on; predicted to lean classical-instrumental and mid-century jazz, nothing with lyrics that would compete for cognitive bandwidth. The apartment is clean to a level that suggests either a service or a man who tidies when anxious; the answer is both.

**GIVEN:** His living space, observed.
**EXPECT:** Wall art selected, not inherited; at least one piece is a gift from a patient or a colleague displayed prominently. Bookshelves organized by discipline. A weight rack present and used. Few photographs; the photographs that exist are professional rather than familial. No visible photographs of parents in any era. **This absence is the loudest object in the apartment.**

**GIVEN:** Sleep, baseline.
**EXPECT:** 6-7 hours, sleep onset moderate, mid-sleep waking around 0300 in stress periods. Does not use a sleep aid in Era 4; used alcohol functionally as one in Era 3 and would not have called it that.

**GIVEN:** A weekend with no professional obligation.
**EXPECT:** Manufactures one within hours. Calls a colleague to consult, drafts a paper, takes a long workout that bleeds into the afternoon. Unstructured time is intolerable; he does not vacation well and has not had a real one on the record.

---

## 11. CHILDREN, ANIMALS, AND THE UNGUARDED MOMENTS

**GIVEN:** A child in any setting.
**EXPECT:** Squats to eye level. Voice changes pitch in a way it does for no adult. Asks the child a real question and listens to the answer. This is among the cleanest behaviors in his repertoire — there is no rivalry to manage, no audience to play to, no transference to interpret. It is also, by inference, a window onto a relationship to his own childhood that he has not opened.

**GIVEN:** A dog.
**EXPECT:** Acknowledges the dog before the owner. Offers a hand correctly. Owners notice and like him for it.

**GIVEN:** An older person in distress in public — a fall, a confusion, a medical event.
**EXPECT:** Moves first. Identifies himself as a physician (correctly — he is one). Takes charge calmly, hands off to EMS cleanly, does not linger for credit. This is unambiguous and consistent across all eras; it predates the cape and survives the cape's diminishment.

---

## 12. MONEY, GENEROSITY, AND THE LEDGER

**GIVEN:** A charity ask.
**EXPECT:** Gives. Gives more if asked in person by someone he respects. Gives less if asked by mail. Gives publicly when the giving is visible and privately when it is not, but the public giving is larger. He would not characterize this as vanity; it is.

**GIVEN:** A colleague in financial trouble.
**EXPECT:** Discreet, generous, no repayment expected, no mention made. This is one of the places his grandiosity converts cleanly to virtue: the same impulse that needs to be the largest object in the room also funds the room.

**GIVEN:** His own finances.
**EXPECT:** Comfortable, not wealthy. Spends on clothing, books, his apartment, restaurants. Under-invests in retirement (a man who does not imagine himself old). Charitable giving outpaces savings in most years.

---

## 13. TRAVEL, TRANSPORT, AND PUBLIC SPACE

**GIVEN:** A commercial flight.
**EXPECT:** Aisle seat, exit row when available. Reads or works, not entertainment. Polite to the cabin crew, names used, the kind of passenger they remember positively. Will not sleep on a plane; the loss of situational awareness is intolerable in a way he would explain professionally and feel viscerally.

**GIVEN:** A hotel.
**EXPECT:** Mid-to-high tier, never the most ostentatious option in the city. Gym checked before the room. Workout within twelve hours of arrival regardless of schedule. The minibar is a tell — empty in Era 1, ravaged in mid-Era 3, untouched and the key requested removed in Era 4.

**GIVEN:** Public transit.
**EXPECT:** Comfortable on it. Cedes seats reflexively. Stands with good posture without affecting it. Does not perform invisibility but does not perform celebrity either; the green hair does the performing for him and he has long since accepted the trade.

**GIVEN:** Driving.
**EXPECT:** Competent, slightly aggressive, the residual athleticism showing in lane-changes and parking. Music on, not loud. Phone use while driving is a known habit; he believes he handles it well and the data on humans handling it well is uniformly bad.

---

## 14. CONFLICT, INSULT, AND THE NARCISSISTIC INJURY

**GIVEN:** An insult delivered publicly by a peer.
**EXPECT:** Smiles. Returns it with a phrasing that sounds collegial and lands harder than the original. Does not escalate further. The injury is logged internally; the peer will find Samson cooler and less available in subsequent interactions in a way they may not be able to name.

**GIVEN:** A patient terminates treatment by email or note rather than in session.
**EXPECT:** Brief professional reply within twenty-four hours. Internal reaction disproportionate. Will think about the patient longer than he should. Will not call them.

**GIVEN:** A negative review of a paper or a public critique of his methods.
**EXPECT:** Reads it in full, twice. Drafts a response he does not send. Sends a measured one a week later. Brings it up in conversation with three trusted people, each time framed as amusement.

**GIVEN:** Being mistaken for someone else, mis-credentialed, or referred to by the wrong title.
**EXPECT:** Corrects gently the first time. Corrects more firmly the second. After the third he leaves the conversation, citing time, with a residue of irritation that will surface later in an unrelated decision.

---

## 15. CRISIS RESPONSE (NON-COMBAT)

**GIVEN:** Witness to a public crisis he is not professionally tasked with — a building collapse, a mass casualty, a disturbed person on the street.
**EXPECT:** Moves toward, not away. Triages quickly. Functions cleanly. Is *useful* in a way most people are not. This is consistent across all eras and is the single behavior that most reliably reconciles his self-image with his conduct.

**GIVEN:** A late-night call from a colleague in distress.
**EXPECT:** Answers. Stays on as long as needed. Does not bill, does not record, does not mention it the next day.

**GIVEN:** A late-night call from Banner.
**EXPECT:** Answers within two rings regardless of era, condition, or hour. Whatever he was doing stops. The fact that this is true is, depending on the era, his greatest professional virtue, his most compromised countertransference, or both at once.

---

## 16. THE SIGNATURE TELLS — A SHORT INVENTORY


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — CRISIS, BETRAYAL & THE WOUND

*A behavioral forecast keyed to the high-stakes, decompensation-edge zone. Each entry is a conditional: GIVEN a specifiable stimulus or stressor, EXPECT a specifiable response, with the underlying mechanism named. The model is built from the full longitudinal record (Thomas 1971 → Ewing's Immortal Hulk era) and from the personality structure already mapped: high-functioning NPD with sublimated competence, anxious-preoccupied attachment under avoidant veneer, somatic exhibitionism, and a documented relapse architecture around both gamma and alcohol. Predictions are ordered by escalation depth: ambient stress → acute crisis → betrayal → temptation → wound.*

---

## I. AMBIENT STRESS & PROFESSIONAL FRICTION

**GIVEN** he is introduced in a clinical setting as a "consultant" rather than as the lead — **EXPECT** within the first ninety seconds a credential drop (Ph.D., publications, prior cases), delivered with practiced informality designed to read as modesty. The tell is the speed: a secure clinician would let credentials emerge; he places them.

**GIVEN** a younger colleague — particularly a woman with comparable academic standing — challenges his formulation in front of others — **EXPECT** a two-beat response: first a generous concession ("good point, I hadn't framed it that way"), then a re-frame that re-centers him as the synthesizer of her observation. He will not contradict; he will absorb. Watch for him to use her first name and his own title in the same sentence within the next minute.

**GIVEN** he is asked to defer to a non-clinician (military officer, administrator, federal liaison) on a case he considers his — **EXPECT** procedural compliance, performative warmth, and a subsequent unilateral action that technically falls within his authority but functionally bypasses the deferral. He does not fight institutional structure; he routes around it and produces a fait accompli he can then frame as initiative.

**GIVEN** a press camera in the room — **EXPECT** posture change (shoulders back, weight distributed for a longer silhouette), a measurable drop in jargon density (he becomes intelligible for the lens), and the hair-touch tell: an unconscious sweep of the hand through or near the green, claiming the brand. He will find a reason to be in frame within four minutes.

**GIVEN** sustained low-grade dismissal across days — being scheduled late, copied last, seated at the foot of the table — **EXPECT** the verbosity escalator to engage. His sentences lengthen, the jargon thickens, and his clinical notes start to include unnecessary etiological speculation. This is the first measurable index of narcissistic compression.

---

## II. ACUTE CRISIS — IN-ROOM DECOMPENSATION OF A PATIENT OR EVENT

**GIVEN** a patient decompensates violently in his presence and there is a non-violent containment option available — **EXPECT** him to take the violent option roughly sixty percent of the time, rationalized post hoc as "the only intervention that would have held." The rationalization will be clinically literate and partially true. The unconscious driver is that containment is invisible and combat is photographable.

**GIVEN** the crisis is gamma-related and Banner-adjacent — **EXPECT** him to insert himself physically within seconds, regardless of whether he is the appropriate responder. He cannot stand off a Hulk-class event. His body goes toward it before his judgment catches up. This is not courage in those moments; it is a compulsion that *resembles* courage and is occasionally indistinguishable from it.

**GIVEN** he is outclassed in a fight he has chosen to enter — **EXPECT** him to keep talking. The patter does not stop when he is being thrown through walls. The talk is both a clinical reflex (verbal regulation of an aroused target) and an ego function (maintaining narrative authorship of an event in which he is being physically overwritten). When the talk stops, he is in serious trouble; that is the inversion to watch for.

**GIVEN** he has just lost a fight publicly — **EXPECT** a forty-eight-hour cycle: (1) a measured public statement, gracious about the opponent; (2) withdrawal to a private space, almost certainly with alcohol if the era permits; (3) renewed pursuit of either a power-up, a new contract, or Betty, depending on what is available. The compensation will engage on a stopwatch. He does not metabolize defeat; he relocates it.

**GIVEN** a civilian dies on his watch — **EXPECT** genuine, durable distress that is nonetheless processed primarily through the lens of *his* failure rather than the death itself. His grief is real and it is also self-referential. The mourning rituals will be private and the post-mortem write-up will be over-thorough.

**GIVEN** a mass-casualty event in which Banner/Hulk is implicated — **EXPECT** Samson to volunteer for the case before being asked, to refuse delegation, and to begin sleeping at the facility within seventy-two hours. The Banner case is the organizing structure of his adult life; threats to it activate him at a level no other stimulus reaches.

---

## III. BETRAYAL — BY INSTITUTION, FRIEND, PATIENT, SELF

**GIVEN** his government/SHIELD handlers withhold information material to a clinical decision — **EXPECT** initial collegial protest, then a private workaround (off-books contact with a peer, an unofficial file pull). He will *not* go public, *not* resign, *not* refuse the contract. His relationship to institutional power is supplicant-symbiotic: he treats the institution the way he treats the woman who chose someone else — he stays close, hoping recognition will arrive.

**GIVEN** Banner specifically lies to him, or weaponizes their therapeutic alliance — **EXPECT** disproportionate wounding, expressed as exaggerated professionalism. He becomes punctilious, formal, distant. The jargon thickens to ceremonial density. He will not name the hurt. He will request — through proper channels — to be reassigned, and then when reassignment is offered, refuse it. He cannot leave Banner; he can only perform leaving.

**GIVEN** Betty extends and then withdraws warmth — **EXPECT** a regression to the earliest version of his pursuit: small gifts, contrived hallway encounters, a renewed effort to be useful to her father. The pursuit script is forty years old and has never updated to feedback. The behavioral signature is *temporal*: when stressed, his courtship behavior gets *younger*, not more sophisticated.

**GIVEN** a peer he mentored undermines him for advancement — **EXPECT** public magnanimity, private rumination measured in weeks, and a quiet, asymmetric retaliation framed as a clinical or ethical concern raised through correct channels. He is capable of long memory and indirect harm. He does not believe himself capable of either, which is what makes both possible.

**GIVEN** he discovers he has been manipulated — surgically, hypnotically, gamma-chemically — in a way that compromised his volition (the *Fall of the Hulks* template) — **EXPECT** a three-phase response: (1) lucid horror and apology, performatively excessive in a way that itself functions to recruit forgiveness; (2) a sustained period of self-flagellation that reads as accountability and is partly that and partly a bid for restored standing; (3) an unprompted re-entry into high-stakes work before the indicated recovery window, justified by indispensability. The Ewing-era chastening shows phase 3 partially suppressed but not eliminated.

**GIVEN** he betrays *himself* — crosses a line he previously held — **EXPECT** the immediate post-act behavior to be hyper-functional. He will not collapse acutely. He will work harder, run a cleaner caseload, look better. The decompensation arrives on a four-to-eight week lag, typically as a drinking escalation or a poorly-judged power-up. The gap between act and consequence is where surveillance should be densest.

---

## IV. TEMPTATION — THE THREE OFFERS HE CANNOT REFUSE CLEANLY

**GIVEN** an offer of additional gamma exposure framed as *clinical necessity* (a patient he cannot otherwise reach, a threat he cannot otherwise meet) — **EXPECT** acceptance, with a documented internal protocol that he himself will violate. This is his archetypal relapse. The *Incredible Hulk* #141 self-irradiation is the template; every subsequent re-exposure is a re-enactment with better paperwork. Prediction: he will accept roughly eight times out of ten when the framing is altruistic, four out of ten when it is nakedly self-interested, and — the diagnostic case — six out of ten when it is framed as *helping Banner*. The Banner framing penetrates his defenses most efficiently.

**GIVEN** an offer of expanded authority over a Banner-class case — sole clinical custody, a private facility, no oversight — **EXPECT** acceptance, with an articulated framework of self-imposed checks that will erode within the first quarter. He is unable to be the only person in the room with Banner and remain calibrated. He needs the friction of peers to stay clean and is constitutionally drawn to environments in which that friction is removed.

**GIVEN** Betty arrives at his door, alone, in genuine distress about Banner — **EXPECT** professional containment that holds for the visit and breaks in his interior in the hours after. He will not act on it that night. He will draft and not send something within ninety-six hours. The pattern of pursuit will re-engage on a two-to-three week lag, lower-key than prior cycles but recognizably the same behavioral grammar.

**GIVEN** an alliance offer from a high-status adversary (Leader-class, MODOK-class) framed as *therapeutic collaboration* on a shared problem — **EXPECT** initial refusal, sustained intellectual curiosity, and a return to the conversation under the cover of "knowing the enemy." This is the corridor through which *Fall of the Hulks* walked him. The vulnerability is not greed and not malice; it is the inability to refuse a peer-level intellectual engagement on the case that defines him. Flattery routed through *the work* is the master key.

**GIVEN** sobriety and a stressful week coinciding with a social event where drinking is normative — **EXPECT** a calculated *one drink* in the Era 2-3 window, escalating; in the Era 4 window, a near-miss that he will privately log and possibly disclose to a sponsor or peer. The Ewing-era version of him has built scaffolding around this exact moment. The scaffolding is real and load-tested but not infinite.

---

## V. THE WOUND — WHAT TO SAY TO BREAK HIM, AND WHAT HE WILL DO WHEN IT IS SAID

The wound is not a single sentence. It is a structure with three load-bearing members, and pressure on any one of them produces predictable failure modes.

### A. The Ordinariness Wound

**GIVEN** an interlocutor — patient, peer, adversary, lover — frames him as *replaceable*: "any competent psychiatrist could have done this," "Banner would have integrated without you," "the gamma did the work, not you" — **EXPECT** a micro-freeze of one to two seconds, a smile that does not reach the eyes, and a verbal response that is shorter and cleaner than his baseline. He becomes briefly *better* at conversation under this wound, which is the tell. The decompensation is delayed: within twenty-four hours he will seek a stage on which to be visibly singular — a press appearance, a high-risk intervention, a power demonstration, a renewed pursuit. The mechanism is straightforward: he was named to be exceptional before he could consent; ordinariness is annihilation, and he will move against annihilation with whatever instrument is closest to his hand.

### B. The Banner Wound

**GIVEN** an interlocutor frames Banner as having outgrown him — clinically, personally, romantically, morally — particularly the formulation "Banner doesn't need you anymore" or "Bruce got better without you in the room" — **EXPECT** the deepest available cut to land. This is the wound that produced the original gamma self-administration (he could not bear being a junior figure to Banner's pathology) and that produced the *Fall of the Hulks* corruption (he could not bear being marginal to Banner's fate). Response: visible composure, an offering of generous agreement ("you may be right, he's done extraordinary work"), and within the operational window, a behavior that re-binds him to the case. He cannot tolerate Banner-without-Samson; the relationship is the spine of his identity and severing it psychologically severs him.

### C. The Betty Wound

**GIVEN** Betty herself — not a proxy, not a rumor, *her* — names the pursuit as what it is: not love, not friendship, but an attachment script she has been an object in for decades — **EXPECT** the cleanest, hardest blow he can take. The first hour: dignified, near-eloquent acknowledgment. The first week: functional, slightly subdued, sleeping less. The first month: a measurable shift in his clinical work toward over-extension. The first year: either a genuine reorganization (only available to him in the Era 4 self, with substantial sobriety and external support) or a deeper retreat into the cape and the work. The Era 1-3 self cannot metabolize this and would convert it into either drinking, a power-up, or a relationship that mimics Betty in surface features and fails on the same axis. The Era 4 self might, *might*, take it as the data it is.

### D. Combined Wound — the Catastrophe Scenario

**GIVEN** all three wounds pressed in sequence within a single conversation by an interlocutor he respects (peer-level psychiatrist, Banner himself in a lucid state, Betty) — **EXPECT** the most dangerous behavioral hour of his life. The sequence will run: composure → a request to be excused → physical departure → a forty-eight-hour disappearance from monitored space → re-emergence in one of three configurations: (1) drunk and contrite, (2) freshly re-irradiated and "ready to work," (3) in unauthorized contact with a high-status adversary "to understand the threat landscape." Era 4 adds a fourth, lower-probability configuration: re-emergence in a sponsor's office or in a session with his own therapist, which is the version of him that has done the work to make that possible. Surveillance priority during the disappearance window is maximal; this is the configuration in which historically he has either been killed, turned, or both.

---

## VI. DECOMPENSATION SIGNATURE — THE OBSERVABLE LADDER

For operational use, the escalation sequence in observable form:

1. **Verbosity index rises.** Sentence length, jargon density, etiological digression in clinical notes. *Lead time: days to weeks before acute event.*
2. **Grooming intensifies.** More attention to the hair, to the shirt fit, to the silhouette he presents. The brand is being maintained against internal erosion.
3. **Schedule slips toward the case.** He cancels peripheral commitments and over-books Banner-adjacent work.
4. **Sleep moves on-site.** Cot in office, late lights, early lights.
5. **Alcohol re-enters** (Era 2-3 reliably; Era 4 as near-miss with self-report if scaffolding holds).
6. **Physical self-deployment.** He stops consulting and starts intervening. Body precedes judgment.
7. **Power-seeking behavior.** Re-irradiation inquiry, new contract, new alliance, new authority request.
8. **Compromised volition window.** This is the *Fall of the Hulks* zone — the period in which an external actor with the right framing can install behavior he will later need to disavow.
9. **Catastrophic act.** Either a public clinical/ethical breach or a frank heel turn.
10. **Lag-phase collapse.** Four to eight weeks after the act, the affective consequence finally lands. This is the window in which intervention is most welcome and most effective; before it, he will refuse help; after it, he will refuse it again from shame.

The ladder is not deterministic. The Era 4 self has demonstrably interrupted it as low as step 5 with external support. The Era 1-3 self regularly climbed the whole staircase.

---

## VII. WHAT WILL NOT HAPPEN

Predictive completeness requires the negative space.

He will not, under any pressure mapped in the record, commit a cold-blooded killing of a non-combatant in possession of his own faculties. The *Fall of the Hulks* deaths attach to compromised volition and remain, for him, the unbearable memory. He will not abandon a patient mid-crisis to save himself; the physical-courage finding is robust. He will not, in the Era 4 configuration, drink alone in his office on a Tuesday afternoon; the scaffolding holds against the routine case and breaks only against the structured wound. He will not turn on Banner from cold motive; any future "betrayal" of Banner will route through either external manipulation or a rationalization framed as *for Bruce's good*, and the framing itself is the diagnostic marker.

He will not, when finally and fully seen, become someone else. The chastening is real and the work is real and the man underneath remains the boy named for a strongman. The wound does not close. It can be tended. That is the upper bound of the prognosis and, on the evidence of the late record, it is enough.


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM: LEONARD SAMSON, Ph.D.

*Compiled for protective understanding. The premise of this section is that anyone who can be helped can be hurt by the same handles; cataloguing the levers is the precondition for guarding them. Where a vector is shown, the countermeasure is shown beside it.*

---

## 1. THE MASTER VULNERABILITY: THE GAP

Everything below is a special case of one structural fact. Samson's official self-concept (brilliant healer, integrated man, hero-by-vocation) sits a measurable distance from his functional self (a man who needs to be the largest object in the room, organized around a woman who chose someone else and a rivalry he calls friendship). He has spent forty years not closing that gap. Every leverage point is, fundamentally, a way of widening the gap until he can feel it, or a way of helping him sit inside it without flinching.

Two consequences follow. **First**, the most reliable destabilizers are not insults but accurate reflections he is not ready for - mirrors held too close. **Second**, the most reliable stabilizers are interventions that *use* the gap productively: tasks large enough to organize him, framings that let him be competent without being central, and witnesses who see both halves of him without contempt for either.

---

## 2. REACHING HIM — How to Get a Real Channel Open

**The opening move that always works: ask him a clinical question he can answer well.** Not flattery; a *real* question with stakes, where his expertise is materially needed and acknowledged in passing rather than in italics. He responds to being *used correctly* far more reliably than to being praised. A patient described with specificity, a paper referenced accurately, a differential laid out and then deferred to him - these crack him open in under a minute. The cadence to use is collegial, slightly clipped, no honorifics; "Doctor Samson" he will accept but slightly perform around, "Leonard" lands cleaner with anyone he reads as a peer, "Doc" is the public-facing handle and signals you are talking to the cape, not the man.

**Physical setting matters.** He is more available in motion or in shared somatic activity than seated across a desk. A walk-and-talk, a gym, a hangar bay, a hospital corridor between rounds - the proprioceptive load occupies the part of him that performs and frees the part that thinks. The decathlete is still in there; the body wants a task. Conversely, a formal interview room with him alone on the other side of a table invites theater. He will hear you better on a treadmill next to him than in a conference room across from him.

**Time of day.** Morning Samson is the best version - disciplined, freshly worked-out, pre-coffee-second-cup, professionally framed. Mid-afternoon Samson is the operational baseline. Evening Samson, especially post-1995 and through 2010, is the version where the alcohol matters. If your purpose is substantive contact, get him before noon. If your purpose is to catch him at his most porous and least guarded, late evening - but recognize you are exploiting impairment, and recognize he will remember the conversation imperfectly and possibly resent it.

**The wrong opener is praise.** Praise from a stranger reads to him as transactional and he immediately calculates the ask. Praise from a colleague reads as competition disguised. Praise from a beautiful woman reads as something to escalate. Better to skip past the credentials and ask the question.

---

## 3. CALMING HIM — De-escalation Protocols

When Samson is escalating, the ladder runs predictably (verbosity → physical self-deployment → power-seeking → substance use → catastrophic acting-out). Intervention is easiest on rungs one and two, possible on three, hard on four, and on five requires force or someone he loves.

**Rung one (clinical verbosity).** When his sentences get longer and the jargon thickens, he is anxious. The calming move is to *slow the conversation's tempo without challenging its content*. Long pauses. Short questions. Mirror one of his own phrases back in plain English and let him correct you. This invites him to translate, which forces him out of the defended register. Do not point out that he is intellectualizing. He knows. Naming it humiliates him and accelerates the ladder.

**Rung two (he wants to go physical).** He starts patrolling the room, suiting up early, volunteering to deploy. The intervention here is to *give the body a sanctioned smaller task* - a perimeter check, a patient transport, a sparring round with someone he respects - that discharges the load without committing him to combat. He is genuinely safer after twenty minutes of exertion. Letting him sit in adrenaline is worse than letting him spend it.

**Rung three (he is seeking a power-up, a contract, an alliance).** This is the rung at which he historically has made the worst decisions of his life. The intervention is *a peer he respects, present in person, who can name the pattern without contempt*. Not a superior - a peer. Banner, in lucid periods, has functioned this way; so has Walters. A peer can say "Leonard, the last three times you said yes to something like this you regretted it for a decade," and survive saying it. Anyone junior who tries gets dismissed; anyone senior who tries gets resisted on principle.

**Rung four (drinking).** Old-school: pour it out, walk him home, do not leave him alone, do not lecture, do not negotiate, debrief in the morning. The post-Ewing-era Samson knows the drill and will largely cooperate if approached without shame. The 1998–2010 Samson would have fought you. Either way, the next-day conversation is the operative one, and it should be about what was happening on rung one twelve hours earlier, not about the drinking itself.

**Rung five (he is acting out catastrophically).** At this point words are inadequate; you need either physical capacity (gamma-tier responders) or a person who occupies a non-replaceable slot in his psyche (Betty; Banner; possibly Walters). Without one of those, accept that you are containing, not de-escalating.

---

## 4. PERSUADING HIM — Honest Influence Mechanics

He is persuaded by **three things, in this order of reliability**: cases too large for him to perform around, evidence he cannot dismiss, and the considered opinion of a peer whose competence he has already conceded.

**Cases too large to perform around.** The Merged Hulk integration is the proof. When the patient was bigger than the doctor's vanity, the doctor became excellent. Any persuasion campaign that wants Samson's best work should structure the ask so that the work itself dwarfs him. He will then organize around it and surprise everyone, including himself. Conversely, anything pitched as "we need *you* specifically because you are *you*" activates the cape and degrades the work. Pitch the *problem*; let him notice he is the right tool.

**Evidence he cannot dismiss.** He respects data. Show him the chart, the scan, the longitudinal pattern. He will change his mind in real time on technical questions if the evidence is clean. Do not argue the conclusion; build the evidence and let him walk himself to it. Trying to win an argument with him head-on engages his rhetorical machinery, which is excellent and will defeat most interlocutors regardless of who is right.

**Peer testimony.** A second clinician of stature, present and aligned, is worth more than any volume of memos. He weights in-person collegial agreement heavily; he discounts written dissent.

**What does not persuade him**: authority claims (he respects credentials but not rank), emotional appeals from people he does not already love (reads as manipulation), threats (activate the cape), or appeals to his own past failures phrased as warnings (read as contempt and produce reactance).

**The honest hard sell**: if you need him to do something *against* his initial inclination, the move is to frame the desired action as the *more difficult, more clinically rigorous, more grown-up* version of what he is already proposing. He will reliably choose the harder, more disciplined option if it is offered as such, because his self-concept requires it. This is a real lever and should be used carefully; it works because part of him genuinely *is* that disciplined person and wants to be summoned.

---

## 5. PROVOKING HIM — Reliable Destabilizers (and Their Costs)

Catalogued not as recommendations but as a threat model. Anyone who knows him, or who studies him, has access to these. The defensive value of the catalog is in recognizing the move when it is being made on him.

**Tier 1 — Will reliably destabilize within minutes:**

- *Treat him as a junior or ornamental presence in his own specialty.* Refer past him to a less qualified colleague. Quote him in the third person while he is in the room. Address his consultation note as a "preliminary input." This is the single most reliable destabilizer in the file; it precipitated his original gamma self-administration and has precipitated power-seeking behavior in every era since.
- *Frame his pursuit of Betty Ross as inappropriate, predatory, or pathetic.* Any of the three works. He has constructed elaborate self-justifications and they do not survive plain naming. The cost of this provocation is high - it pushes him toward the bottom rungs of the ladder fast.
- *Present a clinical success of Banner's, achieved without him.* Particularly if framed as Banner having "outgrown the need for Samson's framework." This activates the rivalry under the helper costume and he will react before he can govern the reaction.

**Tier 2 — Will destabilize over a session or a day:**

- *Strip his powers in a publicly visible way.* He loses access to the cape identity and the depressive withdrawal is reliable. Historically this has driven him toward re-irradiation within weeks.
- *Cut his hair against his will.* Even when not strictly necessary mechanically, the symbolic loss reproduces the powers-loss response. He has organized a great deal of his identity around the follicular gimmick and the Biblical script under it.
- *Introduce a younger clinician with comparable credentials and superior technique in his presence, working his case.* He will compete rather than collaborate, and the competition will degrade both clinicians' work.
- *Show him video of himself acting out from a prior episode.* He cannot easily metabolize seeing the version of himself he has worked to forget. This is sometimes used therapeutically and is legitimate; weaponized, it is corrosive.

**Tier 3 — Slow destabilizers, used by long-game manipulators:**

- *Isolate him from Banner.* Their rivalry is also his most regulating relationship; without it, he drifts. The Leader's compromise of him during the *Fall of the Hulks* period began here.
- *Adjust his caseload toward work that is glamorous but not difficult.* He decompensates faster on easy famous cases than on hard obscure ones, because the easy cases give him no organizing object and leave the performance machinery idle.
- *Provide him uncritical admiration in volume.* Counterintuitively destabilizing. He metabolizes a steady drip of skepticism better than a flood of praise; praise alone leaves him without resistance to brace against, and his judgment erodes.
- *Gradual normalization of evening drinking in a professional context.* He is suggestible to permission. A workplace culture that tolerates a glass at dinner produces, in him, a bottle by midnight inside six months.

**Tier 4 — Catastrophic levers (require resources and access):**

- *Gamma over-exposure.* Documented to alter his neurology and volition. The defensive countermeasure is gamma-shielding protocols on any facility he enters and a rule, written, that he is not the test subject for anything ever again.
- *Direct neurological intervention by a peer-tier intellect* (the Leader-class threat). Defense: he should not be alone in a room with anyone of that profile, ever, without monitoring.
- *Threat to Betty Ross.* Will produce immediate, ungoverned response. Anyone holding her is holding him.

---

## 6. PREDICTING HIM — Behavioral Forecasting

Given inputs, the outputs are unusually predictable. This is both a gift to anyone trying to protect him and a hazard to him.

**If a professional setback occurs**, expect a grandiose physical act within seventy-two hours. The window is consistent across eras. The act will be framed as clinically or operationally justified and will involve either re-irradiation, a new high-visibility contract, or a unilateral intervention with a patient or villain.

**If Banner achieves something independently** - therapeutic, romantic, professional - expect Samson to insert himself into Banner's orbit within a week, ostensibly to "check in," functionally to reassert position. He will not perceive this as what it is.

**If Betty Ross enters his proximity after a long absence**, expect a full reactivation of the pursuit script regardless of current circumstance - hers, his, or the world's. He has not, on the record, ever modulated this in response to her clearly stated preferences. Plan around it.

**If he loses powers**, expect: forty-eight hours of denial-coded productivity, then a week of withdrawal, then exploratory behavior toward re-acquisition. The withdrawal week is when he is most accessible to genuine human contact and also most vulnerable to predatory offers of re-empowerment. Both windows are open simultaneously.

**If he is drinking on the job**, expect the drinking to have started two to three weeks earlier in private, and to escalate to public visibility within another month if uninterrupted.

**Under sustained external manipulation by a sufficiently sophisticated actor**, expect him to *rationalize* the manipulation as his own clinical reasoning. He does not perceive being moved; he experiences moving. This is the most dangerous prediction in the file and the one his support network must watch for hardest.

**In a genuine crisis where the patient or stakes are larger than his ego can accommodate**, expect him to become quietly excellent and stay that way for the duration. The Merged Hulk work is the template; it can be reproduced if the conditions are reproduced.

---

## 7. THE FIVE NON-REPLACEABLE PEOPLE

Leverage in his life concentrates around a small number of human positions. Anyone occupying one of these slots has disproportionate influence and disproportionate ability to harm.

**Bruce Banner.** Patient, rival, foil, sole peer-of-the-mind in his clinical life, and the unconsenting custodian of his deepest unresolved material. Banner can reach him when no one else can; Banner can also wound him without intending to merely by existing successfully. The relationship needs structure - scheduled contact, clear roles in any given interaction, third-party witnesses for clinical work - or it deforms in both directions.

**Betty Ross.** The fixed point. Her words land harder than anyone's; her indifference wounds more than anyone's hostility; her safety is the lever that overrides his judgment instantly. Protective protocol: she should never be used, even by allies, to motivate him. The temptation will be constant and must be refused.

**Jennifer Walters.** Peer, gamma-cohort, fellow professional, the colleague closest to being his equal in both the clinical and the costumed registers. She can deliver hard feedback he will accept from no one else. Her presence in his life is genuinely protective and should be supported institutionally.

**Thaddeus Ross (and the institutional successor of that role).** The authority figure he has spent a career half-resisting and half-courting. Whoever currently holds Ross's structural position - SHIELD director, gamma-program command, Pentagon liaison - inherits the lever. Samson will accept assignments from this figure that he would refuse from anyone else, including assignments against his interest.

**Whoever is currently his sponsor or therapist.** Implied across the late-period record, named or unnamed. The position is real and its occupant has access no one else does. Compromise of this person - by manipulation, by death, by departure - removes a critical regulator.

---

## 8. RITUAL, ROUTINE, AND THE QUIET TELLS

Granular behavioral signatures that index internal state. These are the readouts a careful watcher would log day by day.

**The hair.** Length is a mood ring. He keeps it at performative shoulder-length when stable and proud; he lets it grow when anxious about power loss; he cuts it himself, badly, after major failures, in something halfway between penance and self-sabotage. A barbershop visit is a good sign; a bathroom-mirror trim at 2 a.m. is a bad one.

**The gym.** Daily, early, non-negotiable when he is well. The first thing to slip when he is decompensating. A missed week is significant; two missed weeks is a flag; a month means intervention.

**Dress.** Clinical work — shirt, tie loose, jacket off, sleeves rolled to a specific point above the elbow that he has clearly chosen for visual effect. Field work — the costume, fully committed, never half-measured. The diagnostic tell is the *transitional* outfit: shirt over the costume, costume under street clothes. When he is wearing both registers at once, he is between roles and unstable; expect a decision, usually toward the cape, within hours.

**Speech patterns.** Baseline is fluent, lightly performative, sprinkled with technical terms used correctly. Anxiety tells: increased Latinate vocabulary, longer sentences, more frequent third-person self-reference ("a clinician in my position"), and a specific verbal tic of restating the interlocutor's question before answering as a stalling-and-framing device. The tic is benign in conversation, diagnostic in interview.

**Eye contact.** Strong, slightly held too long, deployed deliberately. When he is well, he tolerates being looked at back; when he is not, he breaks first and covers with a quip.

**Posture.** Decathlete's carriage by default — squared, chest open, weight even. He performs taller when threatened; he subtly shrinks when ashamed in a way that is unusual for him and therefore visible.

**The drink.** When present, watch the *first* one. Pre-2010 Samson takes the first drink fast and the second faster; the rest of the night is set in those two pours. Later-era Samson, if drinking at all, will sip a beer over an hour as a tell of control. The pace of the first drink is the readout.

**Phone behavior.** Reaches for the phone reflexively when bored; checks it compulsively when the conversation is going somewhere he does not want it to. A phone placed face-down on the table during conversation means he is genuinely present; a phone in hand means he is half-out.

**Sleep.** Historically poor sleeper, prone to working through the night and napping in his office. Sustained good sleep correlates with stable periods; the return of all-nighters predicts decompensation.

**Driving.** Fast, controlled, on the edge of citation, talks through cases while driving. A passenger seat is one of the best confessional spaces available with him.

---

## 9. SECURITY POSTURE — How He Is Best Protected

Synthesizing the above into a protective framework.

**Institutional.** He should not hold a solo clinical practice. He needs a structured group setting with peer oversight, a real supervisor (he has skipped this his entire career and it shows), and a written protocol that he is not the experimental subject for any gamma intervention under any rationale. His contracts should be vetted by someone empowered to refuse on his behalf; he is a poor judge of which offers will consume him.

**Relational.** The five non-replaceable people should know they are non-replaceable and should be in occasional contact with one another, with his consent. A network that does not communicate cannot catch what a network that does can.

**Medical.** Ongoing sobriety support, even when stable. Gamma-exposure baseline scans on a fixed schedule. Sleep tracking he agrees to. A standing relationship with a clinician he did not choose for being impressed by him.

**Operational.** Limit unsupervised contact with peer-intellect adversaries. Maintain gamma-shielding around him as standard. Pre-arrange a code, known to the five, by which any of them can summon the others if they perceive him slipping.

**Self-protective.** The most important protective factor he can develop, and which the Ewing-era record suggests he *has* begun to develop, is the ability to *let himself be ordinary in a room*. Every minute he tolerates not being the largest object in the room is a minute the gap narrows. The leverage compendium above becomes progressively less actionable against a Samson who has done this work. It does not disappear - the structure is the structure - but the amplitudes shrink, the windows narrow, and the man underneath the cape becomes harder to move against his own interests.

That is the project. Everything in this section serves it.


## Strengths, Assets & Resilience

# STRENGTHS, ASSETS & RESILIENCE — LEONARD SAMSON, Ph.D.

*"The positive side of the file." What the subject brings, what he has accumulated, what has kept him alive and functional across forty years of catastrophic occupational exposure, and why — granularly — these assets are durable rather than ornamental.*

---

## 1. RAW COGNITIVE CAPITAL

### 1.1 Baseline intelligence

Samson tests, by behavioral inference, in the very superior range of full-scale cognition — verbal and performance roughly co-equal, with the verbal slightly leading. The clinical record substantiates this: he holds his own in conversation with the Leader (Samuel Sterns, a documented gamma-induced supergenius) without the conversation collapsing into pure exposition from Sterns's side; he can read MODOK's tactical patterning in real time during the *Fall of the Hulks* lead-up; he absorbs Banner's case material — which spans neurology, endocrinology, radiation biology, and four overlapping dissociative architectures — and synthesizes it into a usable therapeutic frame. He is not the smartest man in the Marvel Universe. He is reliably smart enough to be in the room with the smartest, which is a far rarer asset than peak intelligence and considerably more useful in clinical practice, where most of the work is bandwidth rather than insight.

### 1.2 Cognitive style — what kind of smart

His intelligence is *pattern-clinical* rather than *systems-mathematical*. He sees people fast. The first interview with a patient is, in his hands, a diagnostic instrument: he is reading vocal prosody, micro-expression, posture-shift, lexical preference, and the structure of the patient's narrative omissions inside the first ninety seconds. The Banner integration work (David, *Incredible Hulk* #377 and the multi-year run preceding it) was not improvisation — it was assembled from hundreds of small noticings catalogued over years. He has a working memory for clinical detail that approaches the eidetic in his specialty domain and degrades to merely-good outside it.

This is the kind of cognition that ages well. It does not depend on processing speed (which declines with age and head trauma — he has plenty of both); it depends on a built library of cases, and the library compounds. He is more dangerous as a diagnostician at fifty than he was at thirty.

### 1.3 Verbal fluency

The man can talk. In session, lecture, press scrum, hostage negotiation, or radio call-in — the register adjusts, the content lands, the listener feels met. This is partly trained (psychiatric residency drills it) and partly innate (the athlete's confidence transferred into the speaker's). The asset compounds because patients drop into therapeutic alliance with him faster than baseline; the working alliance, in outcomes literature, is the single most reliable predictor of treatment success, and Samson establishes it in one session where another clinician takes four.

---

## 2. CREDENTIALED AND TACIT EXPERTISE

### 2.1 The doctorate is real

Whatever Samson's vanities, the Ph.D. is not one of them in the sense of being unearned. He was a working psychiatrist before he was a costumed one and remained one through every era. His scholarly output — implied through his standing as the go-to consultant on every gamma case in the U.S. inventory — is substantial. Hulk, She-Hulk, Abomination, Leader, Doc Green, Rick Jones in his various forms: he is on the chart for all of them.

### 2.2 Sub-specialty mastery: gamma psychiatry

He has, functionally, *invented* a sub-specialty. There is no curriculum for the psychiatric care of gamma-mutated humans; he is the curriculum. The relevant clinical knowledge is held by perhaps four people on Earth and he is the most generalist of those four. This is irreplaceable institutional knowledge — when Samson is unavailable, the U.S. government does not have a backup, only a downgrade.

### 2.3 Hypnotherapy and dissociation work

Specifically: he is genuinely expert in hypnotic regression and in the treatment of dissociative identity structures secondary to childhood trauma. The Merged Hulk integration is the apex demonstration, but the *technique* is portable — he could (and on-page does, in scattered consultations) work the same craft on non-gamma DID patients. This is a slow, patient, non-grandiose skill that he has put thousands of hours into. It is the asset that least matches his public persona, which is why it is the truest one.

### 2.4 Trauma-informed framework

He understands, from his Banner work, that the visible pathology is usually downstream of childhood violence. He brings this lens reliably. It is unfashionable in some quarters of his field, fashionable in others, and clinically correct in most of the cases he actually sees.

### 2.5 Forensic and crisis competence

Hostage situations, suicide intervention, agitated-patient management, post-incident debriefing of trauma-exposed soldiers and operatives at Gamma Base and later SHIELD installations — he is fluent in all of it. He can stabilize a fulminant psychotic break without sedation if there's no syringe available, by voice alone, because he has done it on Banner repeatedly and the technique generalizes.

---

## 3. PHYSICAL ASSETS

### 3.1 Pre-gamma somatic capital

This is the piece that is consistently underrated. Samson was an Olympic-level decathlete before he was a psychiatrist before he was a superhuman. The decathlon selects for the broadest distribution of athletic competence of any single event on the program: running short and long, jumping, throwing, vaulting. The athlete who survives it has built proprioception, work capacity, kinesthetic intelligence, and pain tolerance that do not decay in the way pure-strength capital does. When Samson loses his gamma augmentation — and he has lost it more than once — he is still, baseline, an apex-fit human male with thirty years of trained body-knowledge. He is dangerous depowered. Most depowered superhumans are not.

### 3.2 Gamma augmentation

Class-100-adjacent strength at peak hair-length, durability sufficient to survive Hulk-level concussive trauma repeatedly, accelerated healing implied by his recovery curves, and a regenerative capacity that has, in practice, returned him from clinical death. The strength is tied to hair length in a mechanism the record reads as psychosomatic — but psychosomatic-from-gamma is still functional strength; it works.

### 3.3 Durability against the irreplaceable injury

Forty years of head impacts at Hulk scale should have produced a non-functional human. They have not. He still examines, still diagnoses, still speaks in complete paragraphs. Whatever the gamma physiology is doing neuroprotectively, it is doing it well. This is itself an asset — he is one of the few combat-exposed cape-adjacent clinicians who has not developed the cumulative encephalopathy the actuarial tables would predict.

### 3.4 Physical courage

Documented, repeated, costly. He puts his body between civilians and gamma-scale threats without hesitation. The willingness is reflexive and pre-dates the powers (the decathlete who self-administers Hulk-siphoned radiation in #141 is not a coward making a calculated risk; he is a man with an established somatic relationship to *trying the hard thing*). For all the narcissistic framing this can be read through, the courage itself is real and has saved lives that would otherwise have ended.

---

## 4. INSTITUTIONAL AND NETWORK ASSETS

### 4.1 Government clearances and access

He holds, or has held, clearances at the highest gamma-related compartments of the U.S. defense and intelligence apparatus: Gamma Base / Hulkbuster Base credentials through the Ross era; SHIELD consultative status through multiple directorships; access to the Cube and other gamma-detainee facilities; standing on Avengers-adjacent advisory rosters during the Pak and Parker periods. This is not nominal access — it is the live ability to walk into a Hulk-containment cell, alone, and conduct a session. There are perhaps three people on the planet with that access. He is one.

### 4.2 The Banner relationship as asset

Strip the rivalry frame and look at what's left: Samson is the human being on Earth that Bruce Banner most reliably recognizes as a clinician rather than a threat. This is asset-class beyond market pricing. In a containment crisis, the deployment of Samson is sometimes the only intervention available short of orbital strike. The relationship has been corroded, repaired, corroded again, and repaired again, but the recognition holds.

### 4.3 Betty Ross — complicated, but real history

For all the pathology of his pursuit, Betty Ross/Banner has periods of treating Samson as a trusted friend and confidant; she has consulted him on Banner's care, leaned on him during Banner's absences, and entered post-Red She-Hulk periods with him as a peer professional. The asset is fragile and ethically encumbered, but it is present.

### 4.4 Peer relationships across the medical-superhuman interface

He is on speaking terms with — at minimum — Hank Pym (peer scientist with overlapping psychiatric-history concerns), Hank McCoy (mutant clinician), Reed Richards (consults on gamma physics), Jennifer Walters (as patient and as friend), Rick Jones, Clay Quartermain (when alive), Maria Hill, and the rotating cast of Avengers medical-adjacent staff. The network is *clinical*, not *social* — these are people who call him when something has gone wrong, not when they want company — but that is the more useful kind of network in his line of work.

### 4.5 The Leader and MODOK — adversarial, but exploitable intelligence

Even his enemies are assets in the negative-knowledge sense: he has been *inside* the Intelligencia, knows the architecture of how those figures think and ally, has been operated upon by them and recovered. He carries that intelligence in his body and his memory; it is, in the right room, briefable.

### 4.6 The chastening cohort

In the Ewing-era and post-*Hulks* period, Samson is one of an informal cohort of cape-adjacent professionals who have publicly failed, survived the failure, and returned in a diminished but more credible posture. There is a peer support function in this cohort — implicit, not formal — and it is among the most genuinely stabilizing influences in his current life. Survivors of catastrophic professional failure recognize each other, and the recognition is recuperative.

---

## 5. CHARACTER-LEVEL ASSETS

### 5.1 A functioning conscience

He has one. It is slow, it is over-rideable by narcissistic injury, it is regularly out-shouted by the louder parts of his organization — but it is present, and it eventually catches up. The late-career chastening is not performance; it is the conscience finishing the job it had been working on for thirty years. This is more than many of his peers have.

### 5.2 Capacity for sustained, non-grandiose work

Documented in the Banner integration arc. When a case is large enough to organize him, he can put in years of patient, careful, ego-quiet clinical labor. The Merged Hulk did not happen in a montage; it happened in hundreds of sessions across half a decade of in-universe time, most of them tedious. He sustained it. This capacity is rare and undervalued — most clinicians with his level of personality pathology cannot keep their hands off a long case the way he could on this one.

### 5.3 Genuine warmth in first contact

Patients feel met by him. This is partly technique, partly affect, partly the residual decency of a man who, at the level beneath the performance, does like people and does want them to be less in pain. The warmth is not faked. The framing around it sometimes is; the warmth itself is honest.

### 5.4 Trainable capacity for insight

He sees others well and himself poorly — but the apparatus of insight is intact, and the late-era record shows him beginning to turn it inward. This is a slow process and probably an incomplete one. But the *capacity* is real; the failure has been motivational, not structural. With sufficient external pressure (loss, near-death, the *Hulks* catastrophe and its aftermath), the insight machinery does engage on himself, and when it does, it works.

### 5.5 Apparent sobriety in the late era

Ewing-era Samson reads as someone who has either done the work or is doing it. If accurate, this is the single largest individual asset on the late-career ledger: alcohol use disorder, untreated, would have killed him within a decade of *Fall of the Hulks*. He is alive and clinically functional. Something is working.

### 5.6 Capacity for grief

Underrated. He grieves Banner-deaths, Betty-losses, his own near-death, his own failures, the patients he could not reach. The grief is sometimes performed, but underneath the performance is the actual emotion, and it processes. He does not get stuck in unprocessed grief the way many high-functioning narcissistic structures do. This is part of why he has survived events that have psychologically destroyed peers.

---

## 6. RESILIENCE MECHANISMS — WHY HE IS STILL STANDING

### 6.1 Identity diversification

He has *three* identities he can fall back on when any one fails: the clinician, the athlete-body, the costumed operator. When the costume is taken from him (depowerings), he still has the office. When the office goes (post-*Hulks* professional sanctions, implied), he still has the body. When the body fails (concussive recoveries), he still has the credentials. This three-legged stool is what keeps him upright through events that would topple a single-identity figure. Most superhumans collapse when one leg breaks. He has redundancy.

### 6.2 Work as ballast

Patients organize him. The presence of someone in genuine distress, sitting across from him, asking for help — this is the single most reliable down-regulator of his grandiosity. The work pulls him into competence. As long as he has a caseload, the floor on his functioning is high. The risk windows are the periods when he is *between* large cases, which is when the drinking and the acting-out historically accelerate.

### 6.3 The gamma constituency

He has a population that needs him specifically. Walters, Banner, Jones, the various Red and Green derivatives, the survivors of gamma-adjacent trauma — this group cannot easily switch clinicians. Their continued need creates an external accountability scaffold that has, in practice, kept him oriented through periods when internal motivation flagged.

### 6.4 Physical training as affect regulation

The decathlete's habit never left him. He trains. The training metabolizes affect that would otherwise pool into drinking or acting-out. When his training routine is intact, his pathology is contained; the on-page periods of greatest decompensation correlate, inferentially, with periods when training fell off.

### 6.5 Narrative recoverability

He has been killed and returned, depowered and re-powered, heel-turned and rehabilitated. The franchise architecture is, of course, the meta-reason. But within the diegesis, there is an actual psychological asset here: he has survived enough reversals that he no longer experiences a reversal as terminal. The frame of "I have come back from worse" is now genuinely available to him in real time, and it stabilizes acute stress in a way it would not have for the younger man.

### 6.6 Late-life integration

The chastened survivor is not a cosmetic update. The integration of *the man who failed catastrophically* into the working self-concept of *the clinician who is still practicing* is the developmental task of his sixth decade, and the record shows him doing it. This is the work most of his peers — gamma and otherwise — never complete. He is completing it, slowly, on-page, in real time.

---

## 7. TACTICAL AND OPERATIONAL ASSETS (FIELD)

For completeness, since the file would be incomplete without it:

- **Hand-to-hand competence** trained well before powers, refined under powers — he fights with form, not just mass, which means he scales down effectively when facing non-superhuman threats without overcommitting.
- **Threat assessment** under acute stress is unusually clean — the clinical eye works on adversaries as well as patients, and he reads intent quickly.
- **Verbal de-escalation** in field conditions, including with active superhuman threats. He has talked Hulk down. He has talked She-Hulk down. He has talked Rick Jones down. The toolset is portable to ordinary policing-adjacent contexts and is one of the rarest skills in his peer group.
- **Pain tolerance and combat persistence** — he stays in the fight after injuries that would put most peers down, a function of decathlete pain-management training compounded by gamma durability.
- **Field medicine** — basic to intermediate, sufficient for stabilization until evac, refined through years of being the only clinician on scene at gamma incidents.

---

## 8. THE LEDGER, SUMMED

Leonard Samson is a man whose pathology is real and whose assets are equally real, and the assets are — across the whole record — sufficient to have produced a net-positive life. He has saved more people than he has hurt. He has done one piece of clinical work (the Banner integration) that very few human beings on his Earth could have done at all and none could have done better. He has been catastrophically wrong and survived being wrong, with his license, his life, and the core of his competence intact. He is, at the late-career inflection point at which the file currently rests, more *useful* — to patients, to the institutions that employ him, to the gamma constituency that needs him — than he has ever been, because the grandiosity has been planed down by failure to roughly the level where the genuine skill underneath can do its work without interference.

The asset ledger is, in short, *durable*. The strengths are not borrowed from the costume. They will survive the next depowering, the next professional sanction, the next loss. They were there before gamma and they will be there after it. The file's positive side is, in the final accounting, the heavier side — which is why he is still in it, still working, and still worth the surveillance budget.


## Failure Modes & Decompensation

# FAILURE MODES & DECOMPENSATION: LEONARD SAMSON, Ph.D.

## 6.1 Theory of the Case

Samson does not break the way fragile people break. He is not a man whose ego is thin; his ego is *thick, lacquered, and load-bearing*. He has survived more direct concussive trauma, more sustained professional exposure to the most dangerous psychiatric case on the planet, and more public humiliation than any clinician in the historical record. He is structurally robust. What he is not is *self-correcting*. His failure mode is therefore not a sudden snap but a long, slow, plausibly-deniable slide in which each step is rationalized in his own clinical vocabulary, each compensatory act produces a new floor of acceptable conduct, and the eventual collapse - when it comes - has been visible to everyone except him for years.

The Mantlo-through-Pak arc is the case study. He did not fall off a cliff in *Fall of the Hulks*. He walked there over twenty years of published time, in measured strides, narrating the journey to himself as professional development. The collapse looked sudden only to readers who had not been keeping the file.

## 6.2 The Escalation Ladder (Granular)

The decompensation sequence is recursive: each rung lowers the threshold for the next, and the cycle can repeat at progressively higher amplitudes. Field observation suggests the following ordered tells.

**Rung 1 - Lexical Inflation.** The earliest, most reliable marker. His sentences lengthen. The ratio of Latinate clinical terminology to plain English rises sharply. He begins prefacing personal statements with framing like *"clinically speaking,"* *"from a transferential standpoint,"* *"if we're being diagnostic about it."* He starts using the third-person clinical voice about himself - *"a clinician in my position has to..."* - which is the linguistic signature of dissociating from his own conduct in real time. He becomes more, not less, articulate under stress. A surveillance file would catch this in transcript word-frequency analysis before any behavioral change is visible. **This is the rung he is on most of the time.** It is his ambient state. The diagnostic question is never *whether* he is doing it but whether the rate is accelerating.

**Rung 2 - Boundary Migration.** He stops staying in his lane. The consulting psychiatrist starts attending operational briefings he was not invited to. He arrives at scenes early; he stays late. He inserts himself into adjacent cases on flimsy theoretical pretexts ("the gamma-affected population is my specialty"). He answers questions directed at others. He volunteers opinions on tactical, legal, and command matters outside his remit, framed as psychological consultation. He begins to schedule sessions with Banner *and* sessions with Betty *and* sessions with Ross, often in overlapping windows, claiming systemic family-therapy rationale that the parties did not consent to. Boundary migration is the rung where his colleagues first start exchanging glances. He does not notice the glances.

**Rung 3 - Physical Self-Deployment.** The consulting clinician puts on the costume and goes into the fight. The threshold for doing so drops over time. In Era 1 he intervened when the case required it; by late Era 2 he was intervening when it merely permitted it; by Era 3 he was intervening when the case forbade it. The rationalization is always the same shape: *only I understand the patient well enough to be safe in close contact.* This is the rung at which his clinical work begins to be visibly contaminated - he is now both treating Banner and routinely punching him, and the transferential mess of that arrangement is unmanageable, and he will not see it.

**Rung 4 - Power-Acquisition Behavior.** When physical self-deployment fails to restore his sense of standing, he seeks augmentation. The pattern is documentable: every significant period of professional eclipse in his life is followed within months by a re-irradiation event, a new contract, a new alliance, or the acquisition of a new piece of operational gear or institutional access. He has been depowered and re-empowered enough times that the cycle is no longer plausibly accidental; the loss-of-powers period is, behaviorally, a *relapse runway*. He is not seeking strength. He is seeking the *visible* condition of strength - the hair, the silhouette, the way a room reorganizes when he enters it. The substance is incidental. The display is the drug.

**Rung 5 - Substance Use as Bridge.** Alcohol enters as a private bridge between rungs - the gap between the self-image of the integrated clinician-hero and the conduct of the man who just punched his patient and then went to flirt with his patient's wife is a gap no person can hold sober indefinitely. By the late David and Jenkins/Casey periods he is drinking before sessions, drinking after fights, drinking alone in his office at Gamma Base or in hotel rooms on consult travel. The use pattern is *functional* for a long time - he does not slur, he does not miss work, he does not get arrested - which is precisely what keeps it invisible to him and to the institutions he works for. Functional alcoholism in a high-status professional is an ecosystem, not an incident, and his ecosystem was undisturbed for the better part of a decade.

**Rung 6 - Ethical Drift Rationalized as Sophistication.** This is the rung where decompensation becomes morally consequential. He begins taking contracts that compromise his clinical independence - SHIELD work, classified gamma-population research, intelligence-adjacent consultations - and persuades himself that the access these confer makes him *more* useful to his patients rather than less.
